ہے، ان کی دلیل حضور سالی یا ستم کا یہ ارشاد ہے لاغزون قریشا میں قریش سے ضرور لڑونگا پھر ایک سال کے بعد آپ سال کیا کہ تم نے ان شاء اللہ کہا، یہ دلیل ہے کہ مفصولاً بھی درست ہے۔ نے جمہور کی دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں آپ سال سی ایم نے فرمایا ” جو شخص کسی چیز کی قسم کھائے پھر اس کے علاوہ کو بہتر سمجھے تو کفارہ دے دے اور وہ بہتر کام کرے، آپ سال یا اسلام نے قسم سے نکلنے کے لئے کفارہ متعین کیا ، ورنہ آپ یوں کہتے کہ ان شاء اللہ کہ دے، معلوم ہوا کہ مفصولا درست نہیں ہے۔ نیز اگر مفصولاً صحیح قرار دیں گے تو بہت سارے معاملات باطل ہو جائیں گے، آدمی ان شاء اللہ جب چاہے کہہ دے گا تو عقد ہی باطل ہو جائے گا۔ واختلف في خصوص العموم: مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ جس عام میں پہلی بار تخصیص ہورہی ہو تو اس میں اختلاف ہے، ہمارے نزدیک یہ تخصیص موصولاً درست ہے مفصولاً درست نہیں ہے، اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک مفصولاً بھی صحیح ہے۔ یہ اختلاف در حقیقت ایک دوسرے اختلافی مسئلہ پر مبنی ہے کہ عام تخصیص سے پہلے قطعی ہوتا ہے یا ظنی؟ تو ہمارے نزدیک عام تخصیص سے پہلے بالکل اسی طرح قطعی رہتا ہے جس طرح خاص قطعی ہوتا ہے، اور تخصیص کے بعد عام ظنی ہو جاتا ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک عام تخصیص سے پہلے بھی ظنی ہوتا ہے جیسے تخصیص کے بعد ظنی ہوتا ہے، تو ہمارے نزدیک تخصیص بیان تغییر ہوگی، کیونکہ تخصیص سے عام قطعیت سے ظنیت کی طرف بدل جائے گا، اور بیانِ تغییر میں وصل ضروری ہے، اس لئے ہم نے کہا موصولاً ہونا ضروری ہے، اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک تخصیص بیان تغییر : ہوگی بلکہ بیان تقریر ہوگی ، کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک عام تخصیص سے پہلے بھی ظنی ہوتا ہے اور تخصیص کے بعد بھی تو تخصیص سے کلام میں تبدیلی نہیں ہوئی ، لہذا تخصیص بیان تغییر نہ ہوگی بلکہ بیانِ تقریر ہوگی، اور بیان تقریر میں موصولاً اور مفصولاً دونوں طرح درست ہے۔ تنبيه : یہ بات ذہن میں رہے کہ مذکورہ اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے کہ جب عام میں تخصیص ابتداء ہو، ور نہ عام میں کسی متخصص کے ذریعہ تخصیص ہو چکی ہو تو اس عام مخصوص منہ البعض میں تخصیص مفصولاً ہمارے نزدیک بھی جائز ہوگی ، کیوں عام ایک مرتبہ تخصیص سے ظنی ہو گیا تو ثانیاً جو تخصیص ہوگی وہ ظنی میں ہوگی ، تو یہ تخصیص بیان تغیر نہ ہوگی بلکہ بیان تقریر ہوگی ۔ وعلى هذا قال علماء نا: - ہمارے نزدیک چونکہ تخصیص میں وصل ضروری ہے، اس پر یہ مسئلہ متفرع ہے، انگوٹھی عام کے درجہ میں ہے جو حلقہ اور نگینہ دونوں کو شامل ہے، لہذا اگر کسی نے ایک آدمی کے لئے انگوٹھی کی وصیت کی اور متصلا نگینہ کی وصیت دوسرے کے لئے کر دی تو دوسری وصیت یعنی نگینہ کی وصیت پہلی وصیت یعنی انگوٹھی کی وصیت کے لئے تخصیص ہوگی ، لہذا پہلے شخص کے لئے حلقہ ہوگا اور دوسرے کے لئے نگینہ ہوگا، لیکن اگر دوسری وصیت پہلی وصیت کے ساتھ موصول نہیں کی بلکہ مفصولاً کی تو دوسری وصیت پہلی وصیت کے لئے تخصیص نہ ہوگی بلکہ پہلی وصیت کی وجہ سے حلقہ اور نگینہ دونوں پہلے شخص کے لئے ہو گئے پھر دوسری وصیت کی وجہ سے نگینہ دوسرے آدمی کے لئے بھی ہوا تو دوسری وصیت نگینہ کے بارے میں پہلی وصیت کے معارض ہو گئی ، اس تعارض کی وجہ سے نگینہ دونوں آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہوگا۔
It changed the previous statement, because if there was no suspension, divorce would occur immediately, but with suspension, divorce is delayed until entry of the house. Example of exception: as in 'For Zaid upon me one thousand dirhams except one hundred.' In the beginning of the statement, acknowledgment of one thousand is present, but with 'except one hundred', acknowledgment of nine hundred remains. So 'except one hundred' changed the beginning of the statement. Thus suspension and exception are both bayan taghyir (explanatory change), and bayan taghyir is valid with the condition of connectivity, because condition and exception are not independent speech; without being connected to what precedes, they do not convey meaning. Therefore they must be connected. This is the madhhab of the majority (Jumhur). According to Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him), connectivity is not a condition in suspension and exception; it is valid without connectivity. Their evidence is the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'I will certainly fight the Quraysh,' then after a year he said: 'You said: If Allah wills.' This is evidence that it is valid disconnectedly. The evidence of the Jumhur is the hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever swears an oath to do something and then sees something better, let him expiate and do the better thing.' The Prophet (peace be upon him) prescribed expiation to exit the oath; otherwise he would have said 'If Allah wills.' So it became clear that disconnection is not valid. Also, if disconnection were valid, many transactions would become invalid; a person could say 'If Allah wills' whenever he wants, and the contract would become void. And they differed concerning specification of the general: The author says that when a general term is specified for the first time, there is a difference of opinion. According to us, such specification is valid only if connected, not if disconnected. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, it is valid even disconnected. This difference is actually based on another disputed issue: whether a general term before specification is qat'i (definitive) or zanni (probable). According to us, the general before specification remains qat'i just as the specific is qat'i, and after specification it becomes zanni. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the general is zanni both before and after specification. So according to us, specification is bayan taghyir, because specification changes the general from qat'i to zanni, and connectivity is necessary in bayan taghyir. Therefore we say it must be connected. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, specification is not bayan taghyir but rather bayan taqrir (confirmatory explanation), because according to him the general is zanni both before and after specification, so specification does not change the statement. Therefore specification is bayan taqrir, and in bayan taqrir both connected and disconnected are valid. Note: It should be kept in mind that the aforementioned difference is when specification occurs for the first time in a general term. But if the general has already been specified by a specifier, then in that partially specified general (al-'amm al-makhsus min al-ba'd), disconnection is also permissible according to us, because the general became zanni after the first specification, so the second specification occurs in a zanni context; thus it is not bayan taghyir but bayan taqrir. And upon this our scholars said: According to us, since connectivity is necessary in specification, this issue branches from it: A ring is at the level of general, which includes both the band and the gem. So if someone makes a will of a ring for one person and immediately makes a will of the gem for another, then the second will (of the gem) is a specification for the first will (of the ring). Therefore the first person gets the band and the second gets the gem. But if the second will is not connected to the first will but is made disconnectedly, then the second will is not a specification for the first; rather, due to the first will, both the band and the gem belong to the first person. Then due to the second will, the gem also goes to the second person, so the second will conflicts with the first will regarding the gem, and due to this conflict, the gem will be shared between the two persons.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the requirement of connectivity (ittisal) in two types of explanatory change (bayan taghyir): ta'liq (suspension) and istithna (exception). The author begins by stating that both ta'liq and istithna change the meaning of the prior statement; for example, in ta'liq, saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced' changes the immediate effect of divorce, and in istithna, saying 'except one hundred' reduces the acknowledged amount. Therefore, these are bayan taghyir. For such explanatory change to be valid, the condition or exception must be connected (mawsulan) to the main statement. The reason is that these clauses are not independent; they only make sense when attached to what precedes. This is the position of the majority (Jumhur). The author then mentions the dissenting opinion of Ibn Abbas, who allowed disconnection (mafsulan), citing the incident where the Prophet said 'I will certainly fight the Quraysh' but later added 'if Allah wills' after a year. The Jumhur counter with a hadith where the Prophet prescribed expiation for breaking an oath rather than using 'if Allah wills' retroactively, indicating that disconnection is not permissible. They also point out that allowing disconnection would lead to contractual chaos. Next, the author turns to the specification of a general term (takhsis al-'amm). The Hanafi position is that when a general term is first specified, the specification must be connected. This is because, according to Hanafis, a general term before specification is definitive (qat'i) like a specific term, and specification changes it to probable (zanni). Hence it is bayan taghyir requiring connectivity. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, holds that the general is probable both before and after specification, so specification does not change the level of certainty; it is merely bayan taqrir (confirmatory explanation), which can be disconnected. The author then adds a note (tanbih) clarifying that if the general has already been specified once, subsequent specifications are dealing with a probable term, so they become bayan taqrir, which allows disconnection even for Hanafis. Finally, the author provides a practical branch (furu') from Hanafi scholars: in the case of a will for a ring (which includes both band and gem), if the testator immediately specifies the gem for another person, the second will is a connected specification, so the first gets the band and the second the gem. But if the second will is disconnected, then both parts go to the first, and the second will creates a conflict, resulting in sharing the gem.

Key Terms
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspending a legal effect (like divorce) on the occurrence of a condition.
استثناء (istithna): Exception, excluding part of a statement from the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Jumhur (majority), what is required for suspension (ta'liq) and exception (istithna) to be valid?
A) They must be connected to the main statement.
B) They can be disconnected as long as the intention is clear.
C) They must be separated by a pause.
D) They are valid only if written down.

Key Takeaway
For ta'liq and istithna to change a prior statement, they must be connected immediately; otherwise they are invalid.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Connectivity in Takhsis al-'Amm: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Analyses the dispute over connectivity in the first specification of a general term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis require connectivity for the first specification of a general term and contrast this with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
First specification changes the general from qat'i to zanni, making it bayan taghyir requiring connectivity.

When a general term ('amm) is specified for the first time, a debate arises: must the specifier be connected? The Hanafi school answers affirmatively, based on the nature of the general term before specification. This lesson unpacks the underlying dispute about the epistemic status of 'amm and its impact on the rule of connectivity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on first takhsis
Hanafis hold that when a general term is specified for the first time, the specification must be connected (mawsulan) to the general statement. Disconnection (mafsulan) is invalid.
This applies only to the first specification; subsequent specifications can be disconnected.
2
Identify the underlying dispute: qat'i vs zanni
The difference stems from whether the general term before specification is definitive (qat'i) or probable (zanni). Hanafis say it is qat'i like a specific term; Shafi'is say it is always zanni.
This is a fundamental usul difference between the Hanafi and Mutakallim schools.
3
Analyze how the status affects classification
If the general is qat'i, specification changes it to zanni—a change in certainty. This makes takhsis a bayan taghyir (change), which requires connectivity. If it is already zanni, specification does not change the certainty level, making it bayan taqrir (confirmation), which can be disconnected.
Thus the requirement of connectivity hinges on whether takhsis is taghyir or taqrir.
4
Apply the rule to the ring will example
A ring is a general term covering both band and gem. If a testator wills a ring to one person and immediately specifies the gem for another, that specification is connected and valid: first gets band, second gets gem. If the specification is disconnected, both initially go to the first, and the gem is shared due to conflict.
This illustrates the practical consequence (thamarah) of the rule.
5
Distinguish first specification from subsequent
Once a general term has been specified once, it becomes zanni. Any further specification is then bayan taqrir, so disconnection is allowed even for Hanafis.
This nuance prevents the rule from being applied rigidly.

معارض ہو گئی ، اس تعارض کی وجہ سے نگینہ دونوں آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہوگا۔
It changed the previous statement, because if there was no suspension, divorce would occur immediately, but with suspension, divorce is delayed until entry of the house. Example of exception: as in 'For Zaid upon me one thousand dirhams except one hundred.' In the beginning of the statement, acknowledgment of one thousand is present, but with 'except one hundred', acknowledgment of nine hundred remains. So 'except one hundred' changed the beginning of the statement. Thus suspension and exception are both bayan taghyir (explanatory change), and bayan taghyir is valid with the condition of connectivity, because condition and exception are not independent speech; without being connected to what precedes, they do not convey meaning. Therefore they must be connected. This is the madhhab of the majority (Jumhur). According to Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him), connectivity is not a condition in suspension and exception; it is valid without connectivity. Their evidence is the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'I will certainly fight the Quraysh,' then after a year he said: 'You said: If Allah wills.' This is evidence that it is valid disconnectedly. The evidence of the Jumhur is the hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever swears an oath to do something and then sees something better, let him expiate and do the better thing.' The Prophet (peace be upon him) prescribed expiation to exit the oath; otherwise he would have said 'If Allah wills.' So it became clear that disconnection is not valid. Also, if disconnection were valid, many transactions would become invalid; a person could say 'If Allah wills' whenever he wants, and the contract would become void. And they differed concerning specification of the general: The author says that when a general term is specified for the first time, there is a difference of opinion. According to us, such specification is valid only if connected, not if disconnected. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, it is valid even disconnected. This difference is actually based on another disputed issue: whether a general term before specification is qat'i (definitive) or zanni (probable). According to us, the general before specification remains qat'i just as the specific is qat'i, and after specification it becomes zanni. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the general is zanni both before and after specification. So according to us, specification is bayan taghyir, because specification changes the general from qat'i to zanni, and connectivity is necessary in bayan taghyir. Therefore we say it must be connected. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, specification is not bayan taghyir but rather bayan taqrir (confirmatory explanation), because according to him the general is zanni both before and after specification, so specification does not change the statement. Therefore specification is bayan taqrir, and in bayan taqrir both connected and disconnected are valid. Note: It should be kept in mind that the aforementioned difference is when specification occurs for the first time in a general term. But if the general has already been specified by a specifier, then in that partially specified general (al-'amm al-makhsus min al-ba'd), disconnection is also permissible according to us, because the general became zanni after the first specification, so the second specification occurs in a zanni context; thus it is not bayan taghyir but bayan taqrir. And upon this our scholars said: According to us, since connectivity is necessary in specification, this issue branches from it: A ring is at the level of general, which includes both the band and the gem. So if someone makes a will of a ring for one person and immediately makes a will of the gem for another, then the second will (of the gem) is a specification for the first will (of the ring). Therefore the first person gets the band and the second gets the gem. But if the second will is not connected to the first will but is made disconnectedly, then the second will is not a specification for the first; rather, due to the first will, both the band and the gem belong to the first person. Then due to the second will, the gem also goes to the second person, so the second will conflicts with the first will regarding the gem, and due to this conflict, the gem will be shared between the two persons.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the requirement of connectivity (ittisal) in two types of explanatory change (bayan taghyir): ta'liq (suspension) and istithna (exception). The author begins by stating that both ta'liq and istithna change the meaning of the prior statement; for example, in ta'liq, saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced' changes the immediate effect of divorce, and in istithna, saying 'except one hundred' reduces the acknowledged amount. Therefore, these are bayan taghyir. For such explanatory change to be valid, the condition or exception must be connected (mawsulan) to the main statement. The reason is that these clauses are not independent; they only make sense when attached to what precedes. This is the position of the majority (Jumhur). The author then mentions the dissenting opinion of Ibn Abbas, who allowed disconnection (mafsulan), citing the incident where the Prophet said 'I will certainly fight the Quraysh' but later added 'if Allah wills' after a year. The Jumhur counter with a hadith where the Prophet prescribed expiation for breaking an oath rather than using 'if Allah wills' retroactively, indicating that disconnection is not permissible. They also point out that allowing disconnection would lead to contractual chaos. Next, the author turns to the specification of a general term (takhsis al-'amm). The Hanafi position is that when a general term is first specified, the specification must be connected. This is because, according to Hanafis, a general term before specification is definitive (qat'i) like a specific term, and specification changes it to probable (zanni). Hence it is bayan taghyir requiring connectivity. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, holds that the general is probable both before and after specification, so specification does not change the level of certainty; it is merely bayan taqrir (confirmatory explanation), which can be disconnected. The author then adds a note (tanbih) clarifying that if the general has already been specified once, subsequent specifications are dealing with a probable term, so they become bayan taqrir, which allows disconnection even for Hanafis. Finally, the author provides a practical branch (furu') from Hanafi scholars: in the case of a will for a ring (which includes both band and gem), if the testator immediately specifies the gem for another person, the second will is a connected specification, so the first gets the band and the second the gem. But if the second will is disconnected, then both parts go to the first, and the second will creates a conflict, resulting in sharing the gem.

Key Terms
تخصیص (takhsis): Specification, limiting a general term to some of its individuals.
عام ('amm): A general term that encompasses all its individuals.
قطعی (qat'i): Definitive, certain in meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when must the specification of a general term be connected?
A) Always, regardless of context.
B) Only for the first specification.
C) Only for specifications that are in the form of a condition.
D) Only when the specification is by a Quranic verse.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the first specification of a general term must be connected because it changes the general from qat'i to zanni, making it a bayan taghyir.

The Hanafi and Shafi'i Theories on How Exception Operates
Dispute on the mechanism of exception in usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi and Shafi'i theories of istithna (exception) to interpret statements containing an exception and identify the practical difference in resulting rulings.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, an exception prevents the speaker from speaking about the excepted part; for Shafi'is, it opposes the ruling like a specific proof.

This passage delves into the fundamental disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the very nature of how an exceptional clause (istithna) functions within a statement. Understanding this difference is crucial because it affects the legal interpretation of acknowledgments, contracts, and other speech acts. The practical consequence is dramatically shown in the classic example of a debt acknowledgment with an exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing theories
The text begins by presenting the Hanafi view: istithna prevents speech (takallum) from including the excepted part. Then the Shafi'i view: it prevents the ruling (hukm) by way of opposition.
Both agree that exception modifies the original statement, but the mechanism differs.
2
Analyze the Hanafi mechanism
For Hanafis, the speaker's utterance is considered to apply only to the remaining part after the exception. The exception does not create a contradiction; it modifies the scope of the original statement. In the example, saying 'I owe one thousand except one hundred' means the speaker effectively acknowledges nine hundred.
This is consistent with the earlier discussion of istithna as bayan taghyir.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i mechanism
For Shafi'is, the exception functions like a specific proof (dalil al-khusus) that opposes the general ruling. It is not a mere limitation but an active contradiction. In the same example, the one hundred is not owed at all; it is as if the speaker denied that hundred from the outset.
This view treats the exception as an independent counter-proof.
4
Trace the practical consequence (thamarah)
The Hanafi interpretation results in a binding acknowledgment of nine hundred, while the Shafi'i interpretation leaves the excepted amount unacknowledged. This directly affects the burden of proof in court.
If the creditor claims the one hundred, he must prove it under the Shafi'i view, but under the Hanafi view the debtor has already acknowledged nine hundred.
5
Connect to the broader usul framework
This dispute mirrors the earlier disagreement on ta'liq bi al-shart (suspension by condition), showing consistency in each school's approach to how modifications interact with original statements.
Both examples illustrate how the Hanafi school tends to view modifying clauses as limiting the original speech, while the Shafi'i school sees them as contradictory evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاخْتَلَفُوْا فِيْ كَيْفِيَّةِ عَمَلِ الْإِسْتِثْنَاءِ أَيْضًا قَالَ أَصْحَابُنَا الْإِسْتِثْنَاء يَمْنَعُ التَّكَلُّ بِحُكْمِهِ بِقَدْرِ الْمُسْتَثْنى فَيَكُونُ تَكَلُّمًا بِالْبَاقِي بَعْدَهُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ الله الْاِسْتِثْنَاءُ يَمْنَعْ الْحُكْمَ بِطَرِيْقِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ دَلِيْلِ الْخُصُوصِ كَمَا اِخْتَلَفُوا فِي التَّعْلِيْقِ بِالشَّرْطِ عَلَى مَا سَبَقَ فَصَارَ عِنْدَنَا تَقْرِيرُ قَوْلِهِ لِفُلَانٍ عَلَىَ أَلْفُ دِرْهَمِ إِلَّا مِائَةٌ لَهُ عَلَى تِسْعُمِائَةٍ وَعِنْدَهُ إِلَّا مِائَةٌ فَإِنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ عَلَى ترجمہ : ۔ اور اختلاف کیا ہے (احناف و شوافع نے ) استثناء کے عمل کی کیفیت کے بارے میں ، پس ہمارے اصحاب نے کہا کہ استثناء مستثنی کی مقدار میں اس کے حکم کے ساتھ تکلم کو روکتا ہے، تو ہوگا تکلم اس مقدار کا جو باقی ہے، اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ استثنا روکتا ہے حکم کو معارضہ کے طریقہ پر بمنزل دلیل خصوص کے، جیسا کہ اختلاف کیا ہے (احناف و شوافع نے ) تعلیق بالشرط میں اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو گذر چکی، تو ہمارے نزدیک قائل کے قول لفلان على الف درهم الامائة کی تقریر ہوگی له على تسعمائة ، اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک الامائة فانها ليست علی ہوگی۔
And they differed concerning the modality of the operation of exception as well. Our companions said: Exception prevents speaking with its ruling to the extent of the excepted part, so it constitutes speaking about the remaining part after it. And al-Shafi'i said: Exception prevents the ruling by way of opposition, like a specific proof. Just as they differed concerning suspension by condition as already detailed. So according to us, the interpretation of the statement 'For Zaid upon me one thousand dirhams except one hundred' is: 'He has upon him nine hundred.' And according to him: 'Except one hundred: it is not upon him.' [Urdu translation follows]
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on how exception (istithna) functions in speech. The Hanafi position, as stated by our scholars, is that exception prevents the speaker from including the excepted part under the original ruling. In other words, when a person says 'I owe Zaid one thousand dirhams except one hundred,' the exception (istithna) does not contradict the original statement; rather, it limits the scope of the acknowledgment. The act of speaking (takallum) is considered to apply only to the remaining amount (nine hundred). Therefore, the effect of the exception is that the excepted part is simply not included in the speech. This is in line with the earlier discussion where istithna is considered bayan taghyir (explanatory change). In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that exception works by way of opposition (mu'arada) to the original ruling, similar to a specific proof (dalil al-khusus) that contradicts the general. Under this view, the excepted part is not merely excluded; it actively opposes the claim, so in the example, the excepted one hundred is 'not upon him' in the sense that it is denied from the outset. The practical difference is in the legal construction: for Hanafis, the speaker has effectively acknowledged nine hundred dirhams, while for Shafi'is, the one hundred is not acknowledged at all. The text notes that this dispute parallels the earlier one regarding suspension by condition (ta'liq bi al-shart).

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna): Exception; a clause excluding part of a statement from its ruling.
تکلم (takallum): The act of speaking or uttering a statement.
معارضہ (mu'arada): Opposition or contradiction between two pieces of evidence.
دلیل خصوص (dalil al-khusus): A specific proof that restricts a general ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, what is the effect of saying 'I owe Zaid one thousand dirhams except one hundred'?
A) The speaker acknowledges nine hundred dirhams.
B) The speaker acknowledges nothing because the exception contradicts the statement.
C) The speaker acknowledges one thousand dirhams and the one hundred is an additional debt.
D) The speaker must choose between the two amounts.

Key Takeaway
The difference in how exception operates leads to a concrete difference: Hanafis treat the excepted part as not spoken of, while Shafi'is treat it as contradicted, affecting legal acknowledgment.

How Does Istithna' Work? Hanafi vs Shafi'i Views
Comparing Hanafi and Shafi'i views on how istithna' excludes part of the statement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i views on the operation of istithna' and explain the practical consequence of their theoretical difference in a debt acknowledgment.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, istithna' prevents speaking of the excepted part; for Shafi'is, it creates a conflict that removes it.

This passage presents a foundational usul dispute about how linguistic exception (istithna') operates. Both schools agree on the practical result in the standard example, but their theoretical difference affects how other statements are interpreted. Understanding this distinction sharpens your ability to analyze textual evidence and see how different usul principles lead to the same ruling but through different mechanisms.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed issue
Identify the question: How does istithna' remove the excepted item from the general statement? Does it prevent the speaker from having spoken about that item, or does it create a conflict that cancels the ruling on that item?
2
Identify the Hanafi position
According to the Hanafis (ashabuna), istithna' prevents the speaking of the ruling of the excepted part. The speaker is considered to have only spoken about the remainder. Example: 'I owe 1000 except 100' means he only spoke about 900.
This is based on the linguistic principle that exception is a tool of exclusion from the outset.
3
Identify the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that istithna' prevents the ruling by way of mu'arada (conflict). The general statement includes the excepted item, but the exception conflicts with it, like a specific evidence (dalil al-khusus) overriding a general one.
Under this view, the speaker initially acknowledged 1000, but then the exception removes 100 by conflict.
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In the debt acknowledgment example, both schools reach the same result (900 dirhams owed), but the nature of the acknowledgment differs. For Hanafis, it is a direct acknowledgment of 900; for Shafi'is, it is an acknowledgment of 1000 with a subtraction.
This difference may affect other scenarios, e.g., multiple exceptions or oaths involving the same sum.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The text presents the Hanafi view as the relied-upon position of the school. In Hanafi usul, the immediate exclusion view is considered more consistent with the linguistic custom of Arabs.
Understanding this tarjih helps you see why the Hanafi school adopts certain interpretive principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاخْتَلَفُوْا فِيْ كَيْفِيَّةِ عَمَلِ الْإِسْتِثْنَاءِ أَيْضًا قَالَ أَصْحَابُنَا الْإِسْتِثْنَاء يَمْنَعُ التَكَلُّمَ بِحُكْمِهِ بِقَدْرِ الْمُسْتَثْنى فَيَكُونُ تَكَلُّمًا بِالْبَاقِي بَعْدَهُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ الْإِسْتِثْنَاءُ يَمْنَعُ الْحُكْمَ بِطَرِيْقِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ دَلِيْلِ الْخُصُوصِ كَمَا اِخْتَلَفُوا فِي التَّعْلِيْقِ بِالشَّرْطِ عَلَى مَا سَبَقَ فَصَارَ عِنْدَنَا تَقْرِيرُ قَوْلِهِ لِفُلَانٍ عَلَى أَلْفُ دِرْهَمِ إِلَّا مِائَةٌ لَهُ عَلَى تِسْعُمِائَةٍ وَعِنْدَهُ إِلَّا مِائَةٌ فَإِنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ عَلَى
And they differed also about the modality of the operation of exception (istithna'). Our Companions said: Exception prevents speaking of its ruling to the extent of the excepted part, so one is speaking of the remainder after it. And al-Shafi'i said: Exception prevents the ruling by way of conflict, like a specific evidence. Just as they differed regarding conditional suspension according to what preceded. So according to us, the interpretation of his saying 'To Zayd upon me one thousand dirhams except one hundred' is 'upon me nine hundred,' and according to him, 'except one hundred' means it is not upon him.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
The passage is a usul dispute (ikhtilaf) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the nature of istithna' (exception) in speech. The Hanafi position (qala ashabuna) is that istithna' prevents the speaker from having spoken about the excepted part at all. Thus, when one says 'I owe one thousand dirhams except one hundred,' according to Hanafis he has only spoken about nine hundred; the hundred was never part of his utterance. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the speaker did mention both the general and the exception, but the exception creates a conflict (mu'arada) with the general statement, similar to how a specific evidence (dalil al-khusus) overrides a general one. The exception therefore prevents the ruling on the excepted part by way of conflict, not by preventing the utterance. The author connects this to the earlier dispute on ta'liq bi al-shart (conditional suspension) and takhsis al-amm (specification of general). The practical effect: for the Hanafis, the reduced amount is directly established (the debt is nine hundred), while for the Shafi'is, the one thousand is acknowledged but then the hundred is subtracted due to conflict. The passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of al-Husami, explaining the foundational difference.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithna'): The linguistic operation of excluding something from a general statement using 'except' (illa).
المستثنى (al-mustathna): The excepted item (e.g., one hundred dirhams in the example).
المستثنى منه (al-mustathna minhu): The general amount from which the exception is made (e.g., one thousand dirhams).
المعارضة (al-mu'arada): Conflict between two pieces of evidence; in this context, the exception conflicts with the general statement.
التعليق بالشرط (al-ta'liq bi al-shart): Suspending a ruling on a condition (e.g., 'You are divorced if you enter the house').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, when someone says 'I owe one thousand dirhams except one hundred,' what has he actually acknowledged?
A) One thousand dirhams, but the hundred is removed by conflict.
B) Nine hundred dirhams; the hundred was never part of his speech.
C) One thousand dirhams and the exception is invalid.
D) Nothing until a judge decides.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on whether istithna' prevents speech about the excepted part or creates a conflict, but both reach the same practical result in the standard debt example.

The Effect of Istithna on General Rulings: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute over whether istithna of a condition limits the general ruling to measurable quantities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the effect of an exception (istithna) on a general statement, contrast it with the Shafi'i position, and derive the practical legal consequence using the hadith of selling food.

Core Idea
An exception of a condition does not restrict the general ruling; it only allows one condition.

This passage presents a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over how to interpret an exception in a general command. The hadith 'Do not sell food for food except like for like' is examined: does the exception limit the prohibition to measured quantities only? Understanding this disagreement reveals fundamental differences in how each school handles the relationship between general texts and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Statement and Exception
Locate the general prohibition ('la tabi'u al-ta'am bi al-ta'am') and the exception ('illa sawaan bi sawaan'). Note that both schools agree the statement is general in little and much.
The general phrase covers all quantities of food.
2
State the Opposing Interpretations
Shafi'i holds that the exception acts as a mu'arid (opposing proof) restricting the general to measured items only. Hanafis argue the exception is of a condition (hal), not a quantity, so the general remains for all conditions but only applies to measurable items.
The core disagreement is about the nature of the exception.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Proof
Examine the Quranic verse 'So he stayed among them a thousand years except fifty years.' The exception applies to the number itself, not to the general ruling. Hanafis analogize this: the exception in the hadith applies to the condition, not the general scope.
This shows that exception can target a specific element without restricting the general category.
4
Distinguish Between Types of Istithna
Understand the two types: istithna muttasil (connected) where the excepted item is part of the general, and istithna munfasil (disconnected) where it is not. The Hanafis argue the exception here is muttasil relating to the condition.
The Shafi'i view treats it as a mu'arid that restricts the general, which Hanafis reject.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Work out the practical difference: Hanafi permits selling a handful for two handfuls if the food is not measured (since not subject to the general), while Shafi'i prohibits it because the exception does not exempt small quantities.
This real-world consequence shows the importance of the usul principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَلَى هَذَا اعْتَبَرَ صَدْرَ الْكَلَامِ فِي قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا تَبِيْعُوا الطَّعَامَ بِالطَّعَام إِلَّا سَوَاءً بِسَوَاءٍ عَامًا فِى الْقَلِيْلِ وَالْكَثِيرِ إِلَّا أَنَّ الْإِسْتِثْنَاءَ عَارَضَهُ فِي الْمَكِيْل خَاصَةً فَبَقِيَ عَامًا فِيْمَا وَرَاءَهُ وَقُلْنَا هَذَا اسْتِثْنَاء حَالٍ فَيَكُونَ الصَّدْرُ عَامَّا فِي الْأَحْوَالِ وَذَلِكَ لَا يَصْلَحُ إِلَّا فِى الْمِقْدَارِ وَاحْتَجَ أَصْحَابُنَا رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمْ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَلَبِثَ فِيهِمْ اَلْفَ سَنَةٍ إِلَّا خَمْسِيْنَ عَامًا فَالْخَمْسِينَ تَعَرَّضَ لِلْعَدَدِ الْمُثْبَتِ  ِبالْاَلْفِ لَا لِحُكْمِ مَعَ بَقَاءِ الْعَدَدِ لِاَنَّ الْأَلْفَ مَتى بَقِيَتْ أَلْفًا لَمْ تَصْلَحْ اِسْمًا لِمَادُوْنَهَا بِخِلَافِ الْعَامِ كَاسْمِ الْمُشْرِكِيْنَ إِذَاخْضَ مِنْهُ نَوْعٌ كَانَ الْاِسْمُ وَاقِعًا عَلَى الْبَاقِي بَلَاخَلَلٍ ثُمَّ الْإِسْتِثْنَاء نَوْعَان مُتَّصِل وَهُوَ الْأَصْلُ وَتَفْسِيْرُهُ مَا ذَكَرْنَا وَمُنْفَصِلٌ وَهُوَ مَالَا يَصْلَحُ اسْتِخْرَاجَهُ مِنَ الْأَوَّلِ لِاَنَّ الصَّدْرَ لَمْ يَتَنَاوَلُهُ فَجُعِلَ مُبْتَدَاءً مَجَازًا قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى فَإِنَّهُمْ عَدُوّلَى الْارَبَّ الْعَلَمِيْنَ اى لكِنَّ رَبَّ الْعَلَمِيْنَ
And on this basis, [Imam al-Shafi'i] considered the beginning of the statement general in his saying (peace be upon him): 'Do not sell food for food except like for like' — general in little and much — except that the exception opposed it specifically in measured items, so it remained general in what is beyond that. And we said: This is an exception of a condition, so the beginning is general in conditions, and that is not valid except in quantity. And our companions (may Allah be pleased with them) argued with the saying of Allah Most High: 'So he stayed among them a thousand years except fifty years.' So 'fifty' applies to the number established by 'thousand,' not to the ruling while the number remains, because when 'thousand' remains a thousand it cannot be a name for what is less than it, unlike the general like the name 'polytheists' when a type is specified from it, the name applies to the rest without flaw. Then exceptions are of two types: connected, which is the original, and its explanation is what we mentioned; and disconnected, which is what cannot be extracted from the first because the beginning did not include it, so it is made a separate beginning metaphorically. Allah Most High said: 'Then they are enemies to me, [except] the Lord of the worlds' — meaning 'but the Lord of the worlds.'
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (usul dispute) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the effect of istithna (exception) on a general statement, specifically applied to the hadith: 'Do not sell food for food except like for like.' The Shafi'i view, as presented here, holds that the exception ('except like for like') operates as a mu'arid (opposing proof) that restricts the general prohibition to measured items only. Consequently, the general ruling applies only to what is measurable by weight or volume (makil), and small quantities like handfuls are excluded from the prohibition. The Hanafi response, which is the position of the author, argues that the exception here is an istithna of a condition (hal), not of a quantity. Therefore, the general prohibition applies to all conditions (equal, excess, or estimated), and the exception only allows the condition of equality. This general prohibition covers only items that can be measured (makil), because conditions only apply to quantifiable amounts. To support their view, the Hanafis cite the Quranic verse: 'So he stayed among them a thousand years except fifty years.' The exception of fifty years reduces the number, showing that exception addresses the number itself, not the general ruling. This differs from a general term like 'polytheists' which remains general after specifying a type. The passage concludes by defining the two types of istithna: muttasil (connected) where the excepted item is part of the general category, and munfasil (disconnected) where the excepted item was not included in the general statement and is treated as a separate clause.

Key Terms
استثناء متصل (istithna muttasil): An exception where the excepted item is part of the genus of the general statement and can be extracted from it.
استثناء منفصل (istithna munfasil): An exception where the excepted item was not included in the general statement and is treated as a separate beginning (mubtada') metaphorically.
معارض (mu'arid): An opposing proof that restricts the scope of a general statement, as used by Shafi'i in this dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why does the exception 'except like for like' in the hadith not restrict the prohibition to measured items only?
A) Because the exception is mu'arid and limits the general.
B) Because the exception is of a condition (hal), not a quantity, so the general remains for all conditions but only applies to measurable items.
C) Because the hadith is not authentic.
D) Because the exception is munfasil and therefore does not affect the general ruling.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between an exception of a condition and an exception of a quantity; the former does not restrict the general ruling to a subset but only allows the specific condition.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Definition of Istithna and the Quranic Proof
Defining istithna and presenting the Hanafi proof from Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of istithna and explain how the Quranic verse (29:14) demonstrates that istithna prevents speech, not just the ruling.

Core Idea
Istithna removes the excepted item from the speech itself, not just its ruling.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi definition of istithna as presented in Al-Husami. The central dispute is whether exception only affects the ruling of the excepted item or actually removes it from the utterance. The Hanafis argue from the Quranic verse about Prophet Nuh that 'a thousand years less fifty' must mean that the word 'thousand' is no longer spoken, because it cannot refer to less than a thousand. This leads to a fundamental divergence from the Shafi'i school, which analogizes istithna to general specification (takhsis).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi definition of istithna
Istithna is the extraction of the quantity of the excepted item from the excepted-from such that the excepted-from is no longer spoken for the remainder.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
The verse فلبث فيهم الف سنة الا خمسين عاما (29:14) is cited. The word 'alf' (thousand) is a specific number.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
'Alf' cannot be applied to less than a thousand. When 'illa' removes fifty, the remaining speech is about nine hundred fifty, so 'alf' is no longer spoken. This proves istithna prevents speech.
4
State the Shafi'i position and their analogy
Shafi'is hold that istithna only prevents the ruling, not speech. They analogize to takhsis al-amm: after specifying some polytheists, the word 'mushrikeen' still applies to the rest.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The analogy fails because in takhsis applying the general to the remainder is linguistically sound, but in istithna applying the excepted-from (e.g., 'alf') to the remainder (950) would be defective.

اور یہ عموم صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے مگر مقدار ( میل ) میں، اور ہمارے اصحاب نے استدلال کیا ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے ارشاد فلبث فيهم الف سنة الا خمسين عاما سے، پس لفظ مسین نے تعرض کیا ہے اس عدد سے جو الف سے ثابت ہورہا ہے، نہ کہ الف کے حکم سے عدد کے باقی رہنے کے ساتھ ، اس لئے کہ الف جب تک الف باقی ہے تو وہ مادون الالف کا اسم بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھے گا، بر خلاف عام کے جیسا کہ اسم مشرکین جب اس میں سے ایک نوع کو خاص رلیا جائے تو اس اسم کا اطلاق باقی پر واقع ہوگا بغیر خلل کے۔ پھر استثناء کی دو قسمیں ہیں، ایک متصل ، اور یہی اصل ہے، اور اس کی تفسیر وہ ہے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں، اور دوسری قسم منفصل، اور منفصل وہ ہے جو ماقبل سے اس کو نکالنے کی صلاحیت نہ رکھتا ہو، اس لئے کہ صدر کلام مستثنی کو شامل نہیں ہوتا ہے، پس مستثنی کو مجازاً کلام مستقل قرار دیا جائے گا، اللہ تعالیٰ نے ارشاد فرمایا فانهم عدو لي الارب العالمين عني لكن رب العالمين - تشریح : امام شافعی کا استثناء کے بارے میں یہ اصول ہے کہ استثناء بطریق معارضہ مانع حکم ہوتا ہے، مانع تکلم نہیں ہوتا ، اس اصول کے پیش نظر حضرت امام نے آپ صلی ایم کے ارشاد لا تبيعوا الطعام بالطعام الاسواء بسواء میں صدر کلام یعنی لا تبيعوا الطعام بالطعام کو عام گردانا ہے قلیل وکثیر سب کو عام ہے قلیل یعنی جو کیل میں نہ آسکے جیسے ایک مٹھی دو مٹھی کے بدلہ میں بیچنا، اور کثیر یعنی جو قلیل میں آسکے تو مستثنی منہ سب کو عام ہے، لہذا بیع کی تمام صورتیں حرام ہیں ، پھر الاسواء بسواء“ کے ذریعہ صرف مساوات کی صورت کو خارج کر دیا کہ برابری کے ساتھ اگر بیع ہے تو جائز ہے، اور مساوات کے علاوہ سب صورتیں نا جائز ہیں ، لہذا ایک مٹھی دو مٹھی کے عوض بیچنا بھی ناجائز اور حرام ہے، کیونکہ مساوات سے مراد جو کیل و قدر کے تحت آتی ہو، اور ایک مٹھی اور دو مٹھی یہ کیل کے تحت نہیں آتی لہذا یہ صدر کلام میں شامل رہ کر حرام ہو گی ، اور ہمارے نزدیک ایک مٹھی دو مٹھی کے عوض بیچنا حرام نہیں ہے، کیونکہ مقدار قلیل کو حدیث شامل ہی نہیں ہے۔ احناف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ استثناء میں اصل یہ ہے کہ مستثنی مستثنی منہ کی جنس سے ہو، اور یہاں مستثنی مساوات ہے جو حالت ہے، لہذا مستثنی منہ بھی از قبیل احوال ہوگا اور حالتیں کل تین ہیں (۱) مساوات (۲) مفاضلہ یعنی کمی بیشی کے ساتھ بیچنا (۳) مجازفتہ یعنی انکل اور اندازے سے بیچنا، تو صدر کلام یعنی لا تبيعوا الطعام ان تینوں حالتوں کو عام ہے کہ اناج کو اناج کے بدلہ ان تینوں حالتوں میں سے کسی حالت میں مت بیچو، پھر الا کے ذریعہ مساوات کی حالت کا استثناء کر دیا کہ مساوات کے ساتھ بیع جائز ہے، باقی دو حالتوں میں یعنی مجازفہ اور مفاضلہ جائز نہیں ہے، اور ان تین حالتوں کا تحقق غلہ کی اس مقدار میں ہوتا ہے جو کیل کے تحت آتی ہو، لہذا صدر کلام غلہ کی اسی مقدار کو شامل ہوگا جو کیل کے تحت آتی ہو، اور جو قلیل مقدار ہے صدر کلام اس کو شامل ہی نہیں ہے، لہذا ایک مٹھی دو مٹھی کے بدلہ بیچنا حرام نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ احناف کا مذہب ہے، کیونکہ قلیل کی مقدار نہی کے تحت داخل ہی نہیں ہے، مصنف نے احناف کی صرف ایک ہی دلیل پر اکتفا کیا ہے اس جگہ فریقین کے اور بھی دلائل ہیں، جو مطولات میں دیکھے جا سکتے ہیں۔ واحتج اصحابنا : - احناف کے نزدیک استثناء مستثنی کی مقدار کو خارج کرنے کے بعد باقی کے تکلم کا نام ہے، اور مستدل آیت باری تعالی ہے فلبث فيهم الف سنة الاخمسين عامل اس میں مستثنی یعنی خمسین کو الف سے نکالنے کے بعد باقی کا تکلم ہے، تو اللہ تعالی حضرت نوح کے اپنی قوم میں ساڑھے نوسوسال قیام کی خبر دے رہے ہیں، گو یا الف کا تکلم ہوا ہی نہیں ہے، احناف کے نقطہ نظر سے آیت میں کوئی اشکال نہیں ہے، اگر امام شافعی کے نقطہ نظر سے یہاں استثنا کو صرف مانع حکم قرار دیا جائے ، اور مانع تکلم نہ قرار دیا جائے تو آیت میں اشکال و خرابی لازم آئے گی، کیونکہ آیت کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ الف کا عدد تو باقی ہے مگر اس کا حکم باقی نہیں ہے یعنی الف سے ہزار مراد نہیں بلکہ الامین کے معارض ہونے کی وجہ سے ساڑھے نو سو مراد ہے، تو الف کا اطلاق مادون الالف پر ہورہا ہے اور یہ غلط ہے، کیونکہ الف الف رہتے ہوئے الف سے کم پر نہیں بولا جاتا ہے۔ بخلاف العام : - شوافع کے جواب کی تردید ہے، وہ کہتے ہیں کہ الف کا اطلاق مادون الالف پر ہوسکتا ہے، الف بولکر ساڑھے نو سو مراد لے سکتے ہیں، جیسے عام مخصوص منہ البعض میں، باوجود یکہ مخصوص عام کے حکم سے خارج ہے، پھر بھی عام بولا جاتا ہے جیسے مشرکین کا لفظ ہند، سندھ ، روم سب جگہ کے مشرکین کو شامل ہے، اگر مشرکین ہند کو بذریعہ تخصیص خارج کر دیا جائے تو بھی باقی مشرکین پر یہ لفظ بولا جاتا ہے، ایسے ہی استثنا میں مستثنی کو خارج کرنے کے بعد بقیہ پر مستثنی منہ کو بولا جاسکتا ہے۔ مصنف اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ استثنا کو عام پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے، کیونکہ عام میں تخصیص کے بعد مابقیہ پر عام کا اطلاق کرنے میں کوئی خرابی وخلل لازم نہیں آتا، اور استثنا میں مستثنی کو خارج کر کے بقیہ پر مستثنی منہ کے اطلاق سے خرابی لازم آتی ہے جیسے او پر تفصیل سے گذرا۔ ثم الاستثناء نوعان: مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ استثناء کی دو قسمیں ہیں، (۱) ایک متصل ہے اور یہی اصل ہے، اس کی تفسیر پہلے گزری کہ استثناء مستثنی کی مقدار کو خارج کرنے کے بعد باقی کے تکلم کا نام ہے، گویا مستثنی مستثنی منہ میں داخل ہوتا ہے پھر نکالا جاتا ہے جیسے جاء نی القوم الازید - زید مستثنی متصل ہے، (۲) دوسری قسم مستثنی منقطع ، اسی کو منفصل بھی کہتے ہیں، مستثنی منقطع اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کو اول سے یعنی مستثنی منہ سے نہ نکالا گیا ہو، کیونکہ وہ مستثنی منہ میں داخل ہی نہیں تھا ، جیسے جاء نی القوم الاحماراً، حمار مستثنی منقطع ہے، لہذا مستثنی منقطع مجازاً
And this generality does not possess capacity except in quantity (measure). And our companions have argued from Allah's saying, 'So he stayed among them a thousand years less fifty years.' Thus the word 'sineen' (years) pertains to that number which is established by 'alf' (thousand), not by the ruling of 'alf' with the number remaining. Because as long as 'alf' remains 'alf', it does not have the capacity to be a name for less than 'alf'. Unlike the general, as when the name 'mushrikeen' (polytheists) is specified by removing one type, the name applies to the rest without defect. Then exception is of two types: one is muttasil (connected), and that is the original; its interpretation is what we have mentioned. The second type is munfasil (disconnected), and it is that which does not have the capacity to be extracted from what precedes, because the first part of speech does not include the excepted item; thus the excepted item is metaphorically considered an independent speech. Allah said, 'فانهم عدو لي الارب العالمين عني لكن رب العالمين' [unclear]. Commentary: Imam Shafi'i's principle regarding exception is that exception is a preventer of the ruling by way of opposition, not a preventer of speech. According to this principle, the Imam considered the first part of the hadith, 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal,' as general, including little and much. Little is that which cannot be measured, like selling one handful for two handfuls. Much is that which can be measured. So all forms of sale are prohibited. Then by 'إلا سواء بسواء' (except equal for equal), only the case of equality is excluded: if sale is with equality, it is permissible; all other forms are impermissible. Thus selling one handful for two handfuls is also impermissible and prohibited, because equality refers to that which comes under measure, and one handful and two handfuls do not come under measure; therefore they remain included in the first part and are prohibited. And according to us, selling one handful for two handfuls is not prohibited, because the small quantity is not included in the hadith at all. The Hanafi proof is that the principle in exception is that the excepted item is from the same genus as the excepted-from; here the excepted item is equality, which is a state, so the excepted-from is also of the category of states. And the states are three: (1) equality, (2) mufadila (selling with excess or deficiency), (3) mujazafa (selling by estimation). So the first part 'Do not sell food' is general over these three states: do not sell food for food in any of these states. Then by 'illa' the state of equality is excepted: sale with equality is permissible; the other two states are not permissible. And the realization of these three states occurs in the quantity of grain that comes under measure; therefore the first part includes only that quantity which comes under measure. And what is a small quantity is not included in the first part at all; thus selling one handful for two handfuls is not prohibited, as is the Hanafi school, because the small quantity is not included under the prohibition. The author has sufficed with only one proof of the Hanafis; there are other proofs of both parties which can be seen in the detailed works. And our companions argued: According to the Hanafis, exception is the name for speech after extracting the quantity of the excepted item. And the proof is the verse 'فلبث فيهم الف سنة الا خمسين عاما' (So he stayed among them a thousand years less fifty years). In this, the excepted item, i.e., 'khamseen' (fifty), is extracted from 'alf' (thousand), and then speech remains. So Allah informs of Prophet Nuh's stay among his people of nine hundred fifty years, as if 'alf' was not spoken at all. From the Hanafi perspective, there is no difficulty in the verse. But if from Imam Shafi'i's perspective exception is considered only a preventer of the ruling, not a preventer of speech, then difficulty and corruption would follow in the verse. Because the meaning of the verse would be that the number 'alf' remains, but its ruling does not remain; i.e., by 'alf' not a thousand is meant, but due to the opposition by 'illa', nine hundred fifty is meant. Thus 'alf' is applied to less than 'alf', and this is wrong, because as long as 'alf' is 'alf', it is not uttered for less than 'alf'. Contrary to the general: This is a refutation of the Shafi'i response. They say that 'alf' can be applied to less than 'alf'; one can say 'alf' and mean nine hundred fifty, like a general that is specified from some parts. Even though the specified part is excluded from the ruling of the general, still the general is uttered, e.g., the word 'mushrikeen' includes polytheists of Hind, Sindh, Rum all places. If the polytheists of Hind are excluded by specification, still the word is uttered for the remaining polytheists. Similarly, in exception, after excluding the excepted item, the excepted-from can be uttered for the remainder. The author responds that analogizing exception to the general is not correct. Because in the general, after specification, applying the general to the remainder does not entail any defect. But in exception, applying the excepted-from to the remainder after excluding the excepted item entails a defect, as detailed above. Then exception is of two types: The author says that exception has two types: (1) muttasil, and this is the original; its interpretation has passed, that exception is the name for speech after extracting the quantity of the excepted item, as if the excepted item is included in the excepted-from and then extracted, e.g., 'جاءني القوم إلا زيد' (the people came except Zayd) — Zayd is muttasil exception. (2) The second type is munfasil, also called munqati'; munfasil is that which is not extracted from the first part, i.e., from the excepted-from, because it was not included in the excepted-from, e.g., 'جاءني القوم إلا حماراً' (the people came except a donkey) — the donkey is munfasi exception; thus the munfasil is metaphorically...
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage from the Urdu commentary on Al-Husami deals with the nature of istithna (exception) in usul al-fiqh, focusing on the Hanafi position and its difference from the Shafi'i school. The author begins by explaining that 'general' (عموم) does not have the capacity to include small quantities except in the context of measurement. The Hanafis then present their proof from the Quranic verse about Prophet Nuh (فلبث فيهم الف سنة الا خمسين عاما). The argument is that the word 'alf' (thousand) cannot be applied to less than a thousand; thus when 'illa' (except) removes fifty, the remaining speech is about nine hundred fifty, and 'alf' is no longer spoken. This demonstrates that istithna removes the quantity from speech, not just the ruling. In contrast, the Shafi'i view is that istithna only prevents the ruling, not the speech itself. The author then applies this dispute to the hadith 'لا تبيعوا الطعام بالطعام إلا سواء بسواء' (Do not sell food for food except equal for equal). The Shafi'is hold that the first part is general over all quantities, including small ones like handfuls, and the exception only allows equal measure; thus selling one handful for two is prohibited. The Hanafis argue that the first part only includes quantities that are measured, and small quantities like handfuls are not included at all; thus selling one handful for two is permissible. The author then presents the Hanafi proof that the excepted item (equality) is a state, and the excepted-from is also states (equality, excess/deficiency, estimation). The speech covers states only for measurable quantities. Then the author refutes the Shafi'i analogy to general specification (تخصيص العام), explaining that in takhsis, the general word remains applicable to the remainder without defect, but in istithna, applying the excepted-from to the remainder after extraction would be defective because the word 'alf' cannot mean less than a thousand. Finally, the author defines the two types of istithna: muttasil (connected) where the excepted item is included in the excepted-from and then extracted, and munfasil (disconnected) where it was never included. This is a core usul dispute with practical fiqh implications.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna): Extracting the quantity of the excepted item from the excepted-from such that the excepted-from is no longer spoken for the remainder.
متصل (muttasil): Connected exception where the excepted item is included in the excepted-from and then extracted, e.g., جاءني القوم إلا زيد.
منفصل (munfasil): Disconnected exception where the excepted item was never included in the excepted-from, e.g., جاءني القوم إلا حماراً.
مستثنی (mustathna): The item that is excepted or excluded.
مستثنی منہ (mustathna minhu): The phrase from which the exception is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of istithna (exception) on the excepted-from phrase?
A) It cancels the ruling for the excepted item only, leaving the speech intact.
B) It removes the excepted item from the speech, so the excepted-from is not used for the remainder.
C) It has no effect on speech or ruling.
D) It changes the meaning of the excepted-from to include the excepted item.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis define istithna as extraction of the excepted item from speech, not just from the ruling.

Types of Istithna: Muttasil and Munfasil
Defining the two types of istithna and refuting the Shafi'i analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between muttasil and munfasil istithna and explain why the Hanafi school refutes the Shafi'i analogy between istithna and takhsis.

Core Idea
Muttasil exception removes an included item; munfasil exception treats the excepted item as independent speech.

The previous lesson established the Hanafi definition of istithna. Here we learn about its two types: muttasil (connected) where the excepted item is part of the excepted-from, and munfasil (disconnected) where it is not. The author then reinforces the Hanafi stance by refuting the Shafi'i attempt to analogize istithna to takhsis, showing that the analogy creates linguistic contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Define muttasil istithna
Muttasil is when the excepted item is included in the excepted-from and then extracted, e.g., 'جاءني القوم إلا زيد' (the people came except Zayd). The word 'القوم' includes Zayd, then 'إلا' extracts him.
This is the foundational type.
2
Define munfasil istithna
Munfasil is when the excepted item was never included in the excepted-from, e.g., 'جاءني القوم إلا حماراً' (the people came except a donkey). Donkeys are not part of 'people'.
Also called munqati'.
3
Identify the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i analogy
Shafi'is analogized istithna to takhsis, claiming the excepted-from can be applied to the remainder. Hanafis respond that in takhsis applying the general to the remainder is linguistically sound, but in istithna applying the excepted-from (e.g., 'alf' for 950) is defective.
4
Apply the distinction to the hadith on food sale
The Hanafis argue that the hadith 'لا تبيعوا الطعام بالطعام' only covers measurable quantities. Small quantities like handfuls are not included in the initial speech (like munfasil), so they are not prohibited.
This shows the practical impact.

زید مستثنی متصل ہے، (۲) دوسری قسم مستثنی منقطع ، اسی کو منفصل بھی کہتے ہیں، مستثنی منقطع اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کو اول سے یعنی مستثنی منہ سے نہ نکالا گیا ہو، کیونکہ وہ مستثنی منہ میں داخل ہی نہیں تھا ، جیسے جاء نی القوم الاحماراً، حمار مستثنی منقطع ہے، لہذا مستثنی منقطع مجازاً
And this generality does not possess capacity except in quantity (measure). And our companions have argued from Allah's saying, 'So he stayed among them a thousand years less fifty years.' Thus the word 'sineen' (years) pertains to that number which is established by 'alf' (thousand), not by the ruling of 'alf' with the number remaining. Because as long as 'alf' remains 'alf', it does not have the capacity to be a name for less than 'alf'. Unlike the general, as when the name 'mushrikeen' (polytheists) is specified by removing one type, the name applies to the rest without defect. Then exception is of two types: one is muttasil (connected), and that is the original; its interpretation is what we have mentioned. The second type is munfasil (disconnected), and it is that which does not have the capacity to be extracted from what precedes, because the first part of speech does not include the excepted item; thus the excepted item is metaphorically considered an independent speech. Allah said, 'فانهم عدو لي الارب العالمين عني لكن رب العالمين' [unclear]. Commentary: Imam Shafi'i's principle regarding exception is that exception is a preventer of the ruling by way of opposition, not a preventer of speech. According to this principle, the Imam considered the first part of the hadith, 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal,' as general, including little and much. Little is that which cannot be measured, like selling one handful for two handfuls. Much is that which can be measured. So all forms of sale are prohibited. Then by 'إلا سواء بسواء' (except equal for equal), only the case of equality is excluded: if sale is with equality, it is permissible; all other forms are impermissible. Thus selling one handful for two handfuls is also impermissible and prohibited, because equality refers to that which comes under measure, and one handful and two handfuls do not come under measure; therefore they remain included in the first part and are prohibited. And according to us, selling one handful for two handfuls is not prohibited, because the small quantity is not included in the hadith at all. The Hanafi proof is that the principle in exception is that the excepted item is from the same genus as the excepted-from; here the excepted item is equality, which is a state, so the excepted-from is also of the category of states. And the states are three: (1) equality, (2) mufadila (selling with excess or deficiency), (3) mujazafa (selling by estimation). So the first part 'Do not sell food' is general over these three states: do not sell food for food in any of these states. Then by 'illa' the state of equality is excepted: sale with equality is permissible; the other two states are not permissible. And the realization of these three states occurs in the quantity of grain that comes under measure; therefore the first part includes only that quantity which comes under measure. And what is a small quantity is not included in the first part at all; thus selling one handful for two handfuls is not prohibited, as is the Hanafi school, because the small quantity is not included under the prohibition. The author has sufficed with only one proof of the Hanafis; there are other proofs of both parties which can be seen in the detailed works. And our companions argued: According to the Hanafis, exception is the name for speech after extracting the quantity of the excepted item. And the proof is the verse 'فلبث فيهم الف سنة الا خمسين عاما' (So he stayed among them a thousand years less fifty years). In this, the excepted item, i.e., 'khamseen' (fifty), is extracted from 'alf' (thousand), and then speech remains. So Allah informs of Prophet Nuh's stay among his people of nine hundred fifty years, as if 'alf' was not spoken at all. From the Hanafi perspective, there is no difficulty in the verse. But if from Imam Shafi'i's perspective exception is considered only a preventer of the ruling, not a preventer of speech, then difficulty and corruption would follow in the verse. Because the meaning of the verse would be that the number 'alf' remains, but its ruling does not remain; i.e., by 'alf' not a thousand is meant, but due to the opposition by 'illa', nine hundred fifty is meant. Thus 'alf' is applied to less than 'alf', and this is wrong, because as long as 'alf' is 'alf', it is not uttered for less than 'alf'. Contrary to the general: This is a refutation of the Shafi'i response. They say that 'alf' can be applied to less than 'alf'; one can say 'alf' and mean nine hundred fifty, like a general that is specified from some parts. Even though the specified part is excluded from the ruling of the general, still the general is uttered, e.g., the word 'mushrikeen' includes polytheists of Hind, Sindh, Rum all places. If the polytheists of Hind are excluded by specification, still the word is uttered for the remaining polytheists. Similarly, in exception, after excluding the excepted item, the excepted-from can be uttered for the remainder. The author responds that analogizing exception to the general is not correct. Because in the general, after specification, applying the general to the remainder does not entail any defect. But in exception, applying the excepted-from to the remainder after excluding the excepted item entails a defect, as detailed above. Then exception is of two types: The author says that exception has two types: (1) muttasil, and this is the original; its interpretation has passed, that exception is the name for speech after extracting the quantity of the excepted item, as if the excepted item is included in the excepted-from and then extracted, e.g., 'جاءني القوم إلا زيد' (the people came except Zayd) — Zayd is muttasil exception. (2) The second type is munfasil, also called munqati'; munfasil is that which is not extracted from the first part, i.e., from the excepted-from, because it was not included in the excepted-from, e.g., 'جاءني القوم إلا حماراً' (the people came except a donkey) — the donkey is munfasi exception; thus the munfasil is metaphorically...
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage from the Urdu commentary on Al-Husami deals with the nature of istithna (exception) in usul al-fiqh, focusing on the Hanafi position and its difference from the Shafi'i school. The author begins by explaining that 'general' (عموم) does not have the capacity to include small quantities except in the context of measurement. The Hanafis then present their proof from the Quranic verse about Prophet Nuh (فلبث فيهم الف سنة الا خمسين عاما). The argument is that the word 'alf' (thousand) cannot be applied to less than a thousand; thus when 'illa' (except) removes fifty, the remaining speech is about nine hundred fifty, and 'alf' is no longer spoken. This demonstrates that istithna removes the quantity from speech, not just the ruling. In contrast, the Shafi'i view is that istithna only prevents the ruling, not the speech itself. The author then applies this dispute to the hadith 'لا تبيعوا الطعام بالطعام إلا سواء بسواء' (Do not sell food for food except equal for equal). The Shafi'is hold that the first part is general over all quantities, including small ones like handfuls, and the exception only allows equal measure; thus selling one handful for two is prohibited. The Hanafis argue that the first part only includes quantities that are measured, and small quantities like handfuls are not included at all; thus selling one handful for two is permissible. The author then presents the Hanafi proof that the excepted item (equality) is a state, and the excepted-from is also states (equality, excess/deficiency, estimation). The speech covers states only for measurable quantities. Then the author refutes the Shafi'i analogy to general specification (تخصيص العام), explaining that in takhsis, the general word remains applicable to the remainder without defect, but in istithna, applying the excepted-from to the remainder after extraction would be defective because the word 'alf' cannot mean less than a thousand. Finally, the author defines the two types of istithna: muttasil (connected) where the excepted item is included in the excepted-from and then extracted, and munfasil (disconnected) where it was never included. This is a core usul dispute with practical fiqh implications.

Key Terms
استثناء متصل (istithna muttasil): Connected exception where the excepted item is included in the excepted-from and then extracted.
استثناء منفصل (منقطع) (istithna munfasil (munqati')): Disconnected exception where the excepted item was never included in the excepted-from.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general term by removing some of its instances while the general term remains applicable to the rest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of muttasil istithna?
A) جاءني القوم إلا زيدا (The people came except Zayd)
B) جاءني القوم إلا حمارا (The people came except a donkey)
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Istithna muttasil removes an included item from speech; istithna munfasil treats a non-included item as independent speech.

The Fourth Type: Expression Due to Necessity of Frequent Speech
Defines the fourth type of bayān bi al-ḍarūrah with a Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute and scope limitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the necessity of frequent speech (ḍarūrat kathrat al-kalām) justifies omitting the specified noun after a number, and apply the Hanafi ruling that the conjunction serves as a clarification (bayān) in such cases.

Core Idea
When custom requires brevity, a conjunction after a number clarifies the type, not adds an extra item.

This lesson explores the fourth type of bayān bi al-ḍarūrah, which arises from the need for brevity in everyday speech. The classic example is a debt statement: 'I owe one hundred and a dirham.' The Hanafi school holds that the conjunction immediately clarifies that the hundred refers to dirhams. Imam al-Shafi‘i disagrees, granting the speaker the right to explain. We will analyze the arguments and the role of custom ('urf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourth type of bayān bi al-ḍarūrah
Understand that it is based on the necessity of frequent speech (ḍarūrat kathrat al-kalām), leading to ellipsis (ḥadhf al-ma‘ṭūf ‘alayh).
2
Examine the Hanafi example
A debtor says 'upon me is one hundred and a dirham' or 'one hundred and a qafīz of wheat.' The conjunction 'and' is used without specifying the noun.
The omitted noun would be 'dirhams' or 'qafīz' in the plural.
3
State the Hanafi ruling
The conjunction is treated as a clarification (bayān) of the number, so 'one hundred and a dirham' means one hundred dirhams.
This is based on customary usage (ta‘āruf).
4
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the speaker's own clarification should be accepted, as in the case of 'one hundred and a garment' where the garment is a specific item not subject to such custom.
Thus, the debtor could later explain he meant one hundred dirhams plus a separate dirham, or something else.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and scope
Hanafis respond that omission of the conjoined noun is customary due to frequent use of numbers and lengthy speech. However, this principle applies only to debts for makīl/mawzūn (measured/weighed) items in general transactions; specific items like garments require a salam contract to be established as a debt.
This limits the rule's application and shows the role of 'urf in usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهُ مَا يَثْبُتُ بِضَرُورَةِ كَثْرَةِ الْكَلَام مِثْلُ قَوْلِ عَلَمَائِنَا فِيْمَنْ قَالَ لَهُ عَلَيَّ مِائَةٌ الله.. وَدِرْهَمْ أَوْمِائَةٌ وَقَفِيْزُ حِنْطَةٍ إِنَ الْعَطْفَ جُعِلَ بَيَانًا لِلْمِائَةِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي على اَلْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ فِي بَيَانِ الْمِائَةِ كَمَا إِذَاقَالَ لَهُ عَلَىَ مِائَةٌ وَثَوْبْ قُلْنَا إِنَّ حَذْفَ الْمَعْطُوفِ عَلَيْهِ مُتَعَارَفْ ضَرُوْرَةَ كَثْرَةِ الْعَدَدِ وَطُولِ الْكَلَام ذَلِكَ فِيْمَا يَثْبُتُ وُجُوبُهُ فِي الذِّمَّةِ فِي عَامَةِ الْمُعَامَلَاتِ كَالْمَكِيْلِ وَالْمَوْزُونِ دُونِ الشَّيَابِ فَإِنَّهَا لَا تَثْبتُ فِي الذِمَّةِ إِلَّا بِطَرِيقِ خَاصِ وَهُوَ السَّلَم - ترجمہ : ۔ اور بیان ضرورت کی چوتھی قسم وہ ہے جو کلام کے کثرت استعمال کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے ثابت ہوتی ہے، جیسے ہمارے علماء کا قول اس شخص کے بارے میں جس نے کہا له على مائة ودرهم يا مائة وقفيز حنطة تو عطف مائۃ کا بیان قرار دیا جائے گا، اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ مائة کے بیان میں قائل کا قول معتبر ہوگا ، جیسا کہ جب کہا له على مائة وثوب، ہم کہیں گے کہ معطوف علیہ کا حذف کثرت عدد اور طول کلام کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے متعارف
And from it is that which is established due to the necessity of frequency of speech, like the statement of our scholars concerning one who says 'upon me is one hundred and a dirham' or 'one hundred and a qafīz of wheat': the conjunction is made as clarification of the one hundred. Al-Shāfi‘ī said: the statement is his statement in clarifying the one hundred, just as when he says 'upon me is one hundred and a garment'. We said: indeed, the omission of the conjoined noun is customary due to the necessity of frequent numbers and length of speech. That is in matters whose obligation is established in the dhimmah in general transactions like measured and weighed items, not regarding individual items (shayāb?), for they are not established in the dhimmah except by a special way, which is salam. Translation: And the fourth type of expression by necessity is that which is established due to the necessity of frequent usage of speech. For example, our scholars' statement concerning one who says 'upon me is one hundred and a dirham' or 'one hundred and a qafīz of wheat': the conjunction will be considered as clarification of the one hundred. Imam al-Shāfi‘ī said: regarding the clarification of the hundred, the speaker's statement is credible, just as when he says 'upon me is one hundred and a garment'. We say: the omission of the conjoined noun is customary due to the necessity of frequency of numbers and length of speech.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth type of expression by necessity (بیان ضرورت), which arises from the need for brevity in frequent speech (ضرورة كثرة الكلام). The example given is a person who says, 'I owe one hundred and a dirham' or 'one hundred and a qafīz of wheat.' In such phrases, the number 'one hundred' is general, and the conjunction ('and') is used to specify what the hundred is. According to Hanafi scholars, the conjunction itself acts as an expression clarifying the number. Thus, 'one hundred and a dirham' means one hundred dirhams, and 'one hundred and a qafīz of wheat' means one hundred qafīz of wheat. Imam al-Shāfi‘ī disagrees, arguing that the speaker's own explanation of what he meant by 'one hundred' should be accepted, as in the case of 'one hundred and a garment' where the garment is a specific item. The Hanafi response is that omitting the specified noun (e.g., 'dirhams') after the number is a customary practice (متعارف) due to the frequency of using numbers and the length of speech. However, this principle applies to things that can be established as a debt in the dhimmah (liability) in general transactions, like measured and weighed items (مکیل و موزون). It does not apply to specific individual items (الشياب?), which can only be established in the dhimmah through a special contract, namely salam (advance payment). So the Hanafi position relies on 'urf (custom) and necessity to interpret such statements.

Key Terms
ضرورة كثرة الكلام (ḍarūrat kathrat al-kalām): The necessity arising from frequent usage of speech, leading to brevity and ellipsis.
عطف (‘aṭf): Grammatical conjunction, here used to link a number with a unit, clarifying the number.
حذف المعطوف عليه (ḥadhf al-ma‘ṭūf ‘alayh): Omission of the noun that should follow the number (e.g., 'dirhams' after 'one hundred').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi scholars, if someone says 'I owe one hundred and a dirham', what does it mean?
A) One hundred dirhams
B) One hundred plus a dirham
C) The speaker can later clarify
D) It is ambiguous

Key Takeaway
The necessity of frequent speech justifies interpreting a conjunction after a number as a clarification, not an addition, but only for standard measured/weighed debts.
