Ziyada: Naskh or Bayan? The Hanafi–Shafi'i Dispute on Increasing Quranic Rulings
Explains Hanafi position that ziyada is naskh, not bayan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school treats an increase (ziyada) upon a Quranic ruling via khabar wahid as naskh (abrogation) rather than bayan (clarification), and apply this principle to derive the Hanafi position in the four examples given.

Core Idea
Ziyada that restricts an absolute Quranic rule is naskh; naskh via khabar wahid is impermissible for Hanafis.

This lesson examines a foundational usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding ziyada (increase) upon a Quranic ruling through khabar wahid (single-narrator hadith) or qiyas (analogy). The Hanafi school, following Imam Abu Hanifa, classifies such an increase as naskh (abrogation) because it restricts the absolute or general Quranic command. Since naskh requires definitive evidence (tawatur) in the Hanafi method, a khabar wahid cannot effect it. You will see this principle applied to four concrete fiqh examples with direct practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle: Ziyada as naskh vs bayan
The core of the dispute is whether an addition (ziyada) to a clear Quranic ruling constitutes naskh (abrogation) or bayan (clarification). Hanafis consider it naskh because it changes the ruling; Shafi'is as bayan because it explains what was intended.
This difference stems from epistemological assumptions about the certainty of Quranic texts and the reliability of khabar wahid.
2
Trace the Hanafi dalil and rejection
Hanafis argue that the Quranic texts in question are general (amm) or absolute (mutlaq). Accepting a khabar wahid that restricts them would abrogate that generality/absoluteness, which is naskh. Since naskh requires tawatur (definitive evidence), a khabar wahid (zanni) cannot do it.
Key Quranic verses: 'Read what is easy' (amm), 'Flog them one hundred' (mutlaq), 'Circumambulate' (mutlaq).
3
Apply to Example 1: Fatiha in prayer
Quran: 'Read what is easy of the Quran' (amm). Hadith: 'No prayer except with Fatiha' (khabar wahid). Hanafi: Not making Fatiha fard because that would be naskh. Shafi'i: Makes Fatiha fard as bayan.
This is the most famous example of the dispute.
4
Apply to Examples 2-4: Hadd, Tawaf, Kaffarah
Similarly, for each: identify the Quranic text (mutlaq/amm), the source that would restrict it (khabar wahid or qiyas), and the resulting Hanafi ruling (rejection of the addition, though sometimes treating it as wajib).
Hanafis reject exile as part of hadd, purity as condition for tawaf, and faith condition for all kaffarahs, while Shafi'is accept them.
5
Synthesize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that for Hanafis, Fatiha is not a rukn (pillar), exile is not part of hadd, purity is not a shart (condition) for tawaf, and faith is not required in all kaffarahs; for Shafi'is, all these are required.
The root cause is the usul distinction between naskh and bayan and the role of khabar wahid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لئے ان کے نزدیک مخبر واحد اور قیاس سے زیادتی جائز ہے۔ وهو شيئ [؟] شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي ولهذا لم يجعل علماء نا : - ہمارے نزدیک چونکہ نص پر زیادتی نسخ ہے اور نسخ خبر واحد سے جائز نہیں لہذا ہمارے علماء نے خبر واحد سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی کر کے سورہ فاتحہ کو رکن نہیں قرار دیا، نص ہے فاقرء وا ماتيسر من القرآن، جو عام ہے اس کا عموم بتا رہا ہے کہ بغیر فاتحہ کے بھی نماز جائز ہے، اور خبر واحد ہے لا صلوة الابفاتحة الكتاب “اگر اس خبر واحد سے کتاب اللہ زیادتی کریں گے تو کتاب اللہ کا عام اور مطلق حکم مقید ہو جائے گا، یہ نسخ ہے، کیونکہ اطلاق منسوخ ہو جائے گا، اور خبر واحد سے کتاب اللہ کا نسخ جائز نہیں ہے، اس لئے ہمارے علماء نے خبر واحد سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی نہیں کی ، اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک چونکہ زیادتی نسخ نہیں ہے، بلکہ بیان ہے، اور بیان خبر واحد سے بھی ہو سکتا ہے، اس لئے ان کے نزدیک فاتحہ رکن ہو گا۔ اسی طرح غیر محصن کی حدز نا سو کوڑے ہیں، فاجلدوا كل واحد منهما مائة جلدة، اور خبر واحد ہے البكر بالبكر جلد مائة وتغريب ،عام، اس سے معلوم ہو رہا ہے کہ سو کوڑے کے ساتھ ایک سال جلا وطن کرنا بھی ہے، تو اس خبر واحد سے اگر کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی کرتے ہیں تو نسخ ہورہا ہے کیونکہ کتاب اللہ کا حکم جو مطلق سو کوڑے ہیں وہ ایک سال جلا وطن کے ساتھ مقید ہو جاتا ہے، اور کتاب اللہ کا نسخ خبر واحد سے جائز نہیں تو ہمارے علماء نے اس خبر واحد سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی نہیں کی اور جلاوطن کو حد کا جزء نہیں بنایا، البتہ امام وقت کی مصلحت پر ہے چاہے تو جلا وطن بھی کر سکتا ہے، اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک چونکہ کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی بیان ہے، اس لئے خبر واحد سے بھی جائز ہے تو ان کے نزدیک جلا وطن کرنا حد کا جزو ہے۔ اسی طرح طواف میں نص ہے وليطوفوا بالبيت العتيق، مطلق حکم ہے ، طہارت کی کوئی شرط نہیں ہے، اور مخبر واحد ہے الطواف بالبيت مثل الصلوۃ، جس سے معلوم ہو رہا ہے کہ طواف میں نماز کی طرح طہارت شرط ہے، تو اس مخبر واحد سے اگر کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی کرتے ہیں تو کتاب اللہ کا مطلق حکم طہارت کے ساتھ مقید ہو جاتا ہے، جو نسخ ہے اور نسخ خبر واحد سے جائز نہیں، لہذا زیادتی نہ کریں گے اور طواف میں طہارت کو شرط نہ قرار دیں ، گے البتہ خبر واحد پر عمل کرتے ہوئے طہارت کو واجب قرار دیا گیا ہے، اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک زیادتی چونکہ نسخ نہیں ہے، بیان ہے، اس لئے ان کے نزدیک طواف میں طہارت شرط ہے۔ اسی طرح کفارہ ظہار اور یمین میں تحریر رقبہ ہے مطلق غلام آزاد کرنا، اور کفارہ قتل میں فتحرير رقبة مومنةٍ ہے، مومن کی قید ہے، اب اگر کفارہ ظہار اور یمین کو کفارہ قتل پر قیاس کر کے ایمان کی شرط لگاتے ہیں، تو تحریر رقبتہ جو مطلق حکم ہے اس کو مقید کرنالازم آتا ہے، اور قیاس سے کتاب اللہ کا نسخ لازم آتا ہے، اس لئے ہمارے علماء نے کفارہ ظہار و یمین کو کفارہ قتل پر قیاس نہیں کیا، اور امام شافعی نے کفارہ ظہار و یمین کو کفارہ قتل پر قیاس کر کے ایمان کی شرط لگادی کہ سب کفاروں میں مومن غلام آزاد کرنا ہے، کیونکہ کفارے سب ایک ہی جنس ہیں ، اور کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی ان کے نزدیک نسخ نہیں ہے، بیان ہے، اور بیان قیاس سے جائز ہے۔
For them, increase through a single narrator and analogy is permissible. Explanation of Urdu al-Muntakhab al-Husami: And for this reason our scholars did not make ... because according to us increase upon the text is abrogation and abrogation through a single narrator is not permissible. Hence our scholars did not increase upon the Book of Allah through a single narrator and did not make Surah Fatiha a pillar. The text is 'Recite what is easy of the Quran', which is general, indicating that prayer without Fatiha is valid. And the single narrator report is 'No prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book'. If we increase upon the Book through this report, the general and absolute ruling of the Book becomes restricted – this is abrogation because the absoluteness is abrogated, and abrogation of the Book by a single narrator is not permissible. Therefore our scholars did not increase upon the Book through a single narrator. According to Imam Shafi'i, since increase is not abrogation but clarification, and clarification can be done by a single narrator, so for him Fatiha is a pillar. Similarly, the hadd for an unmarried person is one hundred lashes: 'Flog each of them one hundred lashes', and the single narrator report is 'The unmarried male and unmarried female, flog one hundred and exile'. This indicates that besides the hundred lashes, exile for a year is also required. If we increase upon the Book through this report, abrogation occurs because the absolute rulng of a hundred lashes becomes restricted with exile, and abrogation of the Book by a single narrator is not permissible. So our scholars did not increase upon the Book through this report and did not make exile a part of the hadd. However, it is at the discretion of the ruler to exile if he sees fit. According to Imam Shafi'i, since increase is clarification, it is permissible through a single narrator, so for him exile is a part of the hadd. Similarly, for tawaf, the text is 'And let them circumambulate the Ancient House', an absolute command with no condition of purity. The single narrator report is 'Circumambulation of the House is like prayer', indicating that purity is a condition. If we increase upon the Book through this report, the absolute ruling becomes restricted with purity – this is abrogation and not permissible. Therefore we do not consider purity a condition for tawaf, but acting on the report we consider it obligatory. According to Imam Shafi'i, increase is not abrogation but clarification, so for him purity is a condition. Similarly, for kaffarah of zihar and oath, there is 'freeing a slave' absolute, while for kaffarah of killing there is 'freeing a believing slave' with the condition of faith. If we analogize zihar and oath to killing and require faith, it would restrict the absolute ruling, necessitating abrogation through analogy. Hence our scholars did not analogize. Imam Shafi'i analogized and required faith in all kaffarahs because they are of one kind, and for him increase is not abrogation but clarification, and clarification through analogy is permissible.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul dispute addressing the principle of ziyada (increase) upon a Quranic ruling through khabar wahid (single-narrator hadith) or qiyas (analogy). The Hanafi position, following Abu Hanifa, is that such an increase constitutes naskh (abrogation) because it restricts an absolute (mutlaq) or general (amm) Quranic command. Since naskh through khabar wahid is not permitted in the Hanafi school, the increase is rejected. The Shafi'i school considers the same operation as bayan (clarification), which is permissible through any valid evidence. The author demonstrates with four examples: (1) Surah al-Fatiha in prayer – Quran says 'recite what is easy', general; hadith 'no prayer except with Fatiha' would restrict it; Hanafis do not make it a pillar (fard), while Shafi'is do. (2) Hadd for unmarried fornicator – Quran specifies 100 lashes absolute; hadith adds exile; Hanafis reject exile as part of hadd (though a ruler may exile as policy), Shafi'is include it. (3) Purity in tawaf – Quran commands tawaf absolutely; hadith equates tawaf with prayer requiring purity; Hanafis do not require purity as a condition but deem it wajib, Shafi'is require it. (4) Kaffarah for zihar and oath – Quran says free a slave (absolute); for qatl (killing) it requires a believing slave; qiyas would restrict; Hanafis avoid analogy to prevent naskh, while Shafi'is apply it. This illustrates a foundational usul difference with direct fiqh consequences. The authority weight is from the late Hanafi usul tradition (Husami commentary), but the positions reflect Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
زیادتی (ziyada): Adding a new ruling or condition to a Quranic text through another source (khabar wahid or qiyas).
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a ruling by a later revealed ruling.
بیان (bayan): Clarification of an existing ruling, not changing it.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): Hadith transmitted by one or few narrators, not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is Surah al-Fatiha not considered a fard (pillar) in prayer?
A) Because there is no authentic hadith mentioning Fatiha.
B) Because making it fard would be ziyada on the Quranic text 'Read what is easy', which is considered naskh (abrogation) via khabar wahid, and naskh via khabar wahid is not permitted in Hanafi usul.
C) Because the Quran does not mention prayer at all.
D) Because Imam Abu Hanifa disliked Surah al-Fatiha.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, an increase (ziyada) that restricts an absolute or general Quranic ruling is classified as naskh, and since naskh via khabar wahid is impermissible, such increases are rejected; the Shafi'i school considers them bayan and accepts them.

Distinguishing Mustanbatah from Mannusa and the Concomitant of Ta'diyah
Clarifying the scope of cause and defining the essential function of extension

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mustanbatah and mannusa causes, and explain why Hanafis consider ta'diyah necessary for a valid cause.

Core Idea
The definition of a cause includes extension to new cases; for Hanafis, without ta'diyah there is no valid cause.

This passage first clarifies that when earlier scholars discussed 'adam al-illah (non-existence of the ruling implying non-existence of the cause), they meant causes derived by ijtihad (mustanbatah), not textually stated causes (mannusa). It then defines the ruling of the cause as ta'diyah and presents the Hanafi position that extension is necessary, contrasting with al-Shafi'i who permits causation without extension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of causes
Note the distinction between mustanbatah (derived) and mannusa (textually specified) as stated in the tanbih.
Only mustanbatah are subject to the principle of 'adam al-illah.
2
Understand takhsis in mannusa
Recognize that mannusa causes can be specified (takhsis) due to a preventer like doubt, so the ruling may not follow the cause.
Example: zinā does not always lead to hadd if there is shubha.
3
Define ta'diyah as the ruling of the cause
Identify the definition: extension of the textual ruling to cases with no text, established by predominant opinion with possibility of error.
This is the hukm of the illah.
4
Recognize the Hanafi position
The text states that ta'diyah is a necessary concomitant (lazim) of causation for Hanafis.
Without extension, the cause is not valid.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i view
Al-Shafi'i allows causation without extension, arguing that cause is from the genus of proofs and thus necessitates obligation like any proof.
The Hanafi response (cut off) likely argues that indication of an attribute being a cause does not necessitate extension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه :- مصنف عالیہ نے کتاب میں ملک کا بیان کیا ہے اس سے مراد عللِ مستنبطہ ہیں، عللِ منصوصہ مراد نہیں ہیں، یعنی وہ علتیں مراد ہیں جو ادلہ اربعہ سے مستنبط ہیں، وہ نہیں جن پر نص وارد ہوتی ہیں، کیونکہ اکثر فقہاء عللِ منصوصہ میں تخصیص کے قائل ہیں، جیسے زنا حد کی علت منصوصہ ہے، سرقہ قطع ید کی علت منصوصہ ہے، علل منصوصہ میں بعض صورتوں میں علت کے باوجود کسی مانع کی وجہ سے حکم نہیں پایا جاتا جیسے زنا یا سرقہ پایا گیا کسی شبہ کی وجہ سے ثبوت نہ ہو سکا تو با وجود علت کے حکم محقق نہ ہوگا ، غرض علل منصوصہ میں کسی مانع کے سبب حکم کا علت سے مختلف جائز ہے۔

( فیض سبحانی) وَأَمَّا حُكْمُهُ فَتَعْدِيَةُ حُكْمِ النَّصِّ إِلَى مَالاَ نَصَّ فِيْهِ لِيَثْبَتَ فِيْهِ بِغَالِبِ الرَّأْيِ عَلَى اِحْتِمَالِ الْخَطَأِ فَالتَّعْدِيَةُ حُكْمٌ لاَزِمٌ لِلتَّعْلِيْلِ عِنْدَنَا وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِي هُوَ صَحِيحٌ بِدُونِ التَّعْدِيَةِ حَتَّى جَوَّزَ التَّعْلِيْلَ بِالثَّمَنِيَّةِ وَاحْتَجَّ بِأَنَّ هَذَا لَمَّا كَانَ مِنْ جِئْسِ الْحُجَج وَجَبَ أَنْ يَتَعَلَّقَ بِهِ الْإِيجَابُ كَسَائِرِ الْحُجَجِ أَلَا تَرَىٰ أَنَّ دَلَالَةَ كَوْنِ الْوَصْفِ عِلَّةٌ لاَ يَقْتَضِي تَعْدِيَتَهُ بَلْ يُعْرَفُ ذَلِكَ بِمَعْنًى فِي الْوَصْفِ وَوَجْهُ
A note: The noble author mentioned 'milk' in the book; by that he means derived causes (mustanbatah), not textually specified causes (mannusa). That is, he intends causes that are derived from the four proofs, not those on which a text exists. Because most jurists believe in specification (takhsis) of textually specified causes, such as adultery is the textually specified cause of the hadd punishment, theft is the textually specified cause of amputation. In textually specified causes, in some cases the ruling is not found despite the cause due to a preventer, such as adultery or theft occurred but due to some doubt it could not be established, so despite the cause the ruling is not realized. In short, in textually specified causes, the ruling differing from the cause due to a preventer is permissible. (Fayd Subhani) And as for its ruling: it is the extension of the ruling of the text to that which has no text, so that it may be established therein by predominant opinion with the possibility of error. So extension is a necessary concomitant of cause for us, while according to al-Shafi'i cause is valid without extension, such that he permitted causation by a low value (thumaniyyah), and argued that since this is from the genus of proofs, it is necessary that obligation be attached to it like other proofs. Do you not see that the indication of an attribute being a cause does not necessitate its extension; rather that is known by a meaning in the attribute, and the aspect...
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage consists of two parts. First, a tanbih (note) clarifying that the author's discussion throughout the book about causes refers specifically to `ilal mustanbatah` — causes derived by jurists from the four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas). This is distinct from `ilal mannusa`, causes that are explicitly stated in the texts themselves, such as zinā being the cause for the hadd punishment, or theft for amputation. The note explains that most jurists accept takhsis (specification) in mannusa causes, meaning that the cause may exist but a preventer (like doubt) can block the ruling. For example, if zinā is committed but with a valid doubt (shubha), the hadd is not applied despite the cause being present. So the Hanafi principle of 'adam al-illah applies only to mustanbatah causes. The second part is an Arabic extract (from a text called Fayd Subhani) that defines the hukm (ruling) of the cause as ta'diyah (extension) — i.e., the function of a cause is to extend the ruling from the original text to a new case where no text exists. The Hanafi position is that ta'diyah is necessary for the validity of cause (al-ta'diyah hukm lazim lil-ta'lil), while al-Shafi'i held that cause is valid even without extension, allowing causation by a low value or attribute without requiring transference. Al-Shafi'i argued that since causation is a type of proof, it must entail obligation like other proofs. The text ends mid-argument: the indication of an attribute being a cause does not necessitate its extension; rather that is known by a meaning in the attribute. This concludes the lesson.

Key Terms
علل مستنبطہ (ilal mustanbatah): Causes derived by jurists through ijtihad from the four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), as opposed to causes explicitly stated in the texts.
علل منصوصہ (ilal mannusa): Causes that are explicitly mentioned in the primary texts (e.g., zinā as cause for hadd, theft for amputation). These can be subject to takhsis due to a preventer like doubt.
تعدية (ta'diyah): Extension of the ruling from the original text (asl) to a novel case (far') via the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tanbih, what type of cause does the book's discussion on 'adam al-illah pertain to?
A) Textually specified causes (ilal mannusa)
B) Both mustanbatah and mannusa equally
C) Derived causes (ilal mustanbatah)
D) Causes that are agreed upon by all schools

Key Takeaway
The tanbih delimits the scope of 'adam al-illah to mustanbatah causes, and the Arabic part establishes ta'diyah as the necessary ruling of a cause in the Hanafi school.

Tarjīḥ: The Hanafi Science of Preponderance
Defining tarjīḥ and explaining two types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tarjīḥ according to the Hanafi school and distinguish between its two types: tarjīḥ by qūwwat al-athar and tarjīḥ by qūwwat al-thabāt.

Core Idea
Tarjīḥ prefers one evidence over another by an intrinsic quality, not by adding more evidences.

When two evidences appear equally strong, the jurist must resolve the conflict through tarjīḥ — a principled method of giving preference. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of tarjīḥ and explains two of its four types: strength of effect (qūwwat al-athar) and strength of establishment (qūwwat al-thabāt). Understanding tarjīḥ is essential for reconciling seemingly contradictory proofs in Islamic legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core concept of tarjīḥ
Locate the definition of tarjīḥ in the Arabic text: it is giving precedence to one of two similar evidences over another by a quality (waṣf), not by an independent evidence.
The waṣf is intrinsic to the evidence itself, such as clarity or strength of indication.
2
Distinguish between waṣf and independent evidence
The author stresses that a qiyās cannot be preferred by another qiyās, nor a verse by another verse, because the second evidence is independent, not a quality. Understand why this distinction is crucial.
This prevents infinite regress and maintains the principle that tarjīḥ depends on internal superiority.
3
Analyze the first type: tarjīḥ bi-qūwwat al-athar
Examine the first type: preponderance by strength of effect. This means one proof has a stronger impact in establishing the ruling, like istiḥsān over qiyās. The effect is a quality within the proof.
Istiḥsān is considered stronger because it considers underlying objectives.
4
Analyze the second type: tarjīḥ bi-qūwwat al-thabāt
Study the second type: preponderance by strength of establishment. An evidence that more firmly indicates a ruling aligned with legal objectives (e.g., alleviation) is preferred. The Hanafi example: wiping the head (masḥ) is preferred over washing because it is more established in indicating alleviation.
This contrasts with the Shāfiʿī view that wiping is a pillar requiring repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Chapter on Preponderance (Tarjīḥ). And when conflict (muʿāraḍa) arises, the method in it is preponderance. And it (tarjīḥ) is an expression of preferring one of the two similars over the other by a quality (waṣf). So much so that the scholars said: A qiyās does not become preponderant by another qiyās, and likewise the Book and the Sunnah. Rather, some become preponderant over others by a strength within it. And similarly, the possessor of multiple wounds does not become preponderant over the possessor of a single wound. And the things by which preponderance occurs are four: (1) Preponderance by strength of effect (qūwwat al-athar), because the effect is a quality in the proof; so whenever it is strong, it is more suitable due to superiority in the quality of the proof, like the example of istiḥsān in opposing qiyās. (2) Preponderance by the strength of its establishment (qūwwat thabāt) upon the witnessed ruling, like our saying concerning the head that it is wiped (masḥ), because it is more established (athbat) in indicating alleviation (takhfīf) than their saying that wiping is a pillar (rukn) indicating repetition (takrār). For the pillars of prayer are completed by completion (ikmāl), not by repetition. So the effect of wiping in alleviation is necessary in every purification that is not rationally conceivable to be cleaning, like tayammum and the like. Translation: This chapter is about the explanation of tarjīḥ. And when conflict (muʿāraḍa) occurs, the method in it is tarjīḥ. And tarjīḥ is the name for giving preference to one of two equals over the other in terms of a quality. To the extent that the scholars of uṣūl have said: A qiyās will not become preponderant by another qiyās, and similarly the Book and the Sunnah. Rather, some will become preponderant over others due to a strength that is in it. And similarly, the one with multiple wounds will not be preponderant over the one with a single wound. And the things by which tarjīḥ occurs are four: (1) Giving preference by strength of effect, because the effect is a quality in the proof; so when the effect is strong, the qiyās is more suitable, due to the increase in the quality of the proof, like the example of istiḥsān in opposing qiyās. (2) And tarjīḥ occurs by the strength of its establishment upon the ruling to which it is testified, like our saying concerning the head that it is wiped, because it is more proving (athbat) in indicating alleviation than their saying that wiping is a pillar indicating repetition. Because the pillars of prayer, their completion is by perfection (ikmāl), not by repetition. So, in any case, the effect of wiping in alleviation is necessary in every purification that is not rationally conceivable to be cleaning, like tayammum and its like. Clarification: The noble author begins the explanation of tarjīḥ, and when conflict occurs in evidences, the need for tarjīḥ arises, so that the conflict ends. But if one who argues gives a reason for tarjīḥ, the opponent has the option to give another reason for tarjīḥ to counter it. Conflict in qiyās-based evidences is repelled through tarjīḥ. In any case, tarjīḥ is defined as giving preference to one of two equal evidences over another due to some specific quality. They said 'quality' because it shows that the thing by which tarjīḥ is given is not an independent proof itself, but rather exists as a quality subordinate to some independent proof. Therefore, the testimony of a just person will be preferred over that of a sinful person due to the quality of justice, but the testimony of four men over two men is not subject to tarjīḥ due to the multiplicity of evidence, because the extra two men's testimony is an independent proof, not a quality. For this reason, the uṣūliyyūn say: A qiyās will not become preponderant over another qiyās on account of a third qiyās, because that is not a quality but an independent proof. Similarly is the ruling for the Book and the Sunnah: one verse will not become preponderant over another on account of a third verse, nor one hadith over another on account of a third hadith, because tarjīḥ is based on an additional quality, not on multiplicity of evidence. Yes, each of the Book, Sunnah, and qiyās can be made preponderant over its opponent by the strength that is present in that very evidence. So a clear verse (mufassar) will be preponderant over a vague (mujmal) one, a well-known report (mashhūr) over a solitary one (wāḥid), because this tarjīḥ is due to the quality of strength. Similarly, the one with multiple wounds will not be preponderant over the one with a single wound. For example, Khālid gave Rāshid one wound, and Rāshid gave Khālid multiple wounds, resulting in Khālid's death, so the blood-money is on both...
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on tarjīḥ (preponderance), a critical tool for resolving conflicts between apparently equal evidences. The author first defines tarjīḥ: it is giving preference to one of two similar evidences over another based on a quality (waṣf), not by adding another independent evidence. This is why a qiyās cannot be preferred by another qiyās, nor a verse by another verse, because the additional evidence is independent, not a quality. The passage then explains two of the four types of tarjīḥ. The first is tarjīḥ by 'strength of effect' (qūwwat al-athar): if a proof has a stronger effect (like istiḥsān over qiyās), it is preferred. The second is tarjīḥ by 'strength of establishment' (qūwwat al-thabāt): a proof that is more firmly established in indicating a particular ruling (like wiping the head indicating alleviation) is preferred over one indicating severity (like it being a pillar requiring repetition). The author illustrates with the Hanafi argument that wiping the head in wuḍūʾ (as opposed to washing) is a lightened duty, while the Shafiʿi view that it is a pillar requiring repetition is against the spirit of alleviation. The Urdu commentary expands these points with examples from testimony law and the principle that an external cause cannot serve as a quality.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): Giving preference to one of two similar evidences over another by a quality (waṣf) inherent in the evidence
معارضہ (muʿāraḍa): Conflict between two equally strong evidences
وصف (waṣf): A quality inherent in an evidence that makes it preferable, not an independent evidence
قوت اثر (qūwwat al-athar): The strength of the effect of an evidence, such as a clear textual indication or a principle like istiḥsān
قوت ثبات (qūwwat al-thabāt): The strength of an evidence's establishment in indicating a particular ruling, especially when it aligns with broader legal objectives (like alleviation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can a qiyās not be made preponderant by another qiyās?
A) Because qiyās is not a valid source of evidence in Hanafi law.
B) Because the additional qiyās is an independent evidence, not a quality (waṣf).
C) Because two qiyās can never be compared.
D) Because qiyās is always weaker than istiḥsān.

Key Takeaway
Tarjīḥ is the Hanafi method for resolving conflicts between equally strong evidences by preferring one based on an intrinsic quality, such as stronger effect or stronger establishment in conveying the Law's objectives.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
Definition and Types of Tarjih (Preference) in Conflicting Evidences
Defines tarjih, its condition, and first two types with a practical dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tarjih, identify its essential condition, and apply the first two types to evaluate the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on wiping the head.

Core Idea
Tarjih must be by an attribute inherent in the evidence, not by another independent proof.

When two evidences conflict and are equal in strength, how does a mujtahid choose? The science of usul al-fiqh provides tarjih (preference), a method of weighting one evidence over another. This lesson explains the precise definition of tarjih, its critical condition—that preference is given by an attribute (wasf) within the evidence, not by an external independent proof—and illustrates the first two types: preference by strength of effect and preference by strength of establishment. A classic Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on wiping the head during wudu shows how these types operate in practice.

Guided Path
1
Define tarjih and identify its essential condition
Literally, tarjih means giving preference. In usul, it is giving preference to one of two equal evidences over the other by a specific attribute (wasf) inherent in the evidence, not by another independent evidence. This condition is crucial: the preferring factor must be an attribute subordinate to the evidence, not a separate proof.
Example: preferring a just witness's testimony over a sinner's by the attribute of justice (attribute), not preferring four witnesses over two because the extra witnesses are an independent evidence.
2
Distinguish between preference by attribute and preference by independent evidence
The passage emphasizes that tarjih is by an attribute, not by another evidence. Hence, one qiyas cannot be preferred over another by a third qiyas, nor one verse by another verse, nor one hadith by another hadith. However, preference by strength inherent in the evidence (e.g., preferring a clear verse over a concise one) is valid because the strength is an attribute.
The attribute must be attached to the evidence itself, not an external independent proof.
3
Understand the first type: strength of effect (quwwat al-ta'thir)
When one evidence has a stronger effect in producing its ruling, it is preferred. For example, istihsan (juristic preference) is often preferred over qiyas because its effect is stronger in fulfilling the purposes of the Law.
Strength of effect is an attribute accompanying the evidence, making it a valid basis for tarjih.
4
Understand the second type: strength of establishment (quwwat al-thubat)
Here, the attribute of one evidence is more firmly attached (thabit) to its ruling than another. The passage uses the example of wiping the head (masah 'ala al-ra's). The Hanafis analogize it to other wipings (e.g., over khuffs), taking 'wiping' as the 'illa, which consistently produces relaxation and non-repetition. The Shafi'is analogize it to washing limbs, taking 'pillarhood' as the 'illa, leading to repetition. Hanafis argue that 'pillarhood' does not consistently entail repetition (pillars in prayer are not repeated), so the attribute 'wiping' is more firmly established to the ruling of relaxation.
The more consistently the attribute is attached to the ruling across cases, the stronger the evidence.
5
Analyze the masah dispute using the two types of tarjih
Identify each school's qiyas: Shafi'i uses 'illa of rukniyyah, Hanafi uses 'illa of mash. Then apply strength of establishment: Hanafi 'illa (mash) consistently leads to takhfif in all non-rational purifications, while Shafi'i 'illa (rukn) does not consistently lead to repetition. Therefore, the Hanafi qiyas is preponderant.
This shows how tarjih by strength of establishment resolves an inter-madhhab conflict.

The Divine Flood 301 Urdu commentary of Al-Muntakhab Al-Husami. It is giving preference to one of two problematic [evidences] over the other by virtue of an attribute, so much so that the scholars of usul have said: one qiyas will not be preferred because of another qiyas, and similarly the Book and the Sunnah, and some will be preferred over others because of a strength that is in it, and similarly the one with multiple wounds will not be preferred over the one with one wound. And the things by which preference occurs are four: (1) preference by strength of effect, because effect is an attribute in the proof, so when the effect is strong, the qiyas will be more appropriate, due to increase of attribute in the proof, like the example of istihsan against qiyas. (2) And preference occurs by strength of establishment of the attribute upon the ruling for which it is made a witness, like our statement regarding wiping the head that it is wiping, because it is more establishing in indicating relaxation than the statement of the Shafi'is that wiping is a pillar in indicating repetition, because the pillars of prayer, their completion is by perfection and not by repetition. So anyway, the effect of wiping is in relaxation, so it is necessary for every non-rational purification, like tayammum and the like. Commentary: The honored author begins the discussion of tarjih. When there is conflict among evidences, the need for tarjih arises to remove the conflict. But if the proponent presents a reason for preference, the opponent retains the option to counter it with another reason. By tarjih, conflict in analogical evidences is repelled. Anyway, tarjih is giving preference to one of two equal evidences over the other by a specific attribute. He said 'attribute' to indicate that the thing by which preference is given is not itself an independent evidence, but rather it is found as an attribute subordinate to an independent evidence. Hence, the testimony of a just person is preferred over that of a sinner by the attribute of justice, and the testimony of four men over two men is not eligible for preference due to multiplicity of evidence, because the additional two men's testimony in the four is an independent evidence, not an attribute. For this reason, the usulis say: one qiyas will not be preferred over another qiyas because of a third qiyas, because that is not an attribute, it is an independent evidence. Similarly is the ruling of the Book and Sunnah: one verse will not be preferred over another verse due to a third verse, and one hadith will not be preferred over another hadith due to a third hadith, because the basis of tarjih is on an additional attribute, not on multiplicity of evidence. However, one may prefer the Book, Sunnah, or qiyas over its opposite due to the strength that is present in that evidence itself. Hence, an explanatory verse is preferred over a concise one, a well-known report over a solitary one, because this tarjih is by the attribute of strength. Similarly, one with multiple wounds is not preferred over one with one wound. For example, Khalid wounded Rashid once, and Rashid wounded Khalid multiple times, as a result of which Khalid died; then blood money will be obligatory on both. In contrast, if one's wound is strong and fatal compared to the other, then death will be attributed to him, like one cut off a hand and the other struck the neck; then the one who struck the neck will be considered the killer. And that by which tarjih occurs - the author says: the matters by which tarjih is obtained are four: (1) strength of effect: among two conflicting qiyases, one has strong effect, so it will have preference over the other due to strength of effect. Strength of effect is an attribute that accompanies the qiyas, it is not an independent matter. Hence tarjih occurs through it. For this reason, in most places istihsan is given preference over qiyas, and that is due to strength of effect. (2) The second reason for tarjih is strength of establishment: that the attribute's establishment and attachment to the ruling is strong, i.e., the attribute of one qiyas is more attached to its ruling, and in the other qiyas the attribute does not have such attachment; then the attached is preferred over the non-attached. For example, Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes wiping the head to the washed limbs and takes 'pillarhood' as the cause, and considers repetition and three-fold wiping to be sunnah in head wiping as in the washed limbs. But we hold there is no three-fold repetition. We analogized wiping the head to other forms of wiping like wiping over khuffs etc., and the cause is the act of wiping itself. That is, just as due to wiping, relaxation is sunnah in wiping over khuffs etc., similarly in wiping the head, relaxation is sunnah. Here, Imam al-Shafi'i gave the attribute of pillarhood as cause; this is not more establishing and attached for repetition, because repetition due to pillarhood is not found elsewhere besides the washed limbs in wudu. Pillarhood exists in many places but repetition does not, like in prayer, standing, bowing, prostration etc. are all pillars, but they do not have repetition; rather they have completion and moderation. Therefore, the attribute of pillarhood is not attached for repetition. And the attribute we mentioned - the attribute of wiping - is attached and establishing for relaxation and non-repetition, meaning wherever there is wiping, there is relaxation and non-repetition, like wiping over khuffs, wiping over a splint, wiping in tayammum etc. Hence, the qiyas of the Hanafis by the cause of the attribute of wiping will be preponderant over the qiyas of the Shafi'is by the cause of the attribute of pillarhood, because our qiyas's attribute is more attached and established to the ruling. If someone asks: if a person does istinja with a stone without water, it is true, and there is no non-repetition in it; rather repetition is sunnah. The answer is: we mean those places where purification by wiping is non-rational, and in istinja with a stone, purification is rational because the removal of impurity is occurring. And tarjih by multiplicity of fundamentals, because in multiplicity of fundamentals there is an increase of attachment of the ruling with it, and tarjih by absence in case of its absence, and it is the weakest of the ways of tarjih because absence...

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the concept of tarjih (preference/weighting) in the context of conflicting evidences (ta'arud al-adilla). The author begins by defining tarjih as giving preference to one evidence over another by virtue of a specific attribute (wasf), not by another independent evidence. This is crucial: the preferring factor must be an attribute inherent in the evidence itself, not a separate evidence. For example, the testimony of a just person is preferred over a sinner's by the attribute of justice, but the testimony of four men is not preferred over two simply because there are more witnesses, since the additional witnesses constitute an independent evidence. Similarly, one qiyas is not preferred over another by a third qiyas, nor one verse by another verse, nor one hadith by another hadith. However, preference can be given by strength inherent in the evidence itself, such as preferring a clear (mufassar) verse over a concise (mujmal) one, or a well-known hadith over a solitary one.

The passage then lists four ways of tarjih, but only the first two are explained in detail: (1) tarjih bi quwwat al-ta'thir (preference by strength of effect): when one evidence has a stronger effect in producing its ruling, like istihsan being preferred over qiyas in many cases. (2) tarjih bi quwwat al-thubat (preference by strength of establishment): when the attribute of one evidence is more firmly attached to its ruling than another. The author provides a classic Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute as an example: the number of times to wipe the head in wudu. The Shafi'is analogize wiping the head to washing the limbs, citing 'pillarhood' as the cause, and thus require repetition (three times). The Hanafis analogize wiping the head to other types of wiping (e.g., over khuffs), taking 'wiping' itself as the cause, and thus hold that repetition is not required; rather, relaxation (takhfif) is the ruling. The Hanafi argument is that the attribute 'wiping' is more consistent with relaxation/non-repetition across all forms of wiping, while the attribute 'pillarhood' does not necessarily entail repetition, as pillars in prayer are not repeated. Therefore, the Hanafi qiyas is stronger in establishment.

The passage also briefly mentions the third and fourth types: (3) tarjih bi kathrat al-usul (preference by multiplicity of fundamentals) and (4) tarjih bi al-'adam (preference by absence), stating that the latter is the weakest. The text cuts off mid-sentence on the fourth type.

The commentary (sharh) by the author expands on the matn, clarifying that tarjih is needed only when evidences are equal and conflicting. The opponent can bring counter reasons for preference. The discussion is purely within the framework of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, demonstrating how to weigh evidences when they appear to conflict.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Giving preference to one of two equal evidences over the other by a specific attribute, not by another independent evidence.
قوة التأثير (quwwat al-ta'thir): The strength of effect of an evidence in producing its ruling; a stronger effect makes the evidence preponderant.
قوة الثبات (quwwat al-thubat): The strength of establishment of the attribute (wasf) upon the ruling; how firmly the attribute is attached to the ruling across different cases.
الوصف (al-wasf): An attribute inherent in the evidence that serves as the basis for preference; it must be subordinate to the evidence, not an independent proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the testimony of four witnesses not automatically preferred over two witnesses by way of tarjih?
A) Because all witnesses are equal in reliability.
B) Because the additional two witnesses constitute an independent evidence, not an attribute.
C) Because tarjih cannot be done in testimonies.
D) Because the number of witnesses is not a valid attribute for tarjih.

Key Takeaway
Tarjih resolves conflict by preferring an evidence with a stronger inherent attribute, not by additional independent proofs.

Nisab as Illah Mushabih al-Sabab: Hanafi Classification and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Explaining nisab as a cause resembling a reason, with objection and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criteria for classifying nisab as illah mushabih al-sabab and contrast it with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Nisab for zakat is a cause in name and meaning but its ruling is delayed — it is an illah mushabih al-sabab.

This lesson examines the Hanafi usul concept of illah mushabih al-sabab through the concrete example of nisab for zakat. Understanding why nisab is not a complete cause before the passage of a year reveals how Hanafi legal theory treats delayed rulings. We will also see how this classification leads to a practical difference with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools on when zakat becomes obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Understand the three levels of causality
The passage distinguishes nisab as a cause (illah) in name, in meaning, and in ruling. Identify each: name because it is legislatively set, meaning because it is effective in obligating zakat, but not in ruling because the obligation is delayed.
This tripartite division is crucial for Hanafi usul.
2
Identify the two principles for illah mushabih al-sabab
The author gives two conditions: (1) The intermediate factor (nama) does not originate from the cause (nisab). (2) The intermediate factor is not an independent cause itself. Verify each from the text.
3
Apply the principles to nisab and nama
Check if nama originates from nisab? No — growth comes from trade, feeding, etc. Is nama independent? No — it depends on hawl. Hence nisab is illah mushabih al-sabab, not a true cause nor a pure reason.
4
Examine the objection and its resolution
Why not call nisab sabab mushabih al-illah? The answer: the resemblance to a cause (illah) is stronger because nisab is the origin and nama is an attribute; priority is given to the origin over the attribute.
The author uses the analogy of shooting an arrow to illustrate a true cause (the hitting is from the shot).
5
Compare with Shafi'i and Maliki positions and note the thamarah al-khilaf
Shafi'i: nisab is a complete cause from the start; hawl is only for collection convenience. Maliki: nisab is not a cause at all before hawl. Hanafi: nisab is illah mushabih al-sabab. The practical difference: early payment is wajib (Shafi'i), invalid (Maliki), or permissible but not wajib (Hanafi).

ومن حكمه انه لايظهر: - نصاب جب علت مشابہ بالسبب ہے تو اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ شروع سال - بـ میں زکوۃ کی ادا واجب نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ شروع سال میں وصف نماء نہیں ہے البتہ شروع سال میں ادا ئیگی جائز ہوگی ،
A commentary: Similarly, nisab of zakat before the passage of a year is a cause (illah) in name and meaning but not in ruling (hukman), and it resembles a reason (sabab). It is a cause in name because nisab is legislatively set for the obligation of zakat, and the obligation is attributed to nisab. In meaning it is a cause because nisab is effective in the ruling (obligation), since wealth (from nisab) makes benefiting the poor obligatory, and that is realized by paying zakat. But not a cause in ruling because nisab is not considered an absolute cause, rather a cause with the attribute of growth (nama), whether actual or constructive, for which the passage of a year (hawl) stands in. So nisab becomes a complete cause only with hawl, thus zakat is obligated after hawl. So the ruling is delayed until nama (hawl), resembling a reason (sabab), because between a reason and its effect there is a temporal gap. The author gave two principles: (1) When a cause's ruling is delayed until something not originated from the cause, it is not illah mushabih al-sabab. (2) When the ruling is delayed until something that is not an independent cause but resembling causes, then the first is illah mushabih al-sabab. If the intermediate is an independent cause, the first is a pure sabab. Then objection: Since nisab has both resemblance of cause and reason, why is it called illah mushabih al-sabab? Answer: because the ruling is delayed to a non-independent attribute (nama), so nisab resembles a cause more strongly since nisab is the origin and nama an attribute. Imam Shafi'i considers nisab a complete cause before hawl; Imam Malik says nisab is not a cause at all before hawl. The ruling: at the beginning of the year, zakat is not obligatory but its payment is permissible.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the nature of nisab as a legal cause (illah) for the obligation of zakat in Hanafi usul. The author explains that nisab is an 'illah mushabih al-sabab' — a cause that resembles a reason. It resembles a cause because it is the legislatively designated basis for zakat, and it resembles a reason because the obligation is not immediate but delayed until the attainment of nama (growth) which is marked by the passage of a year (hawl). The author presents two principles to determine when something is considered illah mushabih al-sabab: the intermediate factor (nama) must not originate from the cause (nisab) nor be an independent cause itself. Here, nama does not come from nisab (growth is from trade, feeding, etc.) and is not independent (it depends on hawl). Thus nisab is not a true cause (would require nama from nisab) nor a pure reason (would require nama to be independent). An objection arises: since nisab also resembles a reason (sabab mushabih al-illah), why emphasize its resemblance to a cause? The answer: because the delay of the ruling to nama shows a stronger resemblance to a cause (since the ruling is attributed to nisab as the origin), and priority is given to the origin over the attribute. The passage then contrasts the Hanafi view with that of Imam Shafi'i, who treats nisab as a complete cause from the start of the year (thus zakat is immediately owed but collection delayed), and Imam Malik, who denies nisab as a cause before hawl (so early payment is invalid). The final ruling: at the beginning of the year, zakat is not obligatory but may be paid voluntarily — a key Hanafi position.

Key Terms
علت (illah): A cause or effective attribute that directly produces a ruling in legal theory.
سبب (sabab): A reason or occasion that is external to the ruling and often separated by time.
علت مشابہ بالسبب (illah mushabih al-sabab): A cause that resembles a reason because its ruling is delayed due to an intermediate condition.
نماء (nama): Growth or increase, actual (trade) or constructive (opportunity cost), considered necessary for zakat obligation.
حولان حول (hawlan al-hawl): Passage of a full lunar year; condition for zakat on nisab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in the passage, what is the ruling on paying zakat at the beginning of the year before the passage of hawl?
A) It is wajib and must be paid immediately.
B) It is not wajib but its payment is permissible.
C) It is not permissible to pay before hawl.
D) It is wajib only if the wealth has grown.

Key Takeaway
Nisab is an illah mushabih al-sabab because the ruling (obligation) is delayed until a non-independent and non-originating condition (nama/hawl) is met, distinguishing Hanafi from Shafi'i and Maliki views.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Two Effective Attributes and Substitution in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the rule of two effective attributes and substitution concepts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of two effective attributes to determine which attribute is the legal cause, and use substitution (iqamah al-shay' maqam ghayrihi) to derive rulings where direct evidence is unavailable.

Core Idea
A later attribute becomes cause meaningfully and legally; substitution lets evidence stand for the evidenced.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Husami presents two foundational tools of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The first is the rule of two effective attributes: when a ruling depends on two attributes, the one occurring later is the cause both meaningfully (ma'nan) and legally (hukman), while the earlier remains only a meaningful cause. The second is the principle of substitution (iqamah al-shay' maqam ghayrihi), where a motivating cause or evidence is made to stand in place of the actual motive or evidenced. These tools enable jurists to extend rulings to cases where direct application of the original cause is impractical.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Principles
Read the passage to distinguish the rule of two effective attributes from the concept of substitution. Note that the first principle deals with causes that are composed of multiple attributes, while the second deals with replacing something with its sign or cause.
2
Understand the Classification of Causes
Grasp the three types of cause: meaningful (ma'nan), legal (hukman), and nominal (isman). In the two-attribute rule, the later attribute is both meaningful and legal, but not nominal; the earlier is only meaningful. This classification determines how the ruling is attributed.
3
Apply to Emancipation Example
Work through the example of kinship and ownership causing emancipation. If ownership occurs later, it is the legal cause; if kinship occurs later, it is the legal cause. The earlier attribute remains a meaningful cause because it contributes to the effect.
This shows that both attributes are effective, but their roles differ.
4
Analyze the Riba Dispute
Examine the Hanafi position on riba: the cause is the combination of quantity (qadr) and type (jins). Riba al-fadl requires both attributes; riba al-nasi'ah can be prohibited by a single attribute due to semblance (shabah). Compare this with the Shafi'i position requiring both for any riba.
Use the madhhab_dispute_map block for details.
5
Explore Substitution Types
Identify the two types of substitution: (1) making the motivating cause stand for the motive (e.g., travel for hardship, illness for destruction), and (2) making evidence stand for the evidenced (e.g., wife's statement for love in conditional divorce). Recognize that these are applications of istihsan.
The substitution principle allows rulings to be based on practical indicators when the real cause is hidden.

والسفر علة للمرخصة : - سفر رخصت کے لئے اسما اور حکما علت ہے معنی علت نہیں ہے اسما تو اس لئے ہے کہ رخصت کی سفر کی طرف نسبت ہوتی ہے، جیسے کہا جاتا ہے القصر رخصة السفر، اور حکما اس لئے علۃ ہے کہ نفس سفر سے رخصت کا ثبوت ہو جاتا ہے ، اور معنی اس لئے علت نہیں ہے کہ اصل رخصت سفر کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے، بلکہ مشقت کی وجہ سے ہے مگر مشقت کا اندازہ مشکل تھا، اس لئے سفر کو مشقت کے قائم مقام کر دیا، کیونکہ سفر عام طور پر مشقت کا سبب ہوتا ہے۔
واقامة الشى مقام غیرہ :۔ مصنف یہ کہتے ہیں ایک شی کو اس کے غیر کے قائم مقام کرنا دو طرح سے ہوتا ہے، ایک تو یہ کہ سبب داعی کو مدعو کے قائم مقام کرنا، جیسے سفر مشقت کا سبب داعی ہے، تو اس کو مشقت کے قائم مقام کر دیا ، یعنی سبب کو مسبب کا درجہ دیدیا، اسی طرح مرض یه از دیا د مرض اور ہلاکت کا سبب داعی ہے، یعنی مرض کی وجہ سے بیماری بڑھنے اور ہلاک ہونے کا اندیشہ ہے، مگر باطنی امر ہے ، مرض سے ہلاکت ہو بھی سکتی ہے، اور نہیں بھی ہو سکتی تو اس کا اعتبار ساقط کر کے مرض کو ازدیاد اور ہلاکت کے قائم مقام کر دیا ، اور مرض کو رخصت کی علت قرار دیا۔
دوسرے یہ کہ دلیل کو مدلوں کے قائم مقام کرنا ، جیسے شوہر نے بیوی سے کہا ان احببتنی فانت طالق ، اگر تو مجھ سے محبت کرے گی تو تجھے طلاق ، بیوی نے کہا انا احبک میں تجھ سے محبت کرتی ہوں ،تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی، حالانکہ عورت کی بات محض خبر اور محبت کی دلیل ہے، کیونکہ حقیقی محبت تو دل میں ہوتی ہے ، اس کا پتہ لگانا مشکل ہے، تو اس کا قول جو دلیل محبت ہے اس کو مدلول یعنی محبت کے قائم مقام کر دیا۔
In giving that the report of love is made to stand in place of love, in the husband's statement 'if you love me, you are divorced', and like in purity that it is made to stand in place of need in permissibility of divorce. Commentary: The author (may Allah have mercy on him) is stating a general principle that when a ruling is connected to two effective attributes, then among these two attributes, the one that occurs later in existence will be a cause meaningfully and legally, but not nominally, and the first attribute will be only a meaningful cause, meaning it will also resemble a cause. The later attribute is legally a cause because the ruling is attributed to the second attribute, and the ruling exists only with the existence of this second attribute. And it is meaningful a cause because the later attribute is effective in the ruling. And the first attribute is also effective in the ruling because it is also a meaningful cause, and it is a pillar among the pillars of the cause. Therefore the first attribute will be similar to the cause, not merely a reason, because if we consider the first attribute ineffective in the ruling, it would necessitate that only the later attribute is the cause, while the combination of both attributes is the cause. Like the combination of kinship and ownership is the cause of emancipation. Then whichever occurs later will be effective in the ruling. If ownership is found later, like a person buys his close relative slave, then ownership is the later existence, so it will become a cause meaningfully and legally: legally because immediately after ownership emancipation is established, and meaningfully because ownership is effective in emancipation, and not nominally because ownership has not been set for emancipation, rather the combination of kinship and ownership is set for emancipation. And the first attribute, kinship, will be only a meaningful cause because kinship is also effective in emancipation, but it will not be a cause legally or nominally because after kinship, without ownership, emancipation is not established, nor is kinship set for emancipation; rather the combination of kinship and ownership is set for emancipation. And if the contrary, i.e., kinship is later, like someone bought a slave of unknown lineage, then after a month the slave claimed that the buyer is his real brother and it was proven, then here kinship is the later attribute, so it will become a cause meaningfully and legally, not nominally, and the first attribute ownership will be only a meaningful cause. In any case, when the combination of two attributes is the cause of a ruling, and one is found first and the other later, then the later attribute will be a cause meaningfully and legally, and the first attribute will be a meaningful cause. And if both are simultaneous, then both will be causes meaningfully, legally and nominally, i.e., a complete cause. And when they are effective collectively, they will also be considered effective individually, even if the nature of effectiveness is different. That is, when the two attributes are separate, even if neither attribute is a real cause, still each attribute remains similar to the cause; they will not be called reasons; they will be called causes. Like the cause of riba according to us is the combination of quantity and type. If these two attributes exist, then both riba al-fadl and riba al-nasi'ah, i.e., excess and delay, are prohibited. Hence selling one sa' of wheat for two sa' of wheat is prohibited because it is excess, this is prohibited, and delay is also prohibited, because the combination of quantity and type is a complete cause. And if only one of the two attributes is found, i.e., only quantity or only type, then riba al-fadl (excess) will not be prohibited, but riba al-nasi'ah (delay) will be prohibited even if equal, because in delay, although there is no real riba and excess, but there is a resemblance of excess in that cash and credit differ in price. So when in riba al-nasi'ah there is the semblance of excess and the semblance of riba, to prohibit it, the combination of both attributes i.e., the complete cause is not needed, rather one attribute is sufficient to establish prohibition, because each of the two attributes is similar to the cause, which is called the semblance of cause. So for riba al-fadl which is real riba and of strong degree, the combination of quantity and type is necessary to establish it, while riba al-nasi'ah which is the semblance of riba and of weak degree, is established by the semblance of cause i.e., one attribute. And travel is a cause for concessions: travel is a cause for concessions nominally and legally, not meaningfully. Nominally because the concession is attributed to travel, as it is said 'qasr is the concession of travel', and legally because the concession is established by travel itself, and meaningfully not because the real concession is not due to travel, but due to hardship, but measuring hardship was difficult, so travel was made to stand in place of hardship because travel generally causes hardship. And making a thing stand in place of another: The author says making a thing stand in place of another occurs in two ways: one is making the motivating cause stand in place of the motive, like travel is a motivating cause of hardship, so it was made to stand in place of hardship, i.e., the cause was given the status of the effect. Similarly, illness: illness is a motivating cause of increase and destruction, i.e., due to illness there is fear of worsening and destruction, but it is an internal matter; illness may or may not lead to destruction, so its consideration was dropped and illness was made to stand in place of increase and destruction, and illness was made the cause of concession. The second is making the evidence stand in place of the evidenced, like a husband said to his wife 'if you love me, you are divorced', the wife said 'I love you', then divorce occurs, even though the wife's statement is merely a report and evidence of love, because real love is in the heart, difficult to detect, so her statement which is evidence of love is made to stand in place of the evidenced, i.e., love.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Husami presents two important usul al-fiqh principles. First, when a ruling depends on two effective attributes (sifaat), the one that occurs later in time is considered the cause (illa) both meaningfully (ma'nan) and legally (hukman), but not nominally (isman). The earlier attribute is only a meaningful cause. This is illustrated with the example of emancipation ('itq): kinship (qarabah) and ownership (milk) together cause emancipation. If ownership occurs later, it is the cause legally and meaningfully; if kinship occurs later, it is that cause. The second principle is the substitution of one thing for another (iqamah al-shay' maqam ghayrihi). This occurs in two ways: (1) making a motivating cause (sabab da'i) stand in for the motive (mad'u), e.g., travel stands for hardship, or illness stands for worsening/destruction. (2) Making evidence (dalil) stand in for what is evidenced (madlul), e.g., a wife's statement 'I love you' in a conditional divorce stands for actual love. Both principles are used to derive rulings where direct measurement is difficult. The author, following the Hanafi school, emphasizes that the combination of attributes forms the complete cause, but a single attribute can suffice when it resembles the cause, as in riba al-nasi'ah.

Key Terms
علة (illa): The effective cause that brings about a legal ruling; in this text, a cause can be meaningful (ma'nan), legal (hukman), or nominal (isman).
وصف (sifah): An attribute or characteristic that may serve as part or all of the cause for a ruling.
إقامة الشيء مقام غيره (iqamah al-shay' maqam ghayrihi): Making one thing (a cause or evidence) stand in the place of another (the motive or what is evidenced) for the purpose of deriving rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi position on the cause of riba al-nasi'ah when only one attribute (quantity or type) is present?
A) It is not prohibited because the complete cause is missing.
B) It is prohibited due to the semblance of excess (shubhat al-fadl).
C) It is permissible because equality in quantity makes it valid.
D) It is prohibited only if both attributes are present.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul recognizes that a ruling can be caused by a combination of attributes, where the later one is the legal cause, and that substitution allows practical indicators to stand in for hidden realities.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Shart (Condition): Definition and Types in Hanafi Usul
Defining shart and its categories in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define shart, distinguish it from 'illah and sabab, and apply the Hanafi rule that shart may substitute for 'illah when the 'illah is not suitable, using istihsan.

Core Idea
Shart triggers existence, not obligation; when the 'illah fails, shart can step in by istihsan.

In Hanafi usul, the rulings of Allah are connected to certain categories: cause ('illah), condition (shart), sign ('alamah), and sabab. Among these, shart plays a unique role: it makes the ruling exist without making it obligatory. This lesson unpacks the definition of shart, its two types, and how it interacts with 'illah and sabab, including the critical exception where shart replaces an unsuitable 'illah through istihsan. You will learn the precise boundaries of these concepts, essential for sound legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Define shart in Hanafi usul
Read the opening definition: shart is that to which the existence (wujud) of a ruling is attributed, not its obligation (wujub). Note the exclusion of sabab, 'alamah, and 'illah.
The linguistic meaning 'sign' is secondary; the legal meaning is technical.
2
Identify the two types of shart
The text describes type one: pure shart (e.g., 'if you enter, you are divorced'). Type two: shart that takes the place of 'illah (e.g., digging a well). Understand the conditions for the second type.
The second type is an exception triggered by istihsan.
3
Distinguish shart from 'illah and sabab in the well-digging example
Analyze the three elements: digging (shart), walking (sabab), weight ('illah). Understand why the ruling is attributed to shart, not the others.
The 'illah (weight) is natural and not transgressive; sabab (walking) is permissible.
4
Apply the rule when 'illah is suitable vs. unsuitable
When 'illah is suitable, shart does not override it (e.g., witnesses of yamin vs. shart). When unsuitable, shart can substitute (e.g., well-digging in public land).
This determines liability in case of retraction or accident.

موجود ہو اور حکم کا ، وجوب شرط سے نہ ہو، وجود کی قید سے سبب اور علامت خارج ہو گئے ، اور وجوب کی نفی سے علت خارج ہو گئی ، جیسے کسی نے طلاق معلق دی، ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق کہہ کر تو دخول دار کے وجود سے طلاق موجود ہو گی لیکن اس کا وجوب و ثبوت انتِ طالق “ سے ہوگا، دخول دار سے نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہ تو شرط محض ہے، یہ شرط کی پہلی قسم ہے۔ اور شرط کی دوسری قسم یہ ہے کہ شرط علت کے حکم میں اور اس کے قائم مقام ہوتی ہے ، جیسے راستہ میں کنواں کھودنا، یہ اس میں گرنے کی شرط ہے، اور وہاں تک چل کر جانا سبب محض ہے، اور گرنے والے کے بدن کا ثقل بھاری پن ) اس میں گرنے کی علت ہے لیکن زمین کنواں کھودنے سے پہلے مانع اور ثقل کے عمل کو روکنے والی تھی، پس کنواں کھودنا اس مانع کو زائل کرنا ہوا، اور مانع کا زائل کرنا شرط کہلاتا ہے، تو ثابت ہو گیا کہ کھودنا شرط ہے ، تو اس جگہ شرط ، علت اور سبب سب جمع ہو گئے، اور یہ قاعدہ ہے کہ جب شرط کے ساتھ علت یا سبب ہو اور علت صالح للحکم ہو تو علت کو ترجیح دیجاتی ہے ، اور شرط اور سبب دونوں کو ترک کر دیا جاتا ہے ،مگر یہاں علت حکم کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی کیوں کہ گرنے والے کا ثقل امر طبعی ہے، اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کو اسی طرح پیدا کیا ہے، اور اس میں کوئی تعدی نہیں ہے، الہذا حکم علت کی طرف منسوب نہیں کیا جائے گا، اور اس کا کنویں تک چل کر جانا جو سبب ہے اس کی طرف بھی حکم منسوب نہیں کیا جاسکتا، اس لئے کہ چلنا ایک مباح امر ہے، لہذا چلنے پر بھی ضمان دیت نہ ہوگا ، اب لا محالہ گر کر مرنے کا حکم شرط کی طرف ہی منسوب ہوگا، مگر چونکہ یہ شرط ہے اور شرط میں حقیقتہ ضمان نہیں ہوا کرتا تو ہم نے اس کے اندر دونوں پہلوؤں کی رعایت کی اور کہا کہ اگر اپنی ذاتی زمین میں کنواں کھودا ہے تو شرط ہونے کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا ، یا گرنے والا جان بوجھ کر گرا ہو تب بھی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا ، اور اگر غیر مملوکہ زمین میں کنواں کھودا ہے تو شرط کو علت کے قائم مقام کر کے ضمان واجب کریں گے، کیونکہ شرط علت کے معارض نہیں ہے اس طرح کہ علت صالح نہیں ہے اور شرط صالح الحکم ہے اور شرط کو علت کے ساتھ مشابہت بھی ہے، کیونکہ شرط کے ساتھ وجود متعلق ہے، جیسے علت کے ساتھ وجود متعلق ہوتا ہے ، لہذا شرط کو علت کے قائم مقام کر کے یہ حکم لگا دیا کہ کنواں کھودنے والے پر جان و مال کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ مگر یہ بات ذھن میں رہے کہ مرتکب شرط پر صرف ضمان محل واجب ہوگا یعنی دیت واجب ہوگی ، مباشرت قتل کا ضمان یعنی کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا اور نہ وہ میراث سے محروم ہو گا جب کہ کنویں میں گر کر مرنے والا اس کا مورث ہو، کیونکہ
الفيضُ الحجازي
۳۳۱
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
کنواں کھودنے والا مباشر قتل نہیں ہے۔
وَأَمَّا إِذَا كَانَتِ الْعِلَّةُ صَالِحَةُ لَمْ يَكُنِ الشَّرْطُ فِي حُكْمِ الْعِلَّةِ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا اِنَّ شَهُودَ الشَّرْطِ وَالْيَمِينِ إِذَا رَجَعُوْا جَمِيعًا بَعْدَ الحُكْم إنّ الضَّمَانَ عَلى شُهُودِ الْيَمِين لِأَنَّهُمْ شُهُودُ الْعِلّةِ وَكَذَلِكَ الْعِلَّةُ وَالسَّبَب إِذَا اجْتَمَعَا سَقَطَ حُكُم السَّبَبِ كَشُهُودِ التَّخْبِيْرِ وَالْاِخْتِيَارِ إِذَا اجْتَمَعُوْا فِي الطَّلَاقِ وَالْعَتَاقِ ثُمَ رَجَعُوْا بَعْدَ الحُكْم إِنَّ الضَّمَانَ عَلَى شُهُودِ الْإخْتِيَارِ لأَنَّهُ هُوَ الْعِلَّةُ وَالتَّخْبِيرُ سَبَبْ وَعَلى هَذَا قُلْنَا إِذَا اخْتَلَفَ الْوَلِيُّ وَالْحَافِرُ فَقَالَ الْحَافِرُ انَّهُ أَسْقَطَ نَفْسَهُ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلَهُ اسْتِحْسَانًا لِاَنَّهُ يَتَمَسَّكُ بِمَا هُوَ الْأَصْلُ وَهُوَ صَلَاحِيَةُ الْعِلَّةِ لِلْحُكْمِ وَيُنْكِرُ خِلَافَةَ الشَّرْطِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا ادَّعَى الْجَارِحُ الْمَوْتَ بِسَبَبٍ أَخَرَ لَا يُصَدِّقُ لِأَنَّهُ صَاحِب عِلَّةٍ . ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال جب علت صالح محکم ہو تو شرط علت کے حکم میں نہ ہوگی ، اور اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ جب شرط اور یمین کے گواہوں نے رجوع کر لیا قاضی کے فیصلہ کے بعد ، تو ضمان یمین کے گواہوں پر ہوگا، ( یعنی نصف مہر کا ضمان) اس لئے کہ یہی علت کے گواہ ہیں، اور اسی طرح علت اور سبب جب دونوں جمع ہو جا ئیں تو سبب کا حکم ساقط ہو جائے گا، جیسے تخییر اور اختیار کے گواہ جب طلاق اور عتاق میں جمع ہو جائیں، پھر حکم کے بعد رجوع کرلیں، تو ضمان اختیار کے گواہوں پر ہوگا ، اس لئے کہ اختیار علت ہے اور تخییر سبب ہے، اور اسی بنیاد پر ہم نے کہا کہ جب ولی اور حافر نے اختلاف کیا، پس حافر نے کہا کہ اس نے اپنے آپ کو خود گرایا ہے، تو حاضر کا قول معتبر ہوگا استحسانا ، اس لئے کہ حافر اس چیز سے استدلال کر رہا ہے جو اصل ہے، اور اصل علت کا حکم کی صلاحیت رکھنا ہے، اور شرط کے خلیفہ ہونے کا انکار کر رہا ہے، برخلاف اس کے کہ جب جارح کسی دوسرے سبب سے موت کا دعوی کرے ، تو جارح کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی، اس لئے کہ جارح صاحب علت ہے۔ شریح : جب شرط اور علت جمع ہوں اور علت حکم کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے تو شرط علت کے حکم میں نہ ہوگی ، بلکہ حکم علت کی طرف ہی منسوب ہوگا، جیسے قاضی کے سامنے گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ خالد نے اپنی بیوی کو اس طرح طلاق دی ہے ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق تو یہ شہود یمین ہوئے ، کیونکہ تعلیق یمین بغیر اللہ ہے، پھر دو گواہوں نے شرط کے پائے جانے کی گواہی دی کہ خالد کی بیوی گھر میں داخل ہوئی، تو یہ شہود شرط کہلائیں گے ، اب قاضی نے طلاق
Commentary: The third type of matters related to rulings is shart (condition). Lexically, shart means a sign. In Islamic legal terminology, shart is that thing to which the existence (wujud) of a ruling is attributed, not its obligation (wujud). That is, when the shart is present, the ruling exists, but the obligation of the ruling is not from the shart. By the restriction of existence, sabab and 'alamah are excluded, and by the negation of obligation, 'illah is excluded. For example, if someone gives a suspended divorce by saying, "If you enter the house, you are divorced," then upon entry into the house, the divorce exists, but its obligation and establishment are from "you are divorced," not from entering the house, because that is a pure shart. This is the first type of shart. The second type of shart is that it takes the ruling of 'illah and stands in its place. For example, digging a well in a path: this is a shart for falling into it, walking to that place is a pure sabab, and the weight of the falling person's body is the 'illah for falling. But before digging the well, the ground was a man' (preventer) blocking the action of the weight. So digging the well removes that preventer, and removing a preventer is called shart. Thus it is established that digging is a shart. In this place, shart, 'illah, and sabab are all combined. The rule is: when shart is accompanied by 'illah or sabab and the 'illah is qualified to produce the ruling, then preference is given to the 'illah, and both shart and sabab are disregarded. But here, the 'illah does not have the capacity for the ruling because the weight of the falling person is a natural matter created by Allah, and there is no transgression (ta'diyya). Therefore the ruling will not be attributed to the 'illah. Also, walking to the well, which is the sabab, cannot be attributed to the ruling because walking is a permissible act, so no compensation (daman diyat) will be imposed for walking. Now necessarily, the ruling of death by falling will be attributed to the shart. But because it is a shart and in principle shart does not incur liability, we considered both aspects and said: if he dug the well in his own property, considering it as a shart, no liability is imposed; or if the falling person intentionally fell, then also no liability. But if he dug the well in non-owned (public) land, we will make the shart stand in place of the 'illah and impose liability, because the shart does not oppose the 'illah, since the 'illah is not suitable and the shart is suitable for the ruling, and there is similarity between shart and 'illah because existence is attached to shart just as existence is attached to 'illah. Therefore, by making the shart stand in place of the 'illah, we rule that the digger is liable for life and property. But note that only liability for the property (daman mahal) is imposed, i.e., blood money is obligatory, not the liability of direct killing (i.e., expiation), nor is he deprived of inheritance if the deceased was his relative, because the well-digger is not the direct killer. And when the 'illah is suitable, the shart does not take the ruling of 'illah. That is why we said that if witnesses of shart and yamin (oath) all retract after the judgment, the liability is on the witnesses of the yamin because they are the witnesses of the 'illah. Similarly, when 'illah and sabab combine, the ruling of sabab drops, like witnesses of takhyir (option) and ikhtiyar (choice) in divorce and manumission: if they combine then later retract after judgment, the liability is on the witnesses of ikhtiyar because it is the 'illah and takhyir is the sabab. On this basis we said that if the guardian (wali) and the digger (hafir) dispute, and the digger says "he (the victim) threw himself," then the digger's word is accepted by istihsan because he adheres to what is original, which is the suitability of the 'illah for the ruling, and he denies the substitution of the shart. Unlike if the injurer (jarh) claims death from another cause, he is not believed because he is the one with the 'illah. Translation: And in any case, when the 'illah is suitable for the ruling, the shart will not be in the ruling of the 'illah. For this reason we said that when witnesses of shart and yamin (oath) all retract after the judge's decision, the liability is on the witnesses of the yamin (i.e., half the dower) because they are the witnesses of the 'illah. Similarly, when 'illah and sabab combine, the ruling of sabab drops, like witnesses of takhyir and ikhtiyar in divorce and manumission: if they combine then retract after the ruling, the liability is on the witnesses of ikhtiyar because ikhtiyar is the 'illah and takhyir is the sabab. On this basis we said that when the guardian and the digger dispute, and the digger says that he (the victim) threw himself, the digger's word is accepted by istihsan because he argues from what is original, i.e., the suitability of the 'illah for the ruling, and he denies the substitution of the shart. Unlike if the injurer claims death from another cause, he is not believed because he is the one with the 'illah. Summary: When shart and 'illah combine and the 'illah is suitable for the ruling, the shart does not take the ruling of 'illah; rather the ruling is attributed to the 'illah. For example, witnesses testified before the judge that Khalid divorced his wife by saying, "If you enter the house, you are divorced" — these are witnesses of yamin because the suspended oath is without Allah. Then two witnesses testify to the occurrence of the shart (that the wife entered the house) — these are called witnesses of shart. Then the judge pronounces the divorce.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul commentary explaining the category of shart (condition) among the muta'alliqat al-ahkam (things related to rulings). The author begins by defining shart: in language it means a sign, but in legal terminology it is that to which the existence (wujud) of a ruling is attributed, not its obligation (wujub). This distinguishes shart from sabab (cause), 'alamah (sign), and 'illah (effective cause). Using the example of a suspended divorce (ta'liq), the author illustrates that the condition (entry into the house) triggers the existence of the divorce, but the obligation of the divorce is from the words of the husband, not from the condition. This is the first type of shart — pure shart. The second type is where the shart takes the place of an 'illah. The example given is digging a well in a path: the digging is a shart (removing the preventer), walking to the well is a sabab, and the weight of the falling person is the 'illah. Since the 'illah (weight) is natural and not a transgression, the ruling cannot be attributed to it; similarly the sabab (walking) is permissible. Therefore, the ruling is attributed to the shart, but only if the digging is in non-owned land and the victim did not intentionally fall. In such case, by istihsan, the shart is treated like an 'illah to impose liability (daman diyat). However, the digger is not considered a direct killer, so no expiation or inheritance deprivation. The passage then discusses cases where 'illah is suitable: then shart does not override 'illah. Examples from testimony: witnesses of yamin (oath) are considered 'illah, witnesses of shart (condition) are just condition; if they retract, liability is on the 'illah witnesses. Similarly, in divorce by option, the witnesses of ikhtiyar (choice) are 'illah, witnesses of takhyir (giving option) are sabab; upon retraction, liability on the 'illah witnesses. Finally, a dispute between guardian and digger: the digger's claim that the victim threw himself is accepted by istihsan, because he relies on the original rule that 'illah is suitable, and he denies the substitution of shart. Unlike a direct injurer claiming death from another cause, he is not believed because he is the 'illah-holder.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition upon which the existence of a ruling depends, but not its obligation; it is a category of muta'alliqat al-ahkam.
علة ('illah): The effective cause that necessitates a ruling; in the text, it is that to which the obligation of a ruling is attributed, as opposed to shart which only brings existence.
سبب (sabab): A cause that brings about the ruling, but unlike 'illah, it is a basis for the ruling's existence without necessarily being the primary obligator.
مانع (mani'): A preventer that blocks the action of a cause; removing it is considered a shart.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable result.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the key difference between shart (condition) and 'illah (effective cause) in Hanafi usul?
A) Shart is a type of 'illah, but weaker.
B) Shart is that to which the existence of a ruling is attributed, while 'illah is that to which the obligation of a ruling is attributed.
C) 'Illah is a condition for the validity of an act, while shart is a condition for its obligation.
D) There is no difference; they are synonyms.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, shart triggers a ruling's existence, not its obligation; when the normal 'illah is unsuitable, shart can step in by istihsan to impose liability, but only under specific conditions.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
