Understanding 'Alama as a Sign in Hanafi Usul
Defining 'alama as a condition that indicates a ruling without being its cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'alama (sign) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and distinguish it from sabab (cause) by analyzing the example of ihsan in zina.

Core Idea
'Alama indicates a ruling without causing it — like ihsan for stoning.

In usul al-fiqh, terms like 'cause' and 'condition' are precisely defined. The Hanafi school draws a key distinction between sabab (cause), which directly necessitates a ruling, and 'alama (sign), which merely indicates. This passage introduces 'alama using the example of ihsan (marital status) in the law of zina to illustrate how a sign modifies a ruling without causing it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the Arabic phrase 'fa-mā yu'rafu al-wujūd min ghayri an yata'allaqa bihi wujūb wa lā wujūd' and translate it precisely. Note that it defines 'alama as something that makes existence (of a ruling) known without being attached to obligation or existence itself.
The definition emphasizes a lack of causal connection.
2
Distinguish from sabab
Contrast 'alama with sabab: a sabab is a cause that directly produces the ruling (e.g., the sighting of the moon for fasting). An 'alama is only an indicator.
In Hanafi usul, this distinction is crucial for deriving rulings correctly.
3
Relate 'alama to shart
The text says ‘alama is sometimes called a condition (shart). Understand that both 'alama and shart are prerequisites, but a shart is often necessary for the ruling to apply, while an 'alama signals the ruling's existence without being its cause.
4
Analyze the example of ihsan
Ihsan (being muhsan) is presented as an 'alama in the chapter of zina. When zina occurs, if the person is muhsan, the punishment is stoning; otherwise, it is lashing. Ihsan indicates which punishment applies but does not cause the punishment — the act does.
This example clarifies the practical function of an 'alama.
5
Note the incomplete text
The original passage ends mid-sentence. Recognize that a full understanding may require continuation, but the core concept is clear.
Always check for completeness in source texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْعَلَامَةُ فَمَا يُعْرَفُ الْوُجُودَ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَتَعَلَّقَ بِهِ وُجُوبْ وَلَا وُجُودٌ وَقَدْ يُسَمَّى الْعَلَامَةُ شَرْطًا وَذَلِكَ مَثَلُ الْإِحْصَانِ فِي بَابِ الزِّنَا فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا ثَبَتَ كَانَ مُعَرِّفًا لِحُكْمِ الزِّنَا فَأَمَّا أَنْ يُوجَدَ الزِّنَا بِصُورَتِهِ وَيَتَوَقَّفُ إِنْعِقَادُهُ عِلَّةً عَلَى
As for the sign (alama), it is that by which existence is known without it being attached to any obligation or existence. And the sign is sometimes called a condition. An example is ihsan (marital status) in the chapter of zina: when it is established, it makes the ruling of zina known. But as for the occurrence of zina in its form, and its becoming a cause (for the ruling) depends on...
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage introduces the term 'alama (sign) in usul al-fiqh, which is a type of shart (condition) that indicates the existence of a ruling without being its actual cause. The example given is ihsan (being married or previously married) in the law of zina. Ihsan is a sign: if a person is muhsan (married), then when zina occurs, the punishment changes from lashing to stoning. But ihsan itself is not the cause of the punishment; it merely indicates the appropriate ruling. The cause is the act of zina itself. The text begins to explain that for the act of zina to be effective as a cause, it depends on something else, but the passage is cut off. In Hanafi usul, the distinction between 'alama and sabab is important: a sabab is directly connected to the ruling, while an 'alama is a sign that merely indicates a certain attribute relevant to the ruling.

Key Terms
العلامة (al-‘alāma): A sign that indicates existence (of a ruling) without being attached to obligation or existence itself; often called a condition.
الإحصان (al-iḥṣān): Marital status of being muhsan (a free married Muslim who has consummated marriage); it acts as a sign in zina cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the definition of 'alama, what does it indicate?
A) Existence without attachment to obligation or existence
B) The obligation of an act
C) The existence of a cause
D) The non-existence of a ruling

Key Takeaway
An 'alama is a sign that indicates a ruling without being its cause; it functions as a condition that modifies the ruling.

Distinguishing Condition from Cause: The Birdcage Case
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for opening a cage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a condition (shart) and a cause (sabab/illah) in Hanafi usul and apply the distinction to determine liability in cases involving an intervening free agent.

Core Idea
A condition removes an impediment; a cause generates liability. Acts of free agents are causes, not conditions.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi dispute: if someone opens a birdcage and the bird flies away, is the opener liable? The answer hinges on whether opening the cage is a condition (shart) or a cause (sabab). The case highlights the principle that the intervening act of a free agent is the true cause, and a condition alone does not generate liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is opening a birdcage causing the bird to fly away. The dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say no liability; Imam Muhammad says liability.
2
Understand the principle: shart vs sabab
A condition (shart) removes an impediment but does not cause the act; a cause (sabab) directly leads to the ruling. The bird's act of flying is the cause; opening the cage is a condition because it removes the impediment (the cage door).
Thus the condition is in the meaning of a cause (fi ma'na al-sabab) but not a true cause.
3
Analyze the reasoning of the two shaykhs
They argue that the bird is a free agent; its act is voluntary and not necessitated by opening the door. Therefore, liability falls on the bird's act, not on the condition.
The bird's flying is a free act; the opener's condition does not change that.
4
Analyze Imam Muhammad's reasoning
He argues that the bird's act is not truly free; it arises from the opening of the door. Thus the opening is in the meaning of a cause, making the opener liable.
This view treats the condition as having causal force because the bird's act is triggered by it.
5
Apply to a similar case: falling into a well
The text asks: if someone digs a well and another person falls in, is the digger liable? The answer depends on whether the faller had choice. If the faller deliberately jumped, the digger is not liable; otherwise, the well is a cause.
This extends the principle: a free agent's willful act supersedes the condition.

قال ابوحنيفة وابويوسف :- اسی مذکورہ اصول پر اگر کسی نے پرندے کے پنجرہ کا دروازہ کھول دیا جس کی وجہ سے پرندہ اڑ گیا، توشیخین کے نزدیک دروازہ کھولنے والا پرندے کی قیمت کا ضامن نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ پ کا دروازہ کھولنا شرط ہے اس لیے کہ یہ پرندے اڑنے سے مانع تھا، اور ازالہ مانع کا نام شرط ہے ،مگر یہ شرط علت پر یعنی پرندے کے فعل پر مقدم ہے، لہذا اس شرط میں سبب کے معنی ہوں گے ، اور اس شرط میں علت کے معنی نہیں ہیں، کیونکہ علت یعنی پرندہ کا اڑنا اس شرط سے یعنی دروازہ کھولنے سے پیدا نہیں ہوا، کیونکہ دروازہ کھولنے سے پرندہ کا اڑنا ضروری نہیں ہے، لہذا جب شرط فی معنی السبب ہے نہ کہ فی معنی العلت تو پرندہ کے تلف ہونے کا حکم اس شرط کی طرف سوب نہ ہو گا یعنی دروازہ کھولنے والا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔

وُجُودِ الْإِحْصَانِ فَلَا وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يَضْمَنُ شُهُودُ الإِحْصَانِ إِذَا رَجَعُو بِحَالٍ - ترجمہ: اور بہر حال علامت پس وہ ہے جو وجود کی پہچان کرائے بغیر اس کے کہ اس کے ساتھ وجود یا وجوب متعلق ہو ، اور بھی علامت کا نام رکھا جاتا ہے شرط ، اور وہ جیسے باب زنا میں احسان ہے، اس لئے کہ احسان جب ثابت ہو جائے تو وہ حکم زنا کا معترف ہوگا، پس بہر حال یہ بات کہ زنا اپنی صورت سے پایا جائے اور اس کا علت بن کر منعقد ہونا احصان کے وجود پر موقوف رہے پس ایسا نہیں ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے شہو دا حصان کسی بھی حال میں ضامن نہ ہوں گے جب وہ شہادت سے رجوع کرلیں۔
تشریح :- متعلقات احکام شرع کی چوتھی قسم علامت ہے، علامت کے لغوی معنی نشان کے ہیں، جیسے سڑک پر کلومیٹر کا بورڈ مقدار مسافت کی علامت ہے، شریعت کی اصطلاح میں علامت اس کو کہتے ہیں جو حکم کے وجود کی پہچان کرائے ،لیکن اس کے ساتھ حکم کا وجود یا وجوب متعلق نہ ہو، جیسے تکبیرات صلوۃ انتقال کی علامات ہیں، اذان نماز کا وقت داخل ہونے کی علامت ہے۔ اور کبھی علامت کو مجاز اشرط بھی کہہ دیا جاتا ہے جیسے باب زنا میں احصان ہے،(احصان کہتے ہیں مسلمان ہونا اور شادی شدہ ہونا ) یہ احصان زانی کے مستحق رجم ہونے کی علامت ہے ، احصان شرط نہیں ہے، کیونکہ پہلے آپ پڑھ چکے ہو کہ شرط علت کے بعد آتی ہے اور یہاں احصان بعد زنا آئے تو اس احصان کی وجہ سے رجم ثابت نہ ہوگا، بلکہ احصان قبل زنا سے رجم ثابت ہوگا، یہ دلیل ہے اس بات کی کہ احصان شرط نہیں ہے، بالفاظ دیگر اگر احصان شرط ہوتا تو زنا کے موجود ہونے کے باوجود اس کا علت رجم ہونا احصان پر موقوف رہے گا جب احسان پایا جائے گا تو ز نارجم کی علت بنے گا ، حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ احصان اگر زنا کے بعد پیدا ہوا تو اس سے رجم ثابت نہیں ہوگا معلوم ہوا کہ احصان شرط نہیں ہے، نیز احصان سبب بھی نہیں ہے، کیونکہ احسان کسی بھی درجہ میں مفضی الی الحکم نہیں ہے، اور علت بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کی طرف رجم یعنی حکم کا وجوب منسوب نہیں ہے، اب صرف علامت بچا تو احصان علامت ہوگا۔۔اسی اصول کی بنا پر کہ احصان صرف علامت ہے اگر شہود احصان اپنی شہادت سے رجوع کر لیں تو دیتِ مرجوم کے ضامن نہ ہوں گے، چاہے وہ تنہار جوع کریں یا شہو ر زنا کے ساتھ رجوع کریں،مثلاً چار گواہوں نے زنا کی گواہی دی، پھر دوسرے گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ وہ زانی محصن ہے، پھر اس کو رجم کیا گیا ، بعد میں شہو دِاحصان نے رجوع کر لیا تو ان پر دیت کا ضمان نہ آئے گا، کیونکہ شہود زنا بمنزلہ علت ہیں، اور شہود احصان بمنزلہ علامت ہیں، اور شرط کے اندر تو کسی نہ کسی درجہ میں اس کی اہلیت ہے کہ اس کو علت کا خلیفہ قرار دیا جائے مگر شہو دا حصان تو علامت
The Fays al-Hijazi 335 - Urdu commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami: Releasing an animal is a pure cause (sabab), not a condition (shart), because releasing the animal does not remove an impediment, since the animal was not tied. So how is opening a cage compared to sending? Except that they are answering that this analogy is only in non-liability, i.e., just as the one who opens the cage is not liable, similarly the one who sends is not liable, because in both there is an intervening act of a free agent which is the cause. And when a sound, strong cause exists, the ruling is not attributed to the cause or condition. In short, although they are different—one is a cause and one is a condition—they are equal in non-liability. Bird: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said: According to this mentioned principle, if someone opened the door of a bird's cage causing the bird to fly away, then according to the two shaykhs the one who opened the door is not liable for the bird's value, because opening the door is a condition, since it was preventing the bird from flying, and removing an impediment is called a condition. But this condition precedes the cause, i.e., the bird's act. Therefore this condition is in the meaning of a cause, and not in the meaning of a cause, because the cause—the bird's flying—did not arise from this condition (opening the door), since opening the door does not necessitate the bird's flying. Hence when the condition is in the meaning of a cause and not in the meaning of a cause, the ruling of the bird's destruction is not attributed to this condition, i.e., the one who opened the door is not liable. But a question arises: then falling into a well is also an act of a free agent that did not arise from the condition (digging the well), and digging the well does not have the meaning of a cause, so the digger should not be liable. The answer is that the one who falls is a free agent but he has no choice in falling; if his choice is established and it is proven that he deliberately threw himself, then the digger is not liable. And Imam Muhammad says that the one who opened the door is liable, because the bird's act is not the act of a free agent; rather it arose from the condition (opening the door). So this condition is in the meaning of a cause, so the one who opened the door is liable. And as for the sign (al-alamah), it is that which makes known existence without obligation or existence being attached to it. Sometimes the sign is called a condition, and that is like ihsan in the chapter of zina, for when it (ihsan) is established, it makes known the ruling of zina. But it is not the case that zina exists in its form and its being a cause is contingent upon the existence of ihsan. Therefore witnesses of ihsan are not liable if they retract in any case. Commentary: The fourth category of the attachments of legal rulings is the sign (alamah). In language, alamah means mark, like a kilometer board on a road indicating distance. In shari'ah terminology, alamah is that which makes known the existence of a ruling without the existence or obligation of the ruling being attached to it, like the takbirs of prayer are signs of transition; the adhan is a sign of the entry of prayer time. And sometimes alamah is metaphorically called shart, like ihsan in the chapter of zina (ihsan means being Muslim and married). This ihsan is a sign of the being deserving of stoning. It is not a condition, because you have already read that the condition comes after the cause, and if ihsan comes after zina, then stoning would not be established due to that ihsan. Rather, stoning is established by ihsan before zina. This is proof that ihsan is not a condition. In other words, if ihsan were a condition, then despite the occurrence of zina, its being a cause for stoning would depend on ihsan; when ihsan exists, then zina becomes a cause for stoning. But this is not so, because if ihsan occurs after zina, stoning is not established. Thus it is known that ihsan is not a condition, nor is it a cause (sabab), because ihsan does not lead to the ruling in any degree, nor is it a cause (illah), because the obligation of the ruling (stoning) is not attributed to it. Now only the sign remains, so ihsan is a sign. Based on this principle that ihsan is only a sign, if witnesses of ihsan retract their testimony, they will not be liable for the blood money of the stoned person, whether they retract alone or with the witnesses of zina. For example, four witnesses testified to zina, then other witnesses testified that the adulterer was muhsan, then he was stoned; later the witnesses of ihsan retracted—they are not liable for blood money, because witnesses of zina are like a cause, and witnesses of ihsan are like a sign. As for a condition, to some degree it has the capacity to be considered a deputy of the cause, but witnesses of ihsan are a sign.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary (Sharh al-Husami) covers two main topics: (1) the distinction between 'condition' (shart) and 'cause' (sabab/illah) using the example of opening a birdcage, and (2) the definition of 'sign' (alamah) as the fourth category of legal attributes (after cause, condition, and preventer). The author first discusses a previous point: releasing an animal is a pure cause, not a condition, because it does not remove an impediment. He then presents a dispute: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if someone opens a birdcage and the bird flies away, the opener is not liable because the bird's act (flying) is the direct cause, and the opening is merely a condition that removes the impediment but does not cause the act. Imam Muhammad disagrees, holding the opener liable because the bird's act is not a free choice but arises from the opening. These rulings are based on the principle that liability attaches to the effective cause (illah), not to conditions or signs. The passage then defines 'alamah: it indicates the existence of a ruling without being attached to the ruling's existence or obligation. For example, ihsan (being Muslim and married) in zina cases is a sign that the adulterer deserves stoning, not a condition or cause. This distinction has practical fiqh effects: witnesses of ihsan who retract are not liable for blood money, unlike witnesses of zina (who are like a cause). The commentary emphasizes that ihsan is not a condition because it can occur after zina without establishing stoning, and it is not a cause because the ruling is not attributed to it.

Key Terms
الشرط (al-shart): A condition that removes an impediment and is in the meaning of a cause (sabab) but is not the direct cause of the ruling; it precedes the cause.
السبب (al-sabab): A pure cause that directly leads to the ruling without any intervening free agent's act being the cause.
العلة (al-illah): The effective cause that generates the ruling, often the act of a free agent.
الفاعل المختار (al-fa'il al-mukhtar): A free agent capable of choice; his act is considered the illah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), why is the opener of the birdcage not liable for the bird's loss?
A) Because the opener lacked intent.
B) Because the bird's act is a free act and the true cause; opening the cage is only a condition.
C) Because the bird is considered property of the opener.
D) Because the cage door was not locked.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a condition (shart) removes an impediment; it does not generate liability when a free agent's act intervenes as the cause.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Definition of 'Alamah (Sign) and Its Distinction from Shart
Definition of the fourth category of legal attributes: 'alamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'alamah (sign) in Hanafi legal theory, distinguish it from shart (condition), and apply the distinction to the example of ihsan in zina cases.

Core Idea
A sign indicates a ruling's existence without being attached to its occurrence; it is not a condition or cause.

Having distinguished cause and condition, we now turn to the fourth category of legal attributes: the sign ('alamah). This lesson defines 'alamah and clarifies its difference from shart, using the example of ihsan (being Muslim and married) in zina cases. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining liability and the effect of retracting testimony.

Guided Path
1
Define 'alamah in Hanafi usul
The text defines 'alamah as something that makes known the existence of a ruling without the existence or obligation of the ruling being attached to it.
It is a descriptive indicator, not a causative factor.
2
Contrast 'alamah with shart and sabab
Unlike a condition, a sign does not affect the validity of the cause. Unlike a cause, a sign does not generate the ruling. It simply points to the ruling's applicability.
Example: The takbirs in prayer are signs of transition (e.g., from standing to bowing).
3
Apply to the example of ihsan in zina
Ihsan (being Muslim and married) is a sign that an adulterer is subject to stoning. It is not a condition because stoning is not contingent on ihsan occurring after zina; it is not a cause because the ruling is not attributed to ihsan.
Ihsan before zina indicates that the punishment includes stoning; after zina it does not.
4
Derive the practical consequence for witnesses
Because ihsan is only a sign, witnesses of ihsan who retract are not liable for blood money (diyah) of the stoned person. This is unlike witnesses of zina (who are like a cause) who may be liable if they retract.
The sign does not create the ruling, so retracting it does not affect the ruling's basis.
5
Reinforce via analogy: kilometer board on a road
The text gives a simple analogy: a kilometer board indicates distance but does not cause the distance or condition it. Similarly, 'alamah indicates the ruling without being attached to it.
This clarifies the purely indicative function.

الگ الگ ہیں ایک سبب اور ایک شرط ہے مگر عدم وجوب ضمان میں دونوں برابر ہیں۔

قال ابوحنيفة وابويوسف :- اسی مذکورہ اصول پر اگر کسی نے پرندے کے پنجرہ کا دروازہ کھول دیا جس کی وجہ سے پرندہ اڑ گیا، توشیخین کے نزدیک دروازہ کھولنے والا پرندے کی قیمت کا ضامن نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ پ کا دروازہ کھولنا شرط ہے اس لیے کہ یہ پرندے اڑنے سے مانع تھا، اور ازالہ مانع کا نام شرط ہے ،مگر یہ شرط علت پر یعنی پرندے کے فعل پر مقدم ہے، لہذا اس شرط میں سبب کے معنی ہوں گے ، اور اس شرط میں علت کے معنی نہیں ہیں، کیونکہ علت یعنی پرندہ کا اڑنا اس شرط سے یعنی دروازہ کھولنے سے پیدا نہیں ہوا، کیونکہ دروازہ کھولنے سے پرندہ کا اڑنا ضروری نہیں ہے، لہذا جب شرط فی معنی السبب ہے نہ کہ فی معنی العلت تو پرندہ کے تلف ہونے کا حکم اس شرط کی طرف سوب نہ ہو گا یعنی دروازہ کھولنے والا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔
لیکن سوال یہ پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ پھر کنویں میں گرنا بھی فاعل مختار کا فعل ہے جو شرط سے یعنی کنواں کھودنے سے پیدا
نہیں ہوا، اور کنواں کھودنے میں علت کے معنی بھی نہیں تو کھودنے والے پر ضمان نہ آنا چاہیے۔ اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ گرنے والا ہے تو فاعل مختار مگر گرنے میں اس کا اختیار نہیں ہے ، ہاں اگر گر نے میں اس کا اختیار ثابت ہو جائے اور یہ بات ثابت ہو جائے کہ اس نے جان بوجھ کر اپنے آپ کو گرایا ہے تو پھر حاضر پر
ضمان نہ ہو گا۔
اور امام محمدعلی فرماتے ہیں کہ دروازہ کھولنے والے پر ضمان آئے گا، کیونکہ پرندہ کا فعل فاعل مختار کا فعل نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ شرط یعنی دروازہ کھولنے سے پیدا ہوا ہے، لہذا یہ شرط فی معنی العلہ ہوگی تو دروازہ کھولنے والے پر ضمان آئے گا۔
وَأَمَّا الْعَلَامَةُ فَمَا يُعَرَفُ الْوُجُوْدَ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَتَعَلَّقَ بِهِ وُجُوبْ وَلَا وَجُودٌ وَقَدْ يُسمى الْعَلَامَةُ شَرْطَا وَذَلِكَ مَثَلُ الْإِحْصَانِ فِي بَابِ الزَّنَا فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا ثَبَتَ كَانَ مُعَرِفًا لِحُكْمِ الزِّنَا فَاَمَا أَنْ يُوْجَدَ الزَّنَا بِصُورَتِهِ وَيَتَوَقَّفُ إِنْعِقَادُهُ عِلَّةً عَلَى
الفيضُ الحجازي
۳۳۶
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
وُجُودِ الْإِحْصَانِ فَلَا وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يَضْمَنُ شُهُودُ الإِحْصَانِ إِذَا رَجَعُو بِحَالٍ - ترجمہ: اور بہر حال علامت پس وہ ہے جو وجود کی پہچان کرائے بغیر اس کے کہ اس کے ساتھ وجود یا وجوب متعلق ہو ، اور بھی علامت کا نام رکھا جاتا ہے شرط ، اور وہ جیسے باب زنا میں احسان ہے، اس لئے کہ احسان جب ثابت ہو جائے تو وہ حکم زنا کا معترف ہوگا، پس بہر حال یہ بات کہ زنا اپنی صورت سے پایا جائے اور اس کا علت بن کر منعقد ہونا احصان کے وجود پر موقوف رہے پس ایسا نہیں ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے شہو دا حصان کسی بھی حال میں ضامن نہ ہوں گے جب وہ شہادت سے رجوع کرلیں۔
تشریح :- متعلقات احکام شرع کی چوتھی قسم علامت ہے، علامت کے لغوی معنی نشان کے ہیں، جیسے سڑک پر کلومیٹر کا بورڈ مقدار مسافت کی علامت ہے، شریعت کی اصطلاح میں علامت اس کو کہتے ہیں جو حکم کے وجود کی پہچان کرائے ،لیکن اس کے ساتھ حکم کا وجود یا وجوب متعلق نہ ہو، جیسے تکبیرات صلوۃ انتقال کی علامات ہیں، اذان نماز کا وقت داخل ہونے کی علامت ہے۔ اور کبھی علامت کو مجاز اشرط بھی کہہ دیا جاتا ہے جیسے باب زنا میں احصان ہے،(احصان کہتے ہیں مسلمان ہونا اور شادی شدہ ہونا ) یہ احصان زانی کے مستحق رجم ہونے کی علامت ہے ، احصان شرط نہیں ہے، کیونکہ پہلے آپ پڑھ چکے ہو کہ شرط علت کے بعد آتی ہے اور یہاں احصان بعد زنا آئے تو اس احصان کی وجہ سے رجم ثابت نہ ہوگا، بلکہ احصان قبل زنا سے رجم ثابت ہوگا، یہ دلیل ہے اس بات کی کہ احصان شرط نہیں ہے، بالفاظ دیگر اگر احصان شرط ہوتا تو زنا کے موجود ہونے کے باوجود اس کا علت رجم ہونا احصان پر موقوف رہے گا جب احسان پایا جائے گا تو ز نارجم کی علت بنے گا ، حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ احصان اگر زنا کے بعد پیدا ہوا تو اس سے رجم ثابت نہیں ہوگا معلوم ہوا کہ احصان شرط نہیں ہے، نیز احصان سبب بھی نہیں ہے، کیونکہ احسان کسی بھی درجہ میں مفضی الی الحکم نہیں ہے، اور علت بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کی طرف رجم یعنی حکم کا وجوب منسوب نہیں ہے، اب صرف علامت بچا تو احصان علامت ہوگا۔۔اسی اصول کی بنا پر کہ احصان صرف علامت ہے اگر شہود احصان اپنی شہادت سے رجوع کر لیں تو دیتِ مرجوم کے ضامن نہ ہوں گے، چاہے وہ تنہار جوع کریں یا شہو ر زنا کے ساتھ رجوع کریں،مثلاً چار گواہوں نے زنا کی گواہی دی، پھر دوسرے گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ وہ زانی محصن ہے، پھر اس کو رجم کیا گیا ، بعد میں شہو دِاحصان نے رجوع کر لیا تو ان پر دیت کا ضمان نہ آئے گا، کیونکہ شہود زنا بمنزلہ علت ہیں، اور شہود احصان بمنزلہ علامت ہیں، اور شرط کے اندر تو کسی نہ کسی درجہ میں اس کی اہلیت ہے کہ اس کو علت کا خلیفہ قرار دیا جائے مگر شہو دا حصان تو علامت
The Fays al-Hijazi 335 - Urdu commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami: Releasing an animal is a pure cause (sabab), not a condition (shart), because releasing the animal does not remove an impediment, since the animal was not tied. So how is opening a cage compared to sending? Except that they are answering that this analogy is only in non-liability, i.e., just as the one who opens the cage is not liable, similarly the one who sends is not liable, because in both there is an intervening act of a free agent which is the cause. And when a sound, strong cause exists, the ruling is not attributed to the cause or condition. In short, although they are different—one is a cause and one is a condition—they are equal in non-liability. Bird: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said: According to this mentioned principle, if someone opened the door of a bird's cage causing the bird to fly away, then according to the two shaykhs the one who opened the door is not liable for the bird's value, because opening the door is a condition, since it was preventing the bird from flying, and removing an impediment is called a condition. But this condition precedes the cause, i.e., the bird's act. Therefore this condition is in the meaning of a cause, and not in the meaning of a cause, because the cause—the bird's flying—did not arise from this condition (opening the door), since opening the door does not necessitate the bird's flying. Hence when the condition is in the meaning of a cause and not in the meaning of a cause, the ruling of the bird's destruction is not attributed to this condition, i.e., the one who opened the door is not liable. But a question arises: then falling into a well is also an act of a free agent that did not arise from the condition (digging the well), and digging the well does not have the meaning of a cause, so the digger should not be liable. The answer is that the one who falls is a free agent but he has no choice in falling; if his choice is established and it is proven that he deliberately threw himself, then the digger is not liable. And Imam Muhammad says that the one who opened the door is liable, because the bird's act is not the act of a free agent; rather it arose from the condition (opening the door). So this condition is in the meaning of a cause, so the one who opened the door is liable. And as for the sign (al-alamah), it is that which makes known existence without obligation or existence being attached to it. Sometimes the sign is called a condition, and that is like ihsan in the chapter of zina, for when it (ihsan) is established, it makes known the ruling of zina. But it is not the case that zina exists in its form and its being a cause is contingent upon the existence of ihsan. Therefore witnesses of ihsan are not liable if they retract in any case. Commentary: The fourth category of the attachments of legal rulings is the sign (alamah). In language, alamah means mark, like a kilometer board on a road indicating distance. In shari'ah terminology, alamah is that which makes known the existence of a ruling without the existence or obligation of the ruling being attached to it, like the takbirs of prayer are signs of transition; the adhan is a sign of the entry of prayer time. And sometimes alamah is metaphorically called shart, like ihsan in the chapter of zina (ihsan means being Muslim and married). This ihsan is a sign of the being deserving of stoning. It is not a condition, because you have already read that the condition comes after the cause, and if ihsan comes after zina, then stoning would not be established due to that ihsan. Rather, stoning is established by ihsan before zina. This is proof that ihsan is not a condition. In other words, if ihsan were a condition, then despite the occurrence of zina, its being a cause for stoning would depend on ihsan; when ihsan exists, then zina becomes a cause for stoning. But this is not so, because if ihsan occurs after zina, stoning is not established. Thus it is known that ihsan is not a condition, nor is it a cause (sabab), because ihsan does not lead to the ruling in any degree, nor is it a cause (illah), because the obligation of the ruling (stoning) is not attributed to it. Now only the sign remains, so ihsan is a sign. Based on this principle that ihsan is only a sign, if witnesses of ihsan retract their testimony, they will not be liable for the blood money of the stoned person, whether they retract alone or with the witnesses of zina. For example, four witnesses testified to zina, then other witnesses testified that the adulterer was muhsan, then he was stoned; later the witnesses of ihsan retracted—they are not liable for blood money, because witnesses of zina are like a cause, and witnesses of ihsan are like a sign. As for a condition, to some degree it has the capacity to be considered a deputy of the cause, but witnesses of ihsan are a sign.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary (Sharh al-Husami) covers two main topics: (1) the distinction between 'condition' (shart) and 'cause' (sabab/illah) using the example of opening a birdcage, and (2) the definition of 'sign' (alamah) as the fourth category of legal attributes (after cause, condition, and preventer). The author first discusses a previous point: releasing an animal is a pure cause, not a condition, because it does not remove an impediment. He then presents a dispute: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if someone opens a birdcage and the bird flies away, the opener is not liable because the bird's act (flying) is the direct cause, and the opening is merely a condition that removes the impediment but does not cause the act. Imam Muhammad disagrees, holding the opener liable because the bird's act is not a free choice but arises from the opening. These rulings are based on the principle that liability attaches to the effective cause (illah), not to conditions or signs. The passage then defines 'alamah: it indicates the existence of a ruling without being attached to the ruling's existence or obligation. For example, ihsan (being Muslim and married) in zina cases is a sign that the adulterer deserves stoning, not a condition or cause. This distinction has practical fiqh effects: witnesses of ihsan who retract are not liable for blood money, unlike witnesses of zina (who are like a cause). The commentary emphasizes that ihsan is not a condition because it can occur after zina without establishing stoning, and it is not a cause because the ruling is not attributed to it.

Key Terms
العلامة (al-alamah): A sign that indicates the existence of a ruling without the ruling's existence or obligation being attached to it.
الشرط (al-shart): A condition; in this context, a condition that affects the ruling's existence, unlike a sign.
الإحصان (al-ihsan): Being Muslim and married; a sign that a zani is subject to stoning, not a condition or cause.
السبب (al-sabab): A cause; something that directly leads to the ruling.
العلة (al-illah): The effective cause that generates the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is ihsan not considered a condition for stoning?
A) Because ihsan always occurs before zina.
B) Because if ihsan occurs after zina, stoning is still established.
C) Because stoning is established based on ihsan before zina, not after, and ihsan does not affect the cause of the ruling.
D) Because ihsan is a cause, not a condition.

Key Takeaway
A sign ('alamah) indicates a ruling without conditioning or causing it; ihsan is a sign of stoning liability, not a condition or cause.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
beginner
6 min
Four Types of Ignorance in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Classifies four types of ignorance as legal impediments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of ignorance (jahl) as classified in Hanafi usul and determine which types are valid excuses in the Hereafter and which affect worldly rulings.

Core Idea
Not all ignorance excuses — deliberate denial or opposition to clear proof is never a valid excuse.

In this passage, the Hanafi usuli author classifies ignorance (jahl) as one of the acquired impediments (al-awāriḍ al-muktasabah). Understanding these categories is crucial for a jurist to evaluate when ignorance can mitigate liability (e.g., for a new Muslim) and when it cannot (e.g., for a deliberate denier). The passage describes three invalid types and implies a fourth (valid) type, though only the invalid ones are detailed.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish voluntary vs. involuntary ignorance
Recognize that Hanafi usul treats voluntary ignorance (after clear proof) as blameworthy, while involuntary ignorance may excuse. This passage lists only the blameworthy types.
Valid ignorance is not listed but is understood by contrast.
2
Identify the first type: kufr (disbelief)
This is obstinate denial after clear evidence. It is never a valid excuse in the Hereafter or in worldly rulings.
It is the worst category.
3
Identify the second type: ignorant desire (hawā) and rebellion (baghy)
This includes ignorance of divine attributes or afterlife rulings due to following desires, and the ignorance of the rebel who opposes clear evidence while claiming Qur'anic interpretation. Still invalid in the Hereafter, but because they are Muslims, they must be debated and held liable for damages in worldly matters.
Less severe than kufr but still not excused.
4
Identify the third type: ijtihād contrary to clear nass
A mujtahid who contradicts the Qur'an or widely-known Sunnah, or relies on a rare hadith, is in error. His fatwa is rejected and not an excuse.
Examples: selling ummahāt al-awlād, etc.
5
Infer the fourth type: valid ignorance
By implication, there is a type of ignorance that does excuse (e.g., a new convert unaware of rulings). This type is not detailed because it is not blameworthy.
This classification helps us apply the maxim: 'al-umūr bi-maqāṣidihā' — intention matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ فِي الْعَوَارِضِ الْمُكْتَسَبَةِ أَمَّا الْجَهْلُ فَأَنْوَاعُ أَرْبَعَةٍ: جَهْلٌ بَاطِلٌ بِلَا شُبْهَةٍ وَهُوَ الْكُفْرُ، وَإِنَّهُ لَا يَصْلَحُ عُذْرًا فِي الْآخِرَةِ أَصْلًا لِأَنَّهُ مُكَابَرَةٌ وَجُحُودٌ بَعْدَ وُضُوحِ الدَّلِيلِ. وَجَهْلٌ هُوَ دُونَهُ لَكِنَّهُ بَاطِلٌ لَا يَصْلَحُ عُذْرًا فِي الْآخِرَةِ أَيْضًا، وَهُوَ جَهْلُ صَاحِبِ الْهَوَى فِي صِفَاتِ اللهِ تَعَالَى وَفِي أَحْكَامِ الْآخِرَةِ، وَجَهْلُ الْبَاغِي لِأَنَّهُ مُخَالِفٌ لِلدَّلِيلِ الْوَاضِحِ الَّذِي لَا شُبْهَةَ فِيهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ مُتَأَوِّلٌ بِالْقُرْآنِ فَكَانَ دُونَ الْأَوَّلِ، لَكِنَّهُ لَمَّا كَانَ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ أَوْ مِمَّنْ يَنْتَحِلُ الْإِسْلَامَ لَزِمَنَا مُنَاظَرَتُهُ وَإِلْزَامُهُ، فَلَمْ نَعْمَلْ بِتَأْوِيلِهِ الْفَاسِدِ، وَقُلْنَا إِنَّ الْبَاغِيَ إِذَا أَتْلَفَ مَالَ الْعَادِلِ أَوْ نَفْسَهُ وَلَا مَنْعَةَ لَهُ يَضْمَنُ، وَكَذَلِكَ سَائِرُ الْأَحْكَامِ تَلْزَمُهُ. وَكَذَلِكَ جَهْلُ مَنْ خَالَفَ فِي اجْتِهَادِهِ الْكِتَابَ أَوِ السُّنَّةَ الْمَشْهُورَةَ مِنْ عُلَمَاءِ الشَّرِيعَةِ أَوْ عَمِلَ بِغَرِيبٍ مِنَ السُّنَّةِ عَلَى خِلَافِ الْكِتَابِ أَوِ السُّنَّةِ الْمَشْهُورَةِ مَرْدُودٌ بَاطِلٌ لَيْسَ بِعُذْرٍ أَصْلًا، مِثْلُ الْفَتْوَى بِبَيْعِ أُمَّهَاتِ الْأَوْلَادِ وَحِلِّ مَتْرُوكِ التَّسْمِيَةِ عَامِدًا وَالْقِصَاصِ بِالْقَسَامَةِ وَالْقَضَاءِ بِشَاهِدٍ وَيَمِينٍ.
Section on Acquired Impediments: As for ignorance, it has four types: (1) A false ignorance without any ambiguity, and it is disbelief, and it is not a valid excuse in the Hereafter at all because it is obstinacy and denial after the evidence is clear. (2) An ignorance that is below this but still false, not a valid excuse in the Hereafter either. It is the ignorance of the follower of desire concerning the attributes of Allah Almighty and the rulings of the Hereafter, and the ignorance of the rebel (al-bāghī), because he opposes the clear evidence that has no ambiguity, except that he interprets the Qur'an, so it is below the first. However, since he is among the Muslims or among those who claim Islam, we must debate him and refute him, and we do not act upon his corrupt interpretation. We say: If the rebel destroys the property of the just person or kills him, and he has no protective force, he is liable; similarly, all rulings are binding upon him. (3) Similarly, the ignorance of one who, in his ijtihād, opposes the Book or the widely-known Sunnah among the scholars of the Shariah, or acts upon a rare hadith contrary to the Book or the widely-known Sunnah, is rejected, false, and not an excuse at all. Examples include giving a fatwa permitting the sale of ummahāt al-awlād (mothers of children), deeming that which is intentionally left without mentioning the name of Allah to be lawful, retribution via qasāmah, and judgment based on one witness and an oath.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is a classification of ignorance (jahl) as one of the acquired impediments (al-awāriḍ al-muktasabah) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author distinguishes four categories of ignorance based on their legal effect, particularly whether they serve as an excuse in the Hereafter or affect worldly legal rulings. The first type is the ignorance of the disbeliever (kufr), which is a deliberate denial after clear evidence; it is never a valid excuse. The second type includes ignorance of those who follow desires regarding divine attributes and afterlife rulings, as well as the ignorance of the rebel (bāghī) who opposes clear evidence but claims to interpret the Qur'an. Although this is less severe than disbelief, it is still not a valid excuse in the Hereafter, but because they are Muslims, scholars must engage in debate and refute their false interpretations. In worldly matters, such rebels are liable for damages if they act without protective force. The third type is the ignorance of a mujtahid who contradicts explicit texts of the Qur'an or the widely-known Sunnah, or relies on a rare hadith contrary to those primary sources; this is rejected and not an excuse. The fourth type is implicit: valid ignorance that may excuse; however, this passage only lists the invalid types. Common examples of invalid fatwas based on such ignorance include the permissibility of selling ummahāt al-awlād (enslaved mothers of children born to slave owners), deeming meat intentionally not slaughtered with the name of Allah as lawful, using qasāmah (collective oaths) for retribution, and accepting a single witness with an oath. These examples illustrate rulings that contradict established clear evidence.

Key Terms
الْجَهْلُ (al-jahl): Ignorance, the lack of knowledge that may serve as an excuse if it is involuntary and unavoidable; but here classified into blameworthy types.
الْبَاغِي (al-bāghī): A rebel against the just Imam; one who opposes the clear evidence with a false interpretation.
الْقَسَامَةُ (al-qasāmah): A collective oath taken by the community when a corpse is found, used to establish liability or retribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of the third type of ignorance (ijtihād contrary to clear nass)?
A) A disbeliever who denies the Prophet (ﷺ).
B) A rebel who interprets the Qur'an against clear evidence.
C) A fatwa permitting the sale of ummahāt al-awlād based on a rare hadith.
D) A new Muslim who eats pork unknowingly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of ignorance into three blameworthy types (kufr, desire/rebellion, and ijtihād error) helps jurists determine when ignorance excuses and when it does not, both in the Hereafter and in worldly rulings.

The Binding Effect of Jest (Hazl) in Marriage, Divorce, and Oath
States the rule on hazl in nikah, talaq, yamin with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hadith 'Three things are serious in seriousness and jest' to identify hazl in nikah, talaq, and yamin as legally binding, and derive the ruling using Hanafi usul principles.

Core Idea
Jest in marriage, divorce, and oath is legally binding because the hadith explicitly treats it as serious.

This lesson examines a foundational Hanafi usul rule: certain contracts and actions are so consequential that jest is treated as seriousness. The proof is a hadith listing marriage, divorce, and oath. We will analyze how this hadith serves as a dalil naqli, classify its textual category, and derive the ruling that jest in these matters is effective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue and the three contracts
The text discusses the effect of jest (hazl) in nikah, talaq, and yamin (oath). Note that these are distinct from sale, where jest may invalidate the contract.
2
Locate the dalil (hadith)
The passage quotes the hadith: 'ثلاث جدهن جد وهزلهن جد النكاح والطلاق واليمين'. This is a dalil naqli from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
Hadith ahad, zanni al-thubut, qati al-dalala.
3
Classify the text (usul analysis)
The hadith is an explicit statement (nass) that covers three types. It is 'amm' (general) in that it applies to all instances of these three contracts. Hanafi principle: al-amm yufidu al-wujub? Here it establishes binding effect.
The hadith is not a command, but a declaration of legal reality.
4
Derive the ruling for hazl in each contract
Based on the hadith, hazl in marriage and divorce results in a valid binding contract; hazl in oath (yamin) activates the obligation. The reasoning: the jester chooses the cause, and the ruling cannot be postponed.
Contrast with sale: hazl in sale may make the contract fasid or batil.
5
Note the scope: these contracts do not admit khiyar al-shart
The passage explains that these contracts do not allow the option of rescission (khiyar al-shart) because their rulings are immediate and certain.
This sets up the later dispute on khul'.

أبي حَنِيفَةَ الله فَإِنَّ الطَّلَاقَ يَتَوَقَفْ عَلَى اخْتِيَارِهَا بِكُلِّ حَالِ لِأَنَّهُ بِمَنْزلَةِ خِيَار الشَّرْطِ وَقَدْ نُضَ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ اللّه فِي خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ مِنْ جَانِبِهَا أَنَّ الطَّلَاقَ لا يَقَعُ وَلَا يَجِبْ الْمَالُ إِلَّا أَنْ تَشَاءَ الْمَرْأَةُ فَيَقَعُ الطَّلَاقُ وَيَجِبُ الْمَالُ فَكَذَلِكَ هُهُنَا لَكِنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُقَدَرِ بِالثَّلْثِ وَكَذَلِكَ هَذَا فِي نَظَائِرِهِ - ترجمہ:۔ اور یہ (بیع) نکاح کے برخلاف ہے، چنانچہ بالا جماع اقل واجب ہوگا ، اس لئے کہ نکاح شرط فاسد سے فاسد نہیں ہوتا ہے، پس دونوں موافقتوں پر عمل کرنا ممکن ہو گا، اور اگر دونوں نے نکاح میں دنا نیر کو ذکر کیا، اور ان کی غرض دراہم ہے، تو مہر مثل واجب ہوگا، اس لئے کہ نکاح بغیر تسمیہ کے درست ہے، برخلاف بیع کے ، اور اگر دونوں نے اصل نکاح کے بارے میں مذاق کیا، تو ہنرل باطل ہے اور عقد لازم ہے، اور اسی طرح طلاق، عتاق اور قصاص کو معاف کرنا ، اور یمین ( تعلیق ) اور نذر ہے، آپ علیہ السلام کے ارشاد کی وجہ سے کہ تین چیزیں ایسی ہیں کہ ان کی سنجید گی بھی سنجیدگی ہے اور ان کا مذاق بھی سنجیدگی ہے، نکاح اور طلاق اور یمین ، اور اس لئے کہ مذاق کرنے والا سبب کو اختیار کرنے والا ہے، سبب پر راضی ہے نہ کہ اس کے حکم پر ، اور ان اسباب کا حکم رد اور تراخی کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا ہے، کیا تو نہیں دیکھتا که یہ ( یعنی ان میں سے کوئی بھی ) خیار شرط کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا ہے۔ اور بہر حال وہ عقد جس میں مال مقصود ہو، جیسے خلع ، عشق، علی المال ، اور صلح عن دم العمد ، پس امام محمد نے مبسوط کی کتاب الاکراہ میں ضلع کے بارے میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ، اور مال لازم ہوگا ، اور یہ حکم صاحبین کے نزدیک ہے، اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک ضلع خیار شرط کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا ہے ، خواہ وہ اصل عقد کے بارے میں مذاق کریں، یا بدل ضلع کی مقدار کے بارے میں، یا بدل ضلع کی جنس کے بارے میں ، تو صاحبین کے نزدیک مسمی واجب ہوگا، اور یہ بدل خلع اس چیز کے مانند ہو گیا جو نسخ کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا ہے تابع ہونے کی وجہ سے ، بہر حال امام ابوحنیفہ اللہ کے نزدیک پس طلاق عورت کے اختیار پر موقوف رہے گی ہر حال میں ، اس لئے کہ ہنرل خیار شرط کے درجہ میں ہے، اور (جامع صغیر میں ) عورت کی جانب سے خیار شرط کے بارے میں امام ابو حنیفہ عالیہ سے بصراحت مروی ہے کہ طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی، اور مال واجب نہ ہوگا، مگر یہ کہ عورت چاہے، تو طلاق واقع ہوگی اور مال واجب ہوگا، پس اسی طرح یہاں لیکن یہ خیار تین دن کے ساتھ مقدر نہیں ہے، اور اسی طرح یہ حکم و اختلاف ہے اس کے نظائر میں ۔
Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him): Indeed, divorce is dependent on her choice in every case because it is like khiyar al-shart. And it has been narrated from Abu Hanifa regarding khiyar al-shart from her side that divorce does not occur and the wealth is not obligatory unless the woman wishes, then divorce occurs and wealth is obligatory. So likewise here, but it is not restricted to three days, and similarly this in its parallels. Translation: And this (sale) is contrary to marriage, so when they agree on the lesser, the lesser is obligatory, because marriage is not invalidated by a void condition. So both agreements can be acted upon. And if both mentioned [dananir?] in marriage, and their intention is dirhams, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory, because marriage is valid without specification, unlike sale. And if both jest regarding the original marriage, then the jest is void and the contract is binding. Similarly, divorce, emancipation, forgiveness of qisas, and oath (ta'liq) and nadhr, because of his saying (peace be upon him): Three things are serious in seriousness and jest: marriage, divorce, and oath. And because the jester chooses the cause, is satisfied with the cause, not its ruling, and the ruling of these causes cannot be postponed or delayed. Do you not see that these do not admit khiyar al-shart? And in any case, a contract in which wealth is intended, like khul', 'ushr? 'ala al-mal, and sulh 'an dam al-'amd, then Imam Muhammad mentioned in Kitab al-Ikrah in al-Mabsut regarding [dla'] that divorce will occur and wealth will be obligatory, and this ruling is according to the Sahibayn, because according to them [dla'] does not admit khiyar al-shart, whether they jest about the original contract, or about the amount of the substitute, or about the type of the substitute. So according to the Sahibayn the specified (musamma) is obligatory, and this substitute for khul' becomes like something that cannot be annulled due to being subsidiary. However, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, divorce remains dependent on the woman's choice in every case, because it is at the level of khiyar al-shart. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir it is explicitly narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa concerning khiyar al-shart from the woman's side that divorce does not occur and wealth is not obligatory unless the woman wishes, then divorce occurs and wealth is obligatory. So likewise here, but this khiyar is not restricted to three days, and similarly this ruling and disagreement in its parallels.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is a combined ruling and dispute exposition. It first addresses the distinction between bay' (sale) and nikah (marriage) regarding hazl (jest) in the mahr. In nikah, if both parties jest about the mahr amount, the lesser (the serious one) is obligatory because marriage is not invalidated by a void condition—both agreements (serious and jest) can be accommodated. If they jest about the type of mahr (e.g., mention dananir but intend dirhams), then mahr al-mithl is obligatory because the specific mahr was not agreed upon, and nikah is valid without specification. In contrast, in bay', jest about the price invalidates the contract. For the original contract (e.g., saying 'I marry you in jest'), the jest is void and the contract is binding. This applies similarly to divorce, emancipation, forgiveness of qisas, suspended oaths, and vows, based on the hadith: 'Three things are serious in seriousness and jest: marriage, divorce, and oath.' The reasoning is that the jester chooses the cause (e.g., the words of divorce) and is satisfied with it, but not with the ruling; however, these causes do not admit postponement or delay, and do not accept khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation). Then the passage shifts to contracts where wealth is intended, such as khul', and reports a disagreement. According to Imam Muhammad (and the Sahibayn), in khul' under duress (ikrah), divorce occurs and the specified substitute is obligatory, because such contracts do not admit khiyar al-shart. But Imam Abu Hanifa holds that divorce only occurs if the woman chooses, analogizing it to khiyar al-shart, where the woman's choice is decisive. This khiyar, however, is not limited to three days. This difference extends to similar cases.

Key Terms
هزل (hazl): Jest or joke made seriously; in legal contexts, words spoken in jest that are treated as binding in certain contracts.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option to rescind a contract within a stipulated period (usually three days).
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife for compensation paid to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the hadith, which three contracts are binding even if made in jest?
A) Sale, marriage, divorce
B) Marriage, divorce, oath
C) Divorce, oath, emancipation
D) Marriage, sale, oath

Key Takeaway
Jest in marriage, divorce, and oath is legally binding due to the explicit hadith; the jester's intent does not nullify the ruling.

The Khiyar al-Shart Dispute in Khul': Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-shart in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on khiyar al-shart in khul' contracts, identify the underlying qiyas, and evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa treats khul' like khiyar al-shart; Sahibayn reject the analogy, making talaq immediate.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether khul' (divorce initiated by the wife for compensation) admits khiyar al-shart (option to stipulate). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the woman's choice is analogous to khiyar al-shart, so talaq is suspended on her acceptance. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that khul' does not admit such an option because it is a contract of exchange. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply qiyas and identify the scope of khiyar al-shart.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and the parties
The dispute is about the effect of khiyar al-shart in khul' contracts. Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn. Both are Hanafi.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa: Talaq in khul' is suspended on the woman's choice, analogous to khiyar al-shart from her side. If she does not wish, talaq does not occur and the substitute is not owed.
Analogy (qiyas) to khiyar al-shart.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Sahibayn: Khul' does not admit khiyar al-shart because it is a subsidiary contract of exchange. Therefore, talaq occurs immediately and the specified substitute is obligatory, even under duress.
They argue that the substitute is like an irrevocable payment.
4
Analyze the qiyas argument
Abu Hanifa analogizes the woman's choice in khul' to a buyer's khiyar al-shart. Sahibayn reject this because khul' is a form of divorce, not a sale, and the substitute is not subject to rescission.
The illa (effective cause) is the woman's consent; Abu Hanifa says it is similar to a stipulation, Sahibayn say it is not.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In a coerced khul', according to Abu Hanifa, if the woman does not choose to accept, talaq does not occur. According to Sahibayn, talaq occurs immediately and the substitute is owed.
This affects the validity of forced divorces.

'ala al-mal, and sulh 'an dam al-'amd, then Imam Muhammad mentioned in Kitab al-Ikrah in al-Mabsut regarding [dla'] that divorce will occur and wealth will be obligatory, and this ruling is according to the Sahibayn, because according to them [dla'] does not admit khiyar al-shart, whether they jest about the original contract, or about the amount of the substitute, or about the type of the substitute. So according to the Sahibayn the specified (musamma) is obligatory, and this substitute for khul' becomes like something that cannot be annulled due to being subsidiary. However, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, divorce remains dependent on the woman's choice in every case, because it is at the level of khiyar al-shart. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir it is explicitly narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa concerning khiyar al-shart from the woman's side that divorce does not occur and wealth is not obligatory unless the woman wishes, then divorce occurs and wealth is obligatory. So likewise here, but this khiyar is not restricted to three days, and similarly this ruling and disagreement in its parallels.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is a combined ruling and dispute exposition. It first addresses the distinction between bay' (sale) and nikah (marriage) regarding hazl (jest) in the mahr. In nikah, if both parties jest about the mahr amount, the lesser (the serious one) is obligatory because marriage is not invalidated by a void condition—both agreements (serious and jest) can be accommodated. If they jest about the type of mahr (e.g., mention dananir but intend dirhams), then mahr al-mithl is obligatory because the specific mahr was not agreed upon, and nikah is valid without specification. In contrast, in bay', jest about the price invalidates the contract. For the original contract (e.g., saying 'I marry you in jest'), the jest is void and the contract is binding. This applies similarly to divorce, emancipation, forgiveness of qisas, suspended oaths, and vows, based on the hadith: 'Three things are serious in seriousness and jest: marriage, divorce, and oath.' The reasoning is that the jester chooses the cause (e.g., the words of divorce) and is satisfied with it, but not with the ruling; however, these causes do not admit postponement or delay, and do not accept khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation). Then the passage shifts to contracts where wealth is intended, such as khul', and reports a disagreement. According to Imam Muhammad (and the Sahibayn), in khul' under duress (ikrah), divorce occurs and the specified substitute is obligatory, because such contracts do not admit khiyar al-shart. But Imam Abu Hanifa holds that divorce only occurs if the woman chooses, analogizing it to khiyar al-shart, where the woman's choice is decisive. This khiyar, however, is not limited to three days. This difference extends to similar cases.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife for compensation paid to the husband.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option to rescind a contract within a stipulated period (usually three days).
صاحبان (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why does khul' not admit khiyar al-shart?
A) Because khul' is a form of divorce, not a sale.
B) Because the substitute in khul' is like an irrevocable payment.
C) Because the woman's consent is not required.
D) Because the three-day limit is not applicable.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over khiyar al-shart in khul' hinges on whether the woman's choice is analogous to an option in sale; the practical consequence affects coerced divorces.

The Usul Rule: Marriage Survives Void Conditions — Differentiating Bay' from Nikah in Hazl
Usul rule expansion: hazl in mahr amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that a void condition invalidates a sale but not a marriage, and derive the ruling on mahr amount when jest is involved.

Core Idea
Marriage survives voids that destroy a sale — a key usul divergence.

This passage expands on a critical usul distinction: while a void condition (shart fasid) renders a sale fasid (invalid), marriage remains valid. This difference yields divergent rulings when parties jest about the mahr amount. Understanding this distinction sharpens your ability to apply qiyas and identify the correct illa across contract types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contracts involved
Recognize that the author compares bay' (sale) and nikah (marriage) in the context of hazl (jest) regarding the mahr amount.
2
State the ruling for each contract
In marriage, only the serious amount is mahr; in sale, the jested amount becomes binding according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn hold both are the same.
3
Extract the illa (effective cause) for the difference
The illa is that marriage is not invalidated by a void condition, whereas sale is.
4
Construct the qiyas
Asl (sale with void condition) → hukm: fasid; Far' (marriage with void condition) → hukm: sahih with adjusted mahr. Illa: presence of void condition, but the effect differs due to contract nature.
5
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn analogize marriage to sale, so they rule that the jested amount is binding in both. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes.

شریح : ۔ مصنف عالی فرماتے ہیں کہ بیچ کا مسئلہ جو ماقبل میں مذکور ہوا، وہ مسئلہ نکاح کے برخلاف ہے، چنانچہ نکاح میں اگر عاقدین نے مقدار مہر میں ہزل کیا کہ مہر ایک ہزار ہی ہو گا مگر ہم لوگوں کے سامنے دو ہزار کہیں گے ، تو یہاں امام صاحب اور صاحبین سب کے نزدیک اقل مہر یعنی ایک ہزار واجب ہوگا، دو ہزار واجب نہ ہوگا ، صاحبین کے نزدیک تو بیع اور نکاح کا مسئلہ ایک ہی ہے البتہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک بیچ اور نکاح دیا جائے تو دوسرے ایک ہزار کو قبول کرنے کی شرط فاسد ہوگی ، اور شرط فاسد سے بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے، اور نکاح شرط فاسد سے فاسد نہیں ہوتا ہے، لہذا دو ہزار جس کا دونوں نے ہنرل کیا ہے باطل نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ یہاں موافقت فی الجد یعنی ایک ہزار پر نکاح ہونا اور موافقت فی البزل یعنی دو ہزار کو صرف مذا قأذکر کرنا دونوں جمع ہو سکتے ہیں، لہذا دو ہزار میں ایک ہزار تو سنجیدگی سے کہا ہے، وہ مہر بنے گا ، اور دوسرا ایک ہزار جو مذاقا کہا ہے وہ واجب نہ ہوگا، تو یہ مثال ہوئی مقدار مہر میں ہنرل کی ، اور اگر میاں بیوی نے جنس مہر میں ہنرل کیا جیسے اصل مہر تو دو ہزار درہم ہیں مگر لوگوں کے سامنے انہوں نے دو ہزار دینار کا ذکر کیا، اب اگر دونوں ہنرل پر برقرار ہوں، یا خالی الذھن ہوں، یا ہنرل میں دونوں کا اختلاف ہو جائے تو ان سب صورتوں میں مہر مثل واجب ہوتا ہے، کیونکہ جو چیز اصل مہر ہے اس کا نکاح میں ذکر ہی نہیں آیا تو گویا بغیر مہر کے نکاح ہوا، اور ایسی صورت میں مہر مثل واجب ہوتا ہے، اور اگر ہنرل سے اعراض پر دونوں کا اتفاق ہو جائے تو مسمی واجب ہوگا، برخلاف بیع کے، کیونکہ بیع بغیر شمن کے صحیح ہی نہیں ہوتی ہے، بلکہ بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے، پس جنس ثمن میں ہنرل پر موافقت اور اصل بیچ میں جد پر موافقت دونوں میں تطبیق نہیں ہوسکتی ہے، کیونکہ ہنرل کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ وہ ثمن نہ ہو اور اصل بیع میں جد کا تقاضا ہے کہ وہ شمن ہو، تو تعارض ہو گیا، لہذا بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی، اور نکاح میں دونوں موافقتوں میں تطبیق ممکن ہے جیسا کہ او پر مذکور ہوا۔ ولو هذلا باصل النكاح :- اور اگر میاں بیوی نے اصل نکاح میں ہنرل کیا ، اس طور پر کہ مرد نے عورت سے کہا کہ میں مذا قالوگوں کے سامنے نکاح کرونگا، اور اصل میں ہمارے درمیان نکاح نہیں ہوگا ، پھر یہ دونوں خواہ ہنرزل و مذاق پر متفق ہوں، یا مذاق کو نظر انداز کرنے پر متفق ہوں، یا ہنرل و مذاق ہونے میں دونوں کا اختلاف ہو جائے ، یا دونوں عقد کے وقت ہنرل سے خالی الذھن ہوں بہر صورت عقد لازم ہو جائے گا، اور ہنرل کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا، یہی حکم طلاق کا بھی ہے، کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ میں مذاقاً تجھے طلاق دونگا، اور حقیقت میں طلاق نہ ہوگی ، اسی طرح مولی نے غلام کو کہا میں تجھے مذاقاً آزاد کرونگا، حقیقت میں آزادی نہ ہوگی۔ اسی طرح قاتل سے مقتول کے ولی نے قصاص کو مذاقاً معاف کر دیا ، یا یمین پر ہنرل کیا، یمین سے مراد تعلیق ہے۔ یعنی بیوی سے کہا کہ میں مذاق میں تجھے تعلیقاً طلاق دونگا، یا غلام سے کہا کہ میں مذاقاً تیری آزادی کو معلق کرونگا، یامدا قا نذر مانی تو ان تمام صورتوں میں عقد لازم ہو جائے گا یعنی طلاق ، عتاق واقع ہوگا ، قصاص معاف ہوگا، قسم اور نذر واقع ہو جائے گی ، اور
Explanation: The author says: The issue of sale mentioned previously is contrary to marriage. In marriage, if the contracting parties jest about the amount of mahr, saying 'the mahr is one thousand but we will say two thousand in front of people,' then here according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, the lesser mahr (one thousand) is obligatory, not two thousand. According to the Sahibayn, the issue in sale and marriage is the same; however, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, there is a difference: in sale, in the case of jest, two thousand is obligatory as the price, but in marriage, in the case of jest, one thousand is obligatory. The reason for the difference is that in sale, if two thousand is not set as the price, but one thousand is set as the price, then accepting the other thousand becomes a void condition, and a void condition invalidates the sale. But marriage is not invalidated by a void condition. Therefore, the two thousand which they jested about is not (automatically) binding, because here the agreement in seriousness (i.e., marriage on one thousand) and the agreement in jest (i.e., mentioning two thousand) can be combined. So from the two thousand, the one thousand said seriously becomes the mahr, and the other one thousand said in jest is not obligatory. So this is an example of jest in the amount of mahr. If the spouses jest about the type of mahr, e.g., the actual mahr is two thousand dirhams, but they mention two thousand dinars in front of people: now if they persist in the jest, or are indifferent, or differ about the jest, then in all these cases mahr al-mithl is obligatory, because the thing that is the actual mahr was not mentioned in the marriage, so it is as if they married without specifying mahr, and in such a case mahr al-mithl is obligatory. But if they both agree to abandon the jest, then the specified (musamma) is obligatory, contrary to sale, because sale is not valid without a price, and becomes void. So in sale, agreement on jest in the type of price and agreement in seriousness on the original sale cannot be reconciled, because the jest requires that it not be the price, and the seriousness in the original sale requires that it be the price, so there is conflict, hence the sale becomes void. In marriage, reconciliation between the two agreements is possible, as mentioned above. And if they jest about the original marriage, e.g., the man says to the woman, 'I will marry you in jest in front of people, but actually there will be no marriage between us,' then in all cases—whether they agree on the jest, or agree to ignore it, or differ about it, or are indifferent at the time of the contract—in all cases the contract is binding and the jest is not considered. The same ruling applies to divorce: if someone says to his wife, 'I divorce you in jest, and actually there is no divorce,' similarly, a master says to his slave, 'I free you in jest, actually no freedom,' similarly, the guardian of the victim forgives qisas in jest, or one makes an oath in jest (where oath means suspension), e.g., says to his wife, 'I give you a suspended divorce in jest,' or to his slave, 'I suspend your freedom in jest,' or one makes a vow in jest—in all these cases, the contract is binding: divorce occurs, emancipation occurs, qisas is forgiven, and the oath and vow are effective.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the previous rulings, focusing on the distinction between bay' (sale) and nikah (marriage) in cases of hazl (jest) regarding mahr. The author clarifies that when both parties jest about the mahr amount, the agreed serious amount (the lesser) is binding. The Sahibayn treat sale and marriage identically in this respect, but Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes: in sale, the jested amount becomes the price because sale is invalidated by a void condition, whereas marriage is not. Thus, in sale, if they jest about a higher price, that higher price becomes binding. In marriage, only the serious lower amount is mahr. When jesting about the type of mahr (e.g., dirhams vs dinars), the result is mahr al-mithl (proper mahr) because the intended mahr was not specified; if they later agree to drop the jest, the specified mahr applies. In sale, jesting about the type invalidates the sale due to conflict. Lastly, jesting about the original contract itself (marriage, divorce, emancipation, etc.) is completely ineffective—the contract is binding regardless of intent, in line with the hadith. This shows a consistent principle: substantive contracts are not nullified by jest; only the specifics of consideration may be affected.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper mahr determined by the woman's family status, similar to mahr of her sisters, etc.
مسمی (musamma): The specifically agreed-upon mahr in the marriage contract.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is void and contrary to the contract's purpose, e.g., an additional payment not part of the price.
هزل (hazl): Jest, joking, or speaking without serious intent, especially in contracts.
بيع (bay'): Sale, a contract of exchange.
نكاح (nikah): Marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a couple jests about the mahr amount, saying it is 500 dirhams but publicly state 1000, what is the mahr?
A) 500 dirhams
B) 1000 dirhams
C) Mahr al-mithl
D) The contract is void

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul rule that marriage is not invalidated by void conditions causes a divergence from sale in hazl cases: only the serious portion of mahr binds.

The Principle of Irrelevance of Intent (Hazl) in Core Contracts: Nikah, Talaq, Itq, Qisas
Usul rule: hazl in core contracts is ineffective

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that hazl (jest) in the substance of core contracts (nikah, talaq, itq, etc.) is disregarded, and the contract is binding.

Core Idea
Jest in the contract itself is no defence — the ruling binds regardless of intent.

This passage extends the principle beyond mahr: if the parties jest about the very existence of the marriage contract, or about divorce, emancipation, forgiveness of qisas, oaths, or vows, the contract is fully binding. This reflects the usul rule that contracts of personal status are weighed by their outward expression, not inner intent, based on the hadith 'Three things are serious: marriage, divorce, and emancipation.'

Guided Path
1
List the contracts mentioned
Nikah, talaq, itq, qisas, yamin (oath), nadhr (vow).
2
State the common ruling
In all cases, jest does not affect validity; the contract is binding.
3
Identify the underlying principle
These contracts are based on lafz (utterance), not niyyah (intent) when it comes to validity.
4
Distinguish from the earlier hazl scenarios
Earlier, hazl affected the mahr amount/type but not the contract itself. Here, hazl aims at the contract itself, so the entire contract is binding.
5
Refer to the hadith
The hadith 'Three things are serious: marriage, divorce, and emancipation' grounds this rule.

بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے، پس جنس ثمن میں ہنرل پر موافقت اور اصل بیچ میں جد پر موافقت دونوں میں تطبیق نہیں ہوسکتی ہے، کیونکہ ہنرل کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ وہ ثمن نہ ہو اور اصل بیع میں جد کا تقاضا ہے کہ وہ شمن ہو، تو تعارض ہو گیا، لہذا بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی، اور نکاح میں دونوں موافقتوں میں تطبیق ممکن ہے جیسا کہ او پر مذکور ہوا۔ ولو هذلا باصل النكاح :- اور اگر میاں بیوی نے اصل نکاح میں ہنرل کیا ، اس طور پر کہ مرد نے عورت سے کہا کہ میں مذا قالوگوں کے سامنے نکاح کرونگا، اور اصل میں ہمارے درمیان نکاح نہیں ہوگا ، پھر یہ دونوں خواہ ہنرزل و مذاق پر متفق ہوں، یا مذاق کو نظر انداز کرنے پر متفق ہوں، یا ہنرل و مذاق ہونے میں دونوں کا اختلاف ہو جائے ، یا دونوں عقد کے وقت ہنرل سے خالی الذھن ہوں بہر صورت عقد لازم ہو جائے گا، اور ہنرل کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا، یہی حکم طلاق کا بھی ہے، کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ میں مذاقاً تجھے طلاق دونگا، اور حقیقت میں طلاق نہ ہوگی ، اسی طرح مولی نے غلام کو کہا میں تجھے مذاقاً آزاد کرونگا، حقیقت میں آزادی نہ ہوگی۔ اسی طرح قاتل سے مقتول کے ولی نے قصاص کو مذاقاً معاف کر دیا ، یا یمین پر ہنرل کیا، یمین سے مراد تعلیق ہے۔ یعنی بیوی سے کہا کہ میں مذاق میں تجھے تعلیقاً طلاق دونگا، یا غلام سے کہا کہ میں مذاقاً تیری آزادی کو معلق کرونگا، یامدا قا نذر مانی تو ان تمام صورتوں میں عقد لازم ہو جائے گا یعنی طلاق ، عتاق واقع ہوگا ، قصاص معاف ہوگا، قسم اور نذر واقع ہو جائے گی ، اور
Explanation: The author says: The issue of sale mentioned previously is contrary to marriage. In marriage, if the contracting parties jest about the amount of mahr, saying 'the mahr is one thousand but we will say two thousand in front of people,' then here according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, the lesser mahr (one thousand) is obligatory, not two thousand. According to the Sahibayn, the issue in sale and marriage is the same; however, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, there is a difference: in sale, in the case of jest, two thousand is obligatory as the price, but in marriage, in the case of jest, one thousand is obligatory. The reason for the difference is that in sale, if two thousand is not set as the price, but one thousand is set as the price, then accepting the other thousand becomes a void condition, and a void condition invalidates the sale. But marriage is not invalidated by a void condition. Therefore, the two thousand which they jested about is not (automatically) binding, because here the agreement in seriousness (i.e., marriage on one thousand) and the agreement in jest (i.e., mentioning two thousand) can be combined. So from the two thousand, the one thousand said seriously becomes the mahr, and the other one thousand said in jest is not obligatory. So this is an example of jest in the amount of mahr. If the spouses jest about the type of mahr, e.g., the actual mahr is two thousand dirhams, but they mention two thousand dinars in front of people: now if they persist in the jest, or are indifferent, or differ about the jest, then in all these cases mahr al-mithl is obligatory, because the thing that is the actual mahr was not mentioned in the marriage, so it is as if they married without specifying mahr, and in such a case mahr al-mithl is obligatory. But if they both agree to abandon the jest, then the specified (musamma) is obligatory, contrary to sale, because sale is not valid without a price, and becomes void. So in sale, agreement on jest in the type of price and agreement in seriousness on the original sale cannot be reconciled, because the jest requires that it not be the price, and the seriousness in the original sale requires that it be the price, so there is conflict, hence the sale becomes void. In marriage, reconciliation between the two agreements is possible, as mentioned above. And if they jest about the original marriage, e.g., the man says to the woman, 'I will marry you in jest in front of people, but actually there will be no marriage between us,' then in all cases—whether they agree on the jest, or agree to ignore it, or differ about it, or are indifferent at the time of the contract—in all cases the contract is binding and the jest is not considered. The same ruling applies to divorce: if someone says to his wife, 'I divorce you in jest, and actually there is no divorce,' similarly, a master says to his slave, 'I free you in jest, actually no freedom,' similarly, the guardian of the victim forgives qisas in jest, or one makes an oath in jest (where oath means suspension), e.g., says to his wife, 'I give you a suspended divorce in jest,' or to his slave, 'I suspend your freedom in jest,' or one makes a vow in jest—in all these cases, the contract is binding: divorce occurs, emancipation occurs, qisas is forgiven, and the oath and vow are effective.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the previous rulings, focusing on the distinction between bay' (sale) and nikah (marriage) in cases of hazl (jest) regarding mahr. The author clarifies that when both parties jest about the mahr amount, the agreed serious amount (the lesser) is binding. The Sahibayn treat sale and marriage identically in this respect, but Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes: in sale, the jested amount becomes the price because sale is invalidated by a void condition, whereas marriage is not. Thus, in sale, if they jest about a higher price, that higher price becomes binding. In marriage, only the serious lower amount is mahr. When jesting about the type of mahr (e.g., dirhams vs dinars), the result is mahr al-mithl (proper mahr) because the intended mahr was not specified; if they later agree to drop the jest, the specified mahr applies. In sale, jesting about the type invalidates the sale due to conflict. Lastly, jesting about the original contract itself (marriage, divorce, emancipation, etc.) is completely ineffective—the contract is binding regardless of intent, in line with the hadith. This shows a consistent principle: substantive contracts are not nullified by jest; only the specifics of consideration may be affected.

Key Terms
هزل (hazl): Jest, joking, or speaking without serious intent, especially in contracts.
طلاق (talaq): Divorce, the dissolution of marriage by the husband's pronouncement.
عتاق (itaq): Emancipation of a slave.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory justice in murder or injury cases.
يمين (yamin): Oath, often used to suspend a divorce or emancipation.
نذر (nadhr): A vow, a religious promise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master jests about freeing his slave, saying 'I free you' as a joke, is the slave freed?
A) Yes
B) No
C) Only if the slave takes it seriously
D) The master must pay compensation

Key Takeaway
In core contracts (marriage, divorce, emancipation, etc.), hazl is disregarded; the outward utterance is binding.

The Effect of Hazl (Jest) in Transactions: Agreement and Disagreement
Explanation of the rule of hazl in transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on hazl in transactions, distinguishing between cases where parties agree or disagree on intent.

Core Idea
In contracts, seriousness is presumed; hazl only takes effect when both parties agree on it.

This passage explains a key usul principle: the role of intention in contracts. While hazl (jest) can void transactions, its effect depends on the agreement of the parties. The Hanafi school, through Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, offers nuanced positions. Understanding this rule is essential for resolving disputes over contractual intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction type
Determine whether the transaction admits hazl (e.g., sale, hire, khul'). According to the text, hazl is effective in matters that admit annulment and where wealth is intended.
Hazl is not effective in all transactions; only those that can be annulled.
2
Assess party agreement
Check if both parties agree on hazl, both agree on seriousness, or differ. The ruling depends on this.
Parties may both claim hazl, both claim seriousness, or one claims hazl and the other seriousness.
3
Apply the Hanafi position
If both agree on hazl, it is effective and the transaction is void. If both agree on seriousness or differ, seriousness prevails according to Imam Abu Hanifa, making the transaction valid.
Imam Abu Hanifa's principle: default is seriousness.
4
Consider the Sahibayn position
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that hazl invalidates such transactions regardless of agreement. In their view, if there is hazl, the transaction is void.
This is a direct intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Note the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if parties differ, the contract is valid and obligations stand; according to Sahibayn, it is void and no obligations arise.
In cases of divorce and wealth, the consequences differ accordingly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصنف عاللہ ایک اصول بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ جن معاملات میں ہنرل مؤثر ہے یعنی وہ امور جو نقض کا احتمال رکھتے ہیں، جیسے بیج ، اور اجارہ ، اور امام صاحب کی اصل کے مطابق وہ معاملات جن میں مال مقصود ہوتا ہے جیسے خلع وغیرہ تو یہاں ہنرل کی موافقت پر اس وقت عمل واجب ہو گا جب دونوں عقد کرنے والے ہنرل پر بنا کرنے پر اتفاق کر لیں ، تو اب اس کو ہنرل ہی سمجھیں گے، اور اگر دونوں اس پر اتفاق کرلیں کہ عقد کے وقت دونوں خالی الذھن تھے یا ہنرل اور عدم ہنرل میں دونوں کا اختلاف ہو جائے کہ ایک ہنرل کا مدعی ہو اور دوسرا جذ کا تو جو جد کا مدعی ہے اس کے قول کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا، یہ حکم امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے، اور صاحبین اپنی اصل پر ہیں کہ ان کے نزدیک اس قسم میں ہنرل باطل ہے، جب ہنرل باطل ہے تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور مال واجب ہو جائے گا۔
The author, may Allah have mercy on him, is stating a principle: in those transactions in which hazl is effective, i.e., matters that admit annulment, like sale and hire, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa's principle, transactions in which wealth is intended, like khul' etc., then here acting in accordance with hazl will be obligatory when both contracting parties agree to base it on hazl. So then it will be considered hazl. And if both agree that at the time of contract they were empty-minded, or they differ on whether there was hazl or not – one claims hazl and the other claims seriousness (jidd) – then the one who claims seriousness, his statement will be given weight. This is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) are upon their own principle: according to them, hazl in this category invalidates [the transaction]. When hazl invalidates, then divorce will occur and wealth will be obligatory.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a key usul principle regarding the effect of jest (hazl) in legal transactions. The commentator is clarifying that in matters where hazl can be effective (i.e., transactions that can be annulled, such as sale, hire, and also those where the payment of wealth is the object, like khul'), if both parties agree that they were jesting, then the transaction is void. If they both claim they were serious or disagree, then the claim of seriousness is given precedence according to Imam Abu Hanifa. This is because the default in contracts is seriousness. The two companions (Sahibayn) hold that hazl invalidates such transactions, meaning if there is jest, the transaction is void, and if it is a divorce, it takes effect, and wealth becomes due. This difference arises from different usul positions on the effect of intention in contracts.

Key Terms
هزل (hazl): Jest, joking; speaking or acting in a manner not intended seriously.
جد (jidd): Seriousness, the opposite of hazl; the claim that an act was intended seriously.
خالی الذهن (khali al-dhihn): Empty-minded, i.e., not intending either jest or seriousness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling when two parties disagree on whether a sale was done in jest or seriousness?
A) The sale is void due to hazl.
B) The claim of jest is believed.
C) The claim of seriousness is believed.
D) The sale is suspended pending investigation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, hazl only affects transactions when both parties agree; otherwise, seriousness is presumed.
