The Waw: Absolute Conjunction in Hanafi Usul
Introduction to particles of meaning, focusing on the waw.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the waw, apply it to the examples of conditional triple divorce and manumission of two slaves, and identify the intra-madhhab dispute on the divorce example.

Core Idea
The waw simply joins items without sequence or simultaneity — order must come from outside the waw.

This passage from Al-Muntakhab al-Ḥusāmī introduces the final chapter on particles of meaning. The most frequent of these are conjunctions, and the primary conjunction is waw. Understanding the waw precisely is crucial because many fiqh rulings hinge on whether an action is immediate, sequential, or simultaneous. In this lesson, we will unpack the Hanafi definition and see it in action through two key cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the passage type and topic
This is a definition passage (usul definition) that states the linguistic rule governing the waw. Recognize that the author is setting out the Hanafi position on waw as a particle of meaning.
2
Extract the core definition of the waw
Locate the sentence: 'وَهِيَ لِمُطْلَقِ الْجَمْعِ عِنْدَنَا مِنْ غَيْرُ تَعَرُّضِ لِمُقَارَنَةٍ وَلَا تَرْتِيبٍ'. 'It is for absolute conjunction according to us, without implying simultaneity or order.' Understand that the waw simply collects items; any temporal relationship must be proven by external evidence.
Note: 'عندنا' signals this is the Hanafi position; most linguists and jurists agree.
3
Apply to the triple divorce example
Read the example: 'إِنْ نَكَحْتُهَا فَهِيَ طَالِقٌ وَطَالِقٌ وَطَالِقٌ'. Abu Hanifa says only one divorce occurs. Why? Because the waw does not create sequence; the second and third 'divorce' words are attached to the condition through the first divorce, not by the waw itself. So the condition triggers only the first divorce; the others are dependent on the first, not on the waw.
The disagreement with the two companions is due to their different understanding of the waw's implication (or lack thereof).
4
Apply to the manumission and marriage example
Now examine the second example: the master says 'أعتقت هذه وهذه' while an unauthorized agent had married both slave women to one man. The first emancipation is immediate and destroys the capacity for a suspended (موقوف) marriage; thus the marriage of the second woman becomes void before the second 'هذه' is even uttered. Again, the waw does not delay the first action; it merely joins two independent acts of manumission.
Key: 'صدر الكلام لا يتوقف على آخره' – the beginning does not depend on the end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالَّذِي يَقَعُ بِهِ خَتُمُ الْكِتَابِ بَابَ حُرُوفِ الْمَعَانِي فَشَطْرُ مِنْ مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَيْهَا وَاَكْثَرُهَا وَقُوْعًا حُرُوْفُ الْعَطْفِ وَالْاَصْلُ فِيْهِ الْوَاوَوَهِيَ لِمُطْلَقَ الْجَمْعِ عِنْدَنَا مِنْ غَيْرُ تَعَرُّضِ لِمُقَارَنَةٍ وَلَا تَرْتِيبٍ وَعَلَيْهِ عَامَةُ اَهْلِ اللُّغَةِ وَاَئِمَةُ الْفَتْوَى وَإِنَّمَا يَثْبُتُ التَّرْتِيبَ فِي قَوْلِهِ إِنْ موقوف نہیں ہوتا ہے جب کہ آخر کلام میں ایسی چیز نہ ہو جو اول کلام کو بدل دے، اور پہلی باندی کا آزاد ہونا نکاح موقوف کی محلیت کو باطل کر دیتا ہے، پس دوسری کا نکاح اس کے عشق کے تکلم سے پہلے ہی باطل ہو کلمات ظروف بھی ہیں، مگر چونکہ حروف زیادہ ہیں، اس لئے تغلیباً باب
And that with which the book ends is the chapter on particles of meaning. So a portion of fiqh issues is based on them, and the most frequent of them are conjunctions. And the original in conjunction is the waw, and it is, according to us, for absolute conjunction without implying simultaneity or order. And upon this are the majority of linguists and jurists. And order is established in the statement of a man (to a stranger woman): 'If I marry her, then she is divorced, and divorced, and divorced,' such that only one divorce occurs according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to his two companions, due to the necessity that the second divorce is attached to the condition via the first, not by the requirement of the waw. And in the statement of the master: 'I freed this and this,' when a unauthorized agent (faḍūlī) had married them both to a man, the marriage of the second is void because the beginning of the statement does not depend on its end when there is nothing in its end that changes its beginning, and the freeing of the first invalidates the capacity for the suspended (marriage) contract, so the second marriage becomes void before the utterance of 'I freed her' (regarding the second). Translation: And the chapter with which the book ends is the chapter on particles of meaning. So a portion of fiqh issues depends on them, and among those particles the most frequent are conjunctions. And the original in conjunction is the waw, and according to us the waw is for absolute conjunction without implying simultaneity or order. And that is the position of most linguists and jurists. And order is established in the statement of a man (to a stranger) that 'if I marry her, then she is divorced, and divorced, and divorced' such that only one divorce occurs according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to his two companions, because the second divorce is attached to the condition via the first, not by the requirement of the waw. And in the statement of the master 'I freed this and this,' when an unauthorized agent had married both of them to a man, the marriage of the second is void because the beginning of the statement does not depend on its end when there is nothing in its end that changes its beginning, and the freeing of the first invalidates the capacity for the suspended marriage, thus the second marriage became void before the utterance of her emancipation. Elaboration: The author concludes his book Al-Muntakhab al-Ḥusāmī with a discussion on particles of meaning, and he explains the reason: although the discussion of particles relates to grammar, because many fiqh issues are connected to particles, he made this discussion the conclusion of his book. Then among the particles, the most frequently used are conjunctions, so he first explained conjunctions. Particles include also conditional terms and adverbial terms, but because letters are more numerous, he used the principle of predominance [in naming the chapter].
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage introduces the final chapter of Al-Muntakhab al-Ḥusāmī, on 'particles of meaning' (ḥurūf al-maʿānī). These are words that connect or modify meanings in fiqh rulings. The most common are conjunctions (ḥurūf al-ʿaṭf), with the primary conjunction being wāw. According to the Hanafi school, the wāw indicates absolute conjunction (muṭlaq al-jamʿ), meaning it simply joins items without any implication of sequence (tartīb) or simultaneity (muqārana). This is the position of most linguists and jurists. The author then gives two fiqh examples that depend on this understanding. First, if a man says to a stranger (or in a conditional sentence): 'If I marry her, she is divorced, and divorced, and divorced' (i.e., three connected divorces). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, only one divorce occurs, not three, because the second and third divorces are linked to the condition through the first divorce, not by virtue of the waw. The waw itself does not create sequential effect; instead, the second divorce is triggered by the first, so only the first valid divorce occurs, and subsequent ones are dependent on it. This contradicts the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who would likely hold that three divorces occur due to the repeated wording. Second, if a master says 'I freed this and this' (two slave women), and an unauthorized agent (faḍūlī) had married both women to a man without permission. When the master frees them, the first woman's marriage becomes valid (since her owner ratified? Actually, the text says the first woman's emancipation invalidates the capacity for the suspended marriage, meaning the marriage of the second is void because the beginning of the statement (freeing the first) does not depend on the end; the first emancipation is immediate, and that destroys the possibility of her being a valid object for a suspended marriage (the marriage was suspended on the owner's ratification). Hence the second marriage is void even before the second 'this' is uttered. This shows the waw's function: the freeing of the first occurs instantly, without waiting for the second. The commentary (تشریح) explains why the author included this grammatical chapter: many fiqh rulings hinge on the correct understanding of these particles, even though they are primarily grammatical concepts.

Key Terms
حروف المعانی (ḥurūf al-maʿānī): Words (often particles) that modify meaning in a sentence, including conjunctions, prepositions, and conditionals.
واو عطف (wāw al-ʿaṭf): The conjunctive waw, indicating absolute conjunction without sequence or simultaneity.
مطلق الجمع (muṭlaq al-jamʿ): Absolute conjunction: joining items without any additional implication of order or simultaneity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, what does the waw (و) indicate in conjunction?
A) Sequential order (tartīb).
B) Simultaneous occurrence (muqārana).
C) Absolute conjunction without order or simultaneity.
D) Disjunction (takhīr).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the waw indicates absolute conjunction only; any sequence or simultaneity must be proven by external context, not by the waw itself.

Waw Joining Complete and Incomplete Sentences
Explains when waw joins complete vs incomplete sentences affecting participation in predicate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze a legal utterance containing waw to determine whether the second sentence shares the predicate of the first, based on whether the second sentence is complete or incomplete.

Core Idea
Waw joining two complete sentences keeps them independent; waw joining an incomplete sentence shares the predicate.

This lesson explores a subtle but critical rule in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the function of the conjunction waw when joining sentences in legal speech. Whether the second sentence is complete or incomplete determines if it shares the predicate of the first. This distinction has direct consequences for divorce pronouncements and other contractual language.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sentences joined by waw.
Locate the waw that connects two speech units. Each unit may be a single word or a full sentence. Determine if the second unit has its own predicate (is complete) or relies on the first's predicate (is incomplete).
In Arabic, a sentence is complete if it has both subject and predicate; incomplete if it lacks a predicate.
2
Classify the second sentence as complete or incomplete.
A complete sentence (jumla taammah) is fully meaningful on its own. An incomplete sentence (jumla naaqisah) needs the first sentence's predicate to be meaningful. For example, 'wa hadhihi' (and this one) without a predicate is incomplete.
The presence or absence of a predicate determines completeness.
3
Apply the rule: complete means no sharing; incomplete means sharing.
If the second sentence is complete, it does not share the first's predicate. If incomplete, it shares the predicate and the ruling applies equally to both.
This is the core Hanafi position on waw joining sentences.
4
Test the rule with the divorce example: 'This one is thrice divorced and this one is divorced'.
Both sentences are complete (each has its own predicate). The second does not share 'thrice', so only one divorce applies to the second. If the second were incomplete, it would share the predicate and get three divorces.
Contrast with 'This one is divorced and this one' (incomplete) where both get one.
5
Extend to conditional speech: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced'.
Here, the second 'divorced' is an incomplete sentence (no separate condition). It shares the condition of the first, so both divorces occur upon entry. This differs from 'Zayd and Amr came' where participation in a single act is impossible, requiring an implied separate verb.
The impossibility of sharing an act (like coming) forces an independent implied predicate.

Source Text

ترجمہ :۔ اور کبھی واؤ ایسے جملہ پر داخل ہوتا ہے جو اپنی خبر کے ساتھ مل کر تام ہے، پس خبر میں مشارکت ثابت نہیں ہوگی ، اور یہ جیسے قائل کا قول "هذه طالق ثلاثا وهذه طالق" تو دوسری پر ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی ، اس لئے کہ خبر میں شرکت کلام ثانی کے محتاج ہونے کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے، جب کہ کلام ثانی ناقص ہو، پس جب کلام ثانی کامل ہو تو شرکت کی دلیل ختم ہو گئی، اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ جملہ نا قصہ جملہ اولی کا اس چیز میں شریک ہوتا ہے جس سے بعینہ جملہ اولی تام ہوا ہے، حتی کہ ہم نے شوہر کے قول " ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق وطالق" میں کہا کہ طلاق ثانی بعینہ اس شرط کے ساتھ متعلق ہوگی، اور طلاق ثانی مستقل شرط کا تقاضہ نہ کرے گی ، گویا کہ متکلم نے شرط کا اعادہ کیا ہو، اور مستقل ہونے کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا قائل کے قول ” جاء نی زید و عمرو “ میں اس بات کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے کہ مجي واحد میں مشارکت ممکن نہیں ہے۔

تشریح:- واؤ جیسے عطف مفرد علی المفرد کے لیے آتا ہے ایسے ہی بھی واؤ کے ذریعہ جملہ کاملہ کا عطف جملہ کاملہ پر بھی کیا جاتا ہے، اور جب جملہ کاملہ کا عطف جملہ کاملہ پر ہوگا، تو معطوف معطوف علیہ کی خبر میں شریک نہیں ہوگا ، جیسے "هذه طالق ثلاثا وهذه طالق" میں جملہ کاملہ کا عطف جملہ کاملہ پر ہے، لہذا مبتداء ثانی یعنی " وهذه "مبتداء اول کی خبر یعنی ”طالق ثلاثا“ میں شریک نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ دونوں جملے تام ہیں، لہذا دوسرا جملہ پہلے جملہ کی خبر میں شریک نہ ہوگا ، پس پہلے ” هذه " سے تین طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی، اور دوسرے ” هذه " سے ایک واقع ہوگی ، اس لئے کہ دوسرا جملہ پہلے جملے کی خبر میں اس وقت شریک ہوتا ہے، جب دوسرا جملہ ناقص ہو جیسے ”هذه طالق وهذه “ میں دوسرا جملہ یعنی ” وهذه “ ناقص ہے، پہلے جملہ کی خبر میں شرکت کے بغیر مفید معنی نہیں ہے، لہذا دوسرا جملہ یعنی "وهذه " پہلے جملہ کی خبر یعنی طالق میں شریک ہوگا، تو دونوں کو ایک ایک طلاق پڑے گی۔ بہر حال دوسرے جملہ کی پہلے جملہ کی خبر میں شرکت دوسرے جملہ کے محتاج ہونے کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے، اس لئے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جملہ نا قصہ جملہ اولی کے ساتھ بعینہ اس چیز میں شریک ہوگا جس سے جملہ اولی تام ہوا ہے، چنانچہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق وطالق کہا تو طلاق ثانی بعینہ اس شرط پر معلق ہوگی ، جس شرط پر پہلی طلاق معلق ہے، طلاق ثانی کے لئے مستقل شرط محذوف ماننے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، بلکہ دونوں ایک ہی شرط میں شریک ہیں، لہذا یہ نہیں کہا جائے گا کہ طلاق ثانی کے لئے الگ شرط ہے، گو یا شوہر نے شرط کا اعادہ کیا ہے،اور اس کے قول ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق وطالق کی تقدیر عبارت یوں ہے۔ ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق، اس لئے کہ بعینہ شرط میں شرکت کافی ہے، الگ سے شرط کو مقدر ماننے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔

ہاں! البته جاء نی زید و عمرو، میں عمرہ کے ساتھ مستقل فعل محذوف ماننا پڑے گا، زید اور عمر و دونوں " بعینہ مذکور جاءنی میں شریک نہیں ہوں گے، کیونکہ ایک ہی مجبعیت میں زید اور عمر کا شریک ہونا ممکن نہیں ہے، اس لئے جملہ ثانیہ یعنی عمرو کے لئے مستقل فعل محذوف ماننے کی ضرورت پڑی ، بر خلاف پہلی صورت کے کہ اس میں معطوف علیہ اور معطوف دونوں بعینہ ایک شرط پر معلق ہو سکتے ہیں، جملہ ثانیہ مستقل شرط کا تقاضا نہیں کرتا ہے، لہذا وہاں شرط الگ سے محذوف نہیں مانی جائے گی۔
Translation: And sometimes waw enters a sentence that is complete together with its predicate, so participation in the predicate will not be established. And that is like the speaker's saying "This one is thrice divorced and this one is divorced" so the second will have one divorce, because participation in the predicate occurs due to the need of the second speech, when the second speech is incomplete. So when the second speech is complete, the evidence for participation is gone. For this reason we said that an incomplete sentence shares with the first sentence in exactly that thing by which the first sentence became complete, such that we said in the husband's saying "If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced" that the second divorce is linked to exactly that condition, and the second divorce does not require an independent condition, as if the speaker repeated the condition, and one will refer to being independent in the speaker's saying "Zayd and Amr came to me" due to the need that participation in a single coming is not possible.

Explanation: Waw is used for joining a single word to a single word, similarly a complete sentence is joined to a complete sentence by waw. And when a complete sentence is joined to a complete sentence, the conjoined does not share in the predicate of the first, like "This one is thrice divorced and this one is divorced" where a complete sentence is joined to a complete sentence, so the second subject "and this one" does not share in the predicate of the first subject, i.e., "thrice divorced", because both sentences are complete. Therefore the first "this one" gets three divorces, and the second "this one" gets one. This is because the second sentence shares in the predicate of the first sentence only when the second sentence is incomplete, like in "This one is divorced and this one" the second sentence "and this one" is incomplete, not benefitting meaning without sharing in the predicate of the first sentence. So the second sentence "and this one" will share in the predicate of the first, i.e., "divorced", and both will get one divorce each. In any case, the second sentence's participation in the predicate of the first is due to its need. Therefore we say that an incomplete sentence shares with the first sentence in exactly that thing by which the first sentence became complete. So if someone said to his wife "If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced," the second divorce is suspended on the exact same condition on which the first divorce is suspended; there is no need to assume a separate implied condition for the second divorce. Rather both share in one condition. So it will not be said that the second divorce has a separate condition; it is as if the husband repeated the condition. And the implied expression of his saying "If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced" is "If you enter the house, you are divorced; if you enter the house, you are divorced," because participation in the exact condition is sufficient, and there is no need to assume a separate condition.

Yes, certainly in "Zayd and Amr came to me" one must assume a separate implied verb for Amr. Both Zayd and Amr will not share in the mentioned "came" because it is not possible for Zayd and Amr to share in one act of coming. Therefore there is a need to assume a separate implied verb for the second sentence, i.e., Amr. Unlike the first case, where both the first and the conjoined can be suspended on exactly the same condition; the second sentence does not require an independent condition, so there a condition is not assumed separately as implied.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the function of the letter waw when joining sentences. It distinguishes between joining complete sentences (jumal kaamilah) and incomplete sentences (jumal naaqisah). When waw joins two complete sentences, the second sentence does not share in the predicate of the first; each has its own complete meaning. For example, if a husband says "This woman is thrice divorced, and this woman is divorced," the first woman gets three divorces and the second gets one, because the second sentence is complete with its own predicate. However, when the second sentence is incomplete (like just "wa hadhihi" without a predicate), it shares the first sentence's predicate. In that case, both women get one divorce each because the second borrows the predicate from the first. The passage further applies this to conditional divorces: if a man says "If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced" (with the second "divorced" joined by waw), the second divorce is also conditional on the same condition, not an independent condition. This is because the second part ("and divorced") is an incomplete sentence that shares the condition of the first. In contrast, in "Zayd and Amr came to me," the second subject cannot share the same act of coming because two individuals cannot perform one act of coming; hence a separate verb is implied. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi usul for understanding how waw operates in legal speech, particularly in marriage and divorce utterances.

Key Terms
جملة تامة (jumla taammah): A complete sentence that is fully meaningful without needing another sentence's predicate.
جملة ناقصة (jumla naaqisah): An incomplete sentence that requires another sentence's predicate to be meaningful.
مشاركة (mushārakah): The second sentence sharing the first sentence's predicate when the second is incomplete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example 'هذه طالق ثلاثا وهذه طالق', why does the second woman receive only one divorce?
A) Because the second sentence is incomplete and shares the predicate 'طالق', but not the adverb 'ثلاثا'.
B) Because the second sentence is complete, so it does not share the predicate 'طالق ثلاثا'.
C) Because the waw indicates a separate divorce but the second woman deserves less due to custom.
D) Because the second woman is not explicitly mentioned in the predicate.

Key Takeaway
The conjunction waw joins sentences; only when the second sentence is incomplete does it share the predicate of the first.

The Borrowed Waw for Circumstantial Clause (Haal)
Textual analysis of waw for haal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when waw is used for haal in Quranic and legal texts and apply the Hanafi principle that waw can indicate simultaneity.

Core Idea
Waw borrowed for haal: the circumstance is simultaneous with the action, not sequential.

In Hanafi usul, the letter waw has a literal meaning of conjunction (jama'). However, it is often used metaphorically to introduce a circumstantial clause (haal) because both involve simultaneity. Understanding this distinction is crucial for interpreting Quranic verses and legal utterances correctly—for example, the difference between the gates of Paradise being open before arrival versus opening at the moment of arrival. This lesson unpacks the proof from Surah Az-Zumar and its application in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the literal and metaphorical uses of waw
Recognize that waw originally means conjunction, but can be borrowed for haal due to the common element of simultaneity (al-jam'iyyah).
Al-haal is simultaneous with dhu al-haal; waw joins things.
2
Analyse the Quranic proof
In the verse 'Until when they come to it and its gates are opened' (حَتَّىٰ إِذَا جَاءُوهَا وَفُتِحَتْ أَبْوَابُهَا), determine whether the waw indicates conjunction (gates open simultaneously with arrival) or haal (gates already open).
The Hanafi interpretation opts for haal to honor the believers.
3
Apply to legal utterances
In statements like 'Give me a thousand and you are free' (اد إليّ ألفًا وأنت حر), identify whether the waw is haal or conjunctive. If haal, the freeing occurs only at the moment of payment.
Same applies to 'Come down and you are safe' (انزل وأنت آمن) for a harbi.
4
Derive the usul principle
From the analysis, formulate: 'Waw can be used majazan for haal when the context indicates simultaneity and honor or conditionality.'
This principle guides interpretation of contracts and oaths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يستعار الواو للحال بمعنى الجمع أيضا لان الحال تجامع ذا الحال قال الله تعالى حتى إذا جاءوها وفتحت أبوابها أو وأبوابها مفتوحة وقالوا في قول الرجل لعبدِه اذ إليّ ألفًا وأنت حُرّ وللحربي انزل وأنت أمن إن الواو للحال حتى لا يعتق العبد إلا بالأداء ولا يأمن الحربي ما لم ينزل.

ترجمہ :۔ اور کبھی واؤ کو جمع کے معنی کی وجہ سے حال کے لئے بھی مستعار لیا جاتا ہے، اس لئے کہ حال ذوالحال کے ساتھ جمع ہوتا ہے، اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے يہاں تک کہ جب پہنچ جائیں اس پر اور کھولے جائیں اس کے دروازے" یعنی اس کے دروازے کھلے ہوئے ہوں، اور فقہاء نے کہا مرد کے قول اپنے غلام سے ادالی الفاوانت حر" میں، اور حربی سے انزل وانت آمن" میں کہ واؤ حال کے لئے ہے، حتی کہ غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا مگر ادا سے، اور حربی کو امن نہ ہوگا جب تک کہ وہ نہ اترے۔

تشریح : ۔ واؤ کے حقیقی معنی تو جمع کے ہیں، مگر کبھی مجازا واؤ حال کے لئے بھی استعمال ہوتا ہے، حقیقت اور مجاز میں مشترکہ علت جمعیت کے معنی ہیں، یعنی حال بھی ذوالحال کے ساتھ جمع ہوتا ہے، اور واؤ بھی جمع کے لئے آتا ہے، اس مناسبت سے واؤ مجازاً حال کے لئے استعمال ہوتا ہے جیسے اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا حتى اذا جاءوها وفتحت ابوابها یعنی مومن جب جنت میں آئیں گے تو جنت کے دروازے کھلے ہوئے ہوں گے، اس آیت میں واؤ حال کے لئے ہے عطف کے لئے نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ مومنین کے اکرام کے لئے یہ مناسب ہے کہ دروازے پہلے سے کھلے ہوں، اور یہ اسی وقت ہو سکتا ہے جب واؤ کو حال کے لئے مانا جائے، اور واؤ کو عطف کے لئے مانا جائے تو مومنین کا آنا اور دروازوں کا کھلنا ساتھ ساتھ ہوگا، جو اکرام کے لئے غیر موزوں ہے، اس لئے کہ معزز مہمان کا اکرام یہ ہے کہ دروازہ پہلے سے کھلا رکھا جائے، نہ کہ آنے کے وقت کھولا جائے۔ اسی طرح اگر کسی نے اپنے غلام سے کہا "اد الی الفاوانت حر" یا کسی مسلمان نے حربی سے کہا "انزل وانت آمن" تو اسی طرح واؤ حال کے لئے ہے، لہذا جب تک غلام ایک ہزار (درہم) ادا نہ کرے آزاد نہیں ہوگا، جب غلام ادا کرے گا تو ادا کے وقت آزاد ہوگا، کیونکہ واؤ حال کے لئے ہے، اور حربی جب تک اترے گا امن میں نہیں ہوگا۔
And sometimes waw is borrowed for the circumstantial clause (haal) with the meaning of conjunction, because the circumstance is simultaneous with its owner. Allah Most High said: "Until when they come to it and its gates are opened" or "And its gates are opened". And they (the jurists) said concerning a man's statement to his slave: 'Give me a thousand and you are free', and to a harbi (non-Muslim enemy): 'Come down and you are safe' that the waw is for haal, so that the slave does not become free except with payment, and the harbi does not become safe unless he comes down.

Translation: And sometimes waw is borrowed for haal due to the meaning of conjunction, because the haal is simultaneous with its owner. Allah Most High said: "Until when they come to it and its gates are opened" i.e., its gates are opened. And the jurists said concerning a man's statement to his slave: 'Give me a thousand and you are free', and to a harbi: 'Come down and you are safe' that the waw is for haal, so that the slave does not become free except with payment, and the harbi does not become safe unless he comes down.

Explanation: The original meaning of waw is conjunction, but sometimes it is used metaphorically for haal. The common cause between the literal and metaphorical is the meaning of conjunction; i.e., the haal is simultaneous with its owner, and waw is used for conjunction. Due to this suitability, waw is used metaphorically for haal. As Allah Most High said: "Until when they come to it and its gates are opened" meaning the believers will come to Paradise and its gates will be open. In this verse, waw is for haal, not for conjunction. Because it is appropriate for honoring the believers that the gates are already open, and that can only happen if waw is taken for haal. If waw is taken for conjunction, then the coming of the believers and the opening of the gates would happen simultaneously, which is not suitable for honoring, because honoring a respected guest is to keep the gate open beforehand, not to open it at the time of arrival. Similarly, if someone says to his slave "Give me a thousand and you are free" or a Muslim says to a harbi "Come down and you are safe", then similar to the above, waw is for haal. So the slave does not become free unless he pays the thousand; he becomes free at the time of payment, because the waw is for haal. And the harbi will not be safe until he comes down.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the metaphorical use of the letter waw to indicate a circumstantial clause (haal). While the original meaning of waw is conjunction (jama'), it can be borrowed for haal due to the shared element of simultaneity. In haal, the circumstance is simultaneous with the main action; similarly, waw joins things together. The author provides a Quranic proof: "Until when they come to it and its gates are opened" (Surah Az-Zumar, 39:73). Hanafi scholars interpret the waw here as haal, meaning the gates are already open when they arrive, which shows honor. If waw were a conjunction, it would imply the gates open at the same moment as arrival, which is less dignified. The passage then gives two fiqhi examples: (1) A master saying to his slave "Give me a thousand dirhams and you are free" - the waw denotes haal, meaning the slave becomes free only at the moment of payment, not before. If the slave dies before paying, he is still a slave. (2) A Muslim says to a harbi (enemy combatant) "Come down and you are safe" - the waw indicates haal, so safety is conditional upon descending. If the harbi comes down, he is safe; if he does not, he remains under threat. This analysis is important in Hanafi usul for correctly interpreting legal utterances, especially in contracts and oaths.

Key Terms
الحال (al-haal): A circumstantial clause indicating the state of the subject at the time of the action, often introduced by a waw borrowed for that purpose.
ذو الحال (dhu al-haal): The owner of the state (the subject whose circumstance is described).
الواو المستعارة (al-waw al-musta'arah): Waw borrowed from its literal meaning of conjunction to indicate a circumstantial clause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, what is the common cause (jami') between the literal meaning of waw (conjunction) and its metaphorical use for haal?
A) Sequence of events
B) Simultaneity or conjunction (jam'iyyah)
C) Causality
D) Exclusivity

Key Takeaway
Waw can be metaphorically used for haal when simultaneity is contextually indicated, affecting legal interpretations of contracts, oaths, and conditions.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Hanafi Analysis of Thumma: Complete Delay vs. Partial Delay
Textual analysis of thumma with intra-madhhab dispute and ta'wil example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi linguistic analysis of the particle 'thumma' to determine rulings in conditional divorce and identify when metaphorical interpretation (ta'wil) is necessary.

Core Idea
Thumma indicates delay; complete delay (Abu Hanifa) vs. partial delay (Sahibayn) determines conditional divorce outcomes.

This lesson explores the Hanafi usul analysis of the conjunction particle 'thumma' (then). You will learn the intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding whether the implied delay affects both utterance and ruling or only the ruling. The practical consequences are demonstrated through conditional divorce scenarios. Additionally, you will see how 'thumma' is interpreted metaphorically as 'wa' when its literal meaning is impossible, as in the Quranic verse about faith and righteous deeds.

Guided Path
1
State the general meaning of thumma
Thumma is a harf atf that indicates delay (tarakhi) between the ma'tuf and ma'tuf 'alayh. This is its basic linguistic function.
2
Identify the intra-madhhab dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that the delay is complete: it applies to both utterance (takallum) and ruling (hukm). The Sahibayn hold that delay is only in the ruling, not in utterance. Understand the linguistic rationale for each view.
The Sahibayn are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Apply the dispute to a deferred condition case
Consider a husband telling his non-consummated wife: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced if you enter the house.' According to Abu Hanifa, the first divorce is immediate and not suspended; the subsequent ones are invalid. According to the Sahibayn, all three are suspended on the condition and occur in sequence.
The wife is non-consummated, so one divorce makes her bain, removing the subject for later divorces.
4
Apply the dispute to a brought-forward condition case
If the condition is placed first: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, then divorced, then divorced.' Abu Hanifa suspends only the first divorce on the condition; the second occurs immediately. The Sahibayn suspend all three on the condition.
The second divorce occurs immediately under Abu Hanifa's view because the delay is only in ruling, not utterance? Actually careful: In the brought-forward condition, the first divorce is suspended; the second is not suspended because of the break in utterance? The text says: 'the first is suspended, the second occurs immediately, the third is invalid' for Abu Hanifa. For Sahibayn, all are suspended.
5
Explain the metaphorical use when literal meaning is impossible
When the literal meaning of thumma (delay) is impossible, it can be interpreted metaphorically as 'wa' (and). This is illustrated by Quran 90:17, where righteous deeds precede faith, but faith must accompany them. To avoid contradiction, thumma is taken to mean 'wa' indicating simultaneity.
This is an example of ta'wil (interpretation) based on contextual necessity (muta'azzir).

میں بھی، گو یا متکلم معطوف علیہ کو بول کر چپ ہو گیا، پھر معطوف کا تکلم کیا تو معطوف کلام مستأنف یعنی نیا کلام ہو گیا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تراخی صرف حکم کے پائے جانے میں ہے تکلم میں نہیں ہے، ہتکلم نے واقع ہو جائے گی اور دوسری اور تیسری طلاق لغو ہو جائے گی ، کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک لفظ ثم میں تکلم میں بھی تراخی ہوتی ہے، تو گویا شوہر پہلی طلاق دیکر چپ ہو گیا، پھر از سر نو باقی طلاق کا تکلم کیا، تو يتعلقن جملة : - صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ تکلم میں تراخی نہیں ہوتی ، اس لئے تینوں طلاقیں شرط پر معلق ہو جائیں گی اور شرط کے پائے جانے کے وقت ترتیب سے واقع ہوں گی ، چاہے شرط کو مقدم کیا ہو یا مؤخر ، اس لئے تو پہلی طلاق سے بائنہ ہو جائے گی ، باقی کا محل نہ رہے گی تو باقی دولغو ہو جائیں گی۔ مصنف االلہ فرماتے ہیں کہ کبھی غم واؤ کے معنی میں لیا جاتا ہے مجازاً، جب اس کا حقیقی معنی یعنی تراخی متعذ رہو، جیسے اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمايا ثم كان من الذین آمنوا یہاں تم کو حقیقی معنی میں لینا متعذر ہے، کیونکہ اس سے پہلے کی آیت میں اعمال صالحہ کا ذکر ہے، اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا فلا اقتحم العقبة وما ادرك ما العقبة فك رقبة او اطعام في يوم ذى مسغبة، يتيماذا مقربه او مسكينا ذ ا متربة ، ثم كان من الذين آمنوا". اگر یہاں غم کے حقیقی معنی مراد لیتے ہیں ، تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ فک رقبہ، اطعام طعام وغیر ہ اعمال صالحہ پہلے ہیں ، اور ایمان بعد میں ہے، تراخی کے ساتھ ، حالانکہ ایمان ساتھ ساتھ ہونا چاہیے، بغیر ایمان کے اعمال صالحہ معتبر نہیں ہے، اس تعذر کی وجہ سے تم کو اس کے معنی سے مجاز کی طرف پھیر دیا، واؤ کے معنی میں لیا، تو اب یہ خرابی لازم نہ آئیگی، کیونکہ واؤ مطلق جمع کے لئے ہوتا ہے، لہذا اعمال صالحہ اور ایمان جمع ہو گئے۔
What comes after it is as if he was silent on the first, and they both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: they all (the divorces) are attached (to the condition) together and occur in sequence. And sometimes it (thumma) is used metaphorically in the meaning of waw (and). Allah Most High said: 'Then he became among those who believed.' Translation: Indeed, thumma is a particle of conjunction (atf) with the quality of delay (tarakhi). Then, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the delay is in the manner of separation (qat'), as if the speech is considered a new beginning due to complete delay. According to the Sahibayn, the delay is in the existence of the ruling (hukm), not in the utterance (takallum). The explanation of this difference concerns a man who said to his wife before consummation: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced if you enter the house.' Imam Abu Hanifa says: the first divorce occurs, and the subsequent ones are invalid; as if he pronounced the first divorce and then became silent. The Sahibayn said: all are attached to the condition together and occur in sequence. And sometimes thumma is used metaphorically in the meaning of waw, as Allah Most High said: 'Then he became among those who believed.' Sharh: The third letter among the particles of conjunction is thumma, which comes for 'atf with delay, i.e., it indicates that the ma'tuf is after the ma'tuf 'alayh with delay. Then there is a difference regarding the degree of delay: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, complete delay occurs in both utterance and ruling, i.e., the ma'tuf is delayed in both utterance and ruling compared to the ma'tuf 'alayh, as if the speaker said the ma'tuf 'alayh and then became silent, then spoke the ma'tuf, so the ma'tuf becomes a new speech (musta'naf). According to the Sahibayn, delay is only in the ruling, not in utterance; the speaker uttered both the ma'tuf 'alayh and the ma'tuf together. The fruit of this difference appears in this example: If a husband said to his non-consummated wife: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced', then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the first divorce occurs and the second and third are invalid, because in his view thumma implies delay also in utterance, so as if the husband said the first divorce and then became silent, then spoke the remaining divorces anew; so the first divorce is not suspended on the condition, rather it occurs immediately. Since the wife is non-consummated, she becomes bain (irrevocably separated) by one divorce, so there remains no subject for the second and third divorces, hence they are invalid. This case is when the condition is deferred. If the condition is brought forward and he says: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, then divorced, then divorced', then the first divorce is suspended on the condition, the second occurs immediately, and the third is invalid. And they (the Sahibayn) said: they all are attached together (to the condition): According to the Sahibayn, since there is no delay in utterance, all three divorces are suspended on the condition, and when the condition occurs they take effect in sequence, whether the condition is brought forward or deferred, because due to conjunction the three divorces are combined, and due to delay they occur one after another. If the wife is consummated, then when the condition occurs all three occur in sequence; if non-consummated, she becomes bain by the first, no subject remains for the rest, so the remaining two are invalid. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) says that sometimes thumma is used metaphorically in the meaning of waw, when its literal meaning (delay) is impossible (muta'azzir), as in Allah's saying: 'Then he became among those who believed.' Here taking thumma in its literal meaning is impossible, because the preceding verse mentions righteous deeds: {فَلَا اقْتَحَمَ الْعَقَبَةَ وَمَا أَدْرَاكَ مَا الْعَقَبَةُ فَكُّ رَقَبَةٍ أَوْ إِطْعَامٌ فِي يَوْمٍ ذِي مَسْغَبَةٍ يَتِيمًا ذَا مَقْرَبَةٍ أَوْ مِسْكِينًا ذَا مَتْرَبَةٍ ثُمَّ كَانَ مِنَ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا} If we take thumma with its literal meaning, it would mean that righteous deeds come first and faith after with delay, whereas faith must be simultaneous, as righteous deeds without faith are not valid. Due to this impossibility, thumma is turned from its literal meaning to metaphorical, taken in the meaning of waw, so this defect does not arise, because waw is for absolute conjunction, so righteous deeds and faith are combined.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the Arabic particle 'thumma' (then) from the perspective of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It begins by stating the general rule: thumma is a conjunction (atf) indicating delay (tarakhi). However, the nature of this delay differs between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the delay is complete, affecting both the utterance (takallum) and the ruling (hukm). That is, when a speaker says 'A, then B', it is as if he said A, paused, and then began a new speech act for B. Consequently, the first part (ma'tuf 'alayh) is independent from the condition, if any. In contrast, the Sahibayn hold that the delay is only in the ruling, not in the utterance; both parts are spoken in one connected speech, but the ruling takes effect sequentially. The author illustrates this difference with a classic Hanafi example: a husband says to his non-consummated wife, 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced, if you enter the house' (with the condition deferred). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the first divorce is not suspended on the condition; it occurs immediately, making the wife bain (irrevocably separate). Since she is non-consummated, she becomes bain with one divorce, so the remaining divorces are invalid because there is no marital bond left. According to the Sahibayn, all three divorces are suspended on the condition, and when the condition occurs, they take effect in sequence. If the wife is non-consummated, the first divorce effects bain, and the subsequent ones are invalid due to loss of subject. The passage then addresses a secondary issue: when the literal meaning of thumma (delay) is impossible, it may be used metaphorically in the sense of 'wa' (and), as in the Quranic verse {ثُمَّ كَانَ مِنَ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا} ('Then he became among those who believed') after mentioning righteous deeds. Since faith must precede or accompany righteous deeds, taking thumma literally would contradict this, so it is interpreted as 'wa' to indicate simultaneity. This is a clear example of the Hanafi use of linguistic analysis (lugha) and the principle of ta'wil (interpretation) based on contextual necessity.

Key Terms
ثُمَّ (thumma): A particle of conjunction (harf atf) indicating delay (tarakhi) between the ma'tuf and ma'tuf alayh.
تَرَاخٍ (tarakhi): Delay; the temporal or sequential interval indicated by 'thumma'.
قَطْع (qat'): Separation; the idea that after uttering the first part, the speaker is considered to have stopped and started a new speech act.
مُتَعَذِّر (muta'azzir): Impossible or not feasible; used to describe a situation where the literal meaning of a word cannot be applied without causing contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a husband says to his non-consummated wife, 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced' (without any condition), what happens?
A) All three divorces occur immediately in sequence.
B) The first divorce occurs immediately, and the second and third are invalid because she becomes bain.
C) No divorce occurs because the marriage is not consummated.
D) Only the first divorce occurs, but it is suspended on an implied condition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi analysis of thumma distinguishes between complete delay (Abu Hanifa) and partial delay (Sahibayn), directly affecting whether conditional divorces are suspended or immediate, and thumma can be interpreted as 'wa' when literal meaning is impossible.

The Particle Bal: Nullification and Substitution in Conditional Statements
Textual analysis of the particle 'bal' and its application in a divorce case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of the particle 'bal' to determine the number of divorces in a conditional divorce statement where 'bal' is used.

Core Idea
When 'bal' nullifies the first but nullification is impossible, the second becomes a separate oath, and both take effect.

The Arabic particle 'bal' (but rather) is used to affirm the second element and disregard the first. In legal contexts, however, nullification of the first element may be impossible, leading to an interesting Hanafi ruling. This lesson analyzes the linguistic rule of 'bal' and its application in a divorce scenario, demonstrating how the Hanafi imams derived the total number of divorces when a husband uses 'bal' in a conditional statement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic function of 'bal'
State the rule: 'bal' affirms what comes after it and turns away from what precedes it.
2
Recognize the legal scenario
A husband says to his wife before consummation: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced once, no but rather twice.'
The condition (entering the house) is shared.
3
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
Abu Hanifa: 'bal' is for nullifying the first and establishing the second in its place. However, nullifying the first (the 'once' divorce) is not within the husband's capacity because the condition attaches to both parts.
Nullification is physically impossible since the first utterance has legal effect once the condition is met.
4
Derive the legal effect
Since nullification is impossible, the second part ('twice') is treated as directly attached to the condition without intermediary, like a separate oath. Thus, when the condition is fulfilled, both the 'once' and the 'twice' take effect, totaling three divorces.
One divorce from 'once' and two from 'twice'.
5
Contrast with other conjunctions
Unlike conjunction with 'wa' (and), where only the last statement would count, 'bal' creates two separate conditional oaths.
The passage mentions 'contrary to conjunction with waw'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا بَلْ فَمَوْضَوْعْ لِإِثْبَاتِ مَا بَعْدَهُ وَالْإعْرَاضِ عَمَّا قَبْلَهُ يُقَالُ جَاءَ نِي زَيْدٌ بَلْ عَمْرُو وَقَالُوْا جَمِيعًا فِيْمَنْ قَالَ لِاِمْرَأَتِهِ قَبْلَ الدُّخُول بهَا إنْ دَخَلْتِ الدَّارَ فَانْتِ طَالِقٌ وَاحِدَةً لَا بَلْ ثِنَتَيْنِ أَنَّهُ يَقَعُ الثَّلْثُ إِذَا دَ خَلْتِ الدَّارَ بِخِلَافِ الْعَطْفِ بِالْوَاوِ وَعِنْدَ ا بِي حَنِيفَةَ الله لِأَنَّهُ لَمَا كَانَ لِإِبْطَالِ الْأَوَلِ وَإِقَامَةِ الثَّانِي مَقَامَهُ كَانَ مِنْ قَضْيَتِهِ اتَّصَالُ الثَّانِي بِالشَّرْطِ بِلَاوَاسِطَةٍ لَكِنَّ بِشَرْطِ إِبْطَالِ الْأَوَّلِ وَلَيْسَ فِي وَسْعِهِ ذَلِک وَفِي وَسْعِهِ إِفْرَادُ الثَانِي بِالشَّرْطِ لِيَتَصِلَ بِهِ بِغَيْرِ وَاسِطَةٍ فَيَصِيْرُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْحَلْفِ بِيَمِيْنَيْنِ فَيَثْبُتُ مَا فِي وُسْعِهِ - ترجمہ:۔ اور بہر حال بل تو وہ وضع کیا گیا ہے اپنے مابعد کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے ،اور اپنے ماقبل سے اعراض کرنے کے لئے ، کہا جاتا ہے جاء نی زید بل عمرو ، اور ائمہ ثلاثہ نے فرمایا ہے اس شخص کے بارے میں جس نے اپنی بیوی سے دخول سے پہلے کہا " ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق واحدة لا بل ثنتن “ کہ عورت جب گھر
As for 'bal' (but rather), it is placed to affirm what comes after it and to turn away from what precedes it. One says: 'Zaid came to me, but rather 'Amr.' And they (the three imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) all said concerning one who said to his wife before consummation: 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced once, no but rather twice,' that three (divorces) occur when she enters the house, contrary to conjunction with waw. And according to Abu Hanifa, because it (bal) is for nullifying the first and establishing the second in its place, it requires that the second is directly connected to the condition without intermediary, but with the condition of nullifying the first. And that (nullifying) is not within his capacity, whereas it is within his capacity to single out the second with the condition so that it is directly attached to it without intermediary, so it becomes like swearing two oaths, so what is within his capacity is established. Translation: Indeed, 'bal' is placed to affirm what comes after it and to turn away from what precedes it. One says: 'Zaid came to me, but rather 'Amr.' And the three imams have ruled concerning a man who said to his wife before consummation: 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced once, no but rather twice,' that three divorces occur when she enters the house, unlike conjunction with waw. And according to Abu Hanifa, because bal is for nullifying the first and establishing the second in its place, it requires that the second is directly connected to the condition without intermediary, but with the condition of nullifying the first. And that nullification is not within his capacity (because he cannot undo the first divorce), but it is within his capacity to single out the second with the condition so that it is directly attached without intermediary, so it becomes like two separate oaths, so what is within his capacity (three divorces) is established.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the Arabic particle 'bal' (but rather) in the context of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It states the general linguistic rule: 'bal' is used to affirm the second element and disregard the first. The author then presents a legal example: a husband says to his wife before consummation, 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced once, no but rather twice.' The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) agree that three divorces occur when the condition is fulfilled, unlike what would happen if the conjunction 'wa' (and) were used. The reasoning, attributed to Abu Hanifa, is that 'bal' functions to nullify the first statement and establish the second in its place. However, nullifying the first divorce is not possible because it has already taken effect (if the condition is met, the first divorce has already occurred? Actually the condition is not yet fulfilled, but the statement 'once' is part of the conditional sentence. The reasoning is nuanced: the speaker intends to negate the 'once' and replace it with 'twice', but since the first is part of the condition, it cannot be undone. So the second ('twice') is taken as directly attached to the condition, resulting in two divorces from that phrase, plus the initial 'once' which is not nullified, totaling three. The text explains that because nullifying the first is not within his capacity (since it was uttered as part of the condition), the second is treated as if it were a separate conditional statement ('twice'), making it akin to two separate oaths. Therefore, when the condition is fulfilled, both the 'once' and the 'twice' take effect, giving three divorces (one from the first, two from the second). The text contrasts this with conjunction using 'wa', where only the last would count? Actually it says 'contrary to conjunction with waw' meaning if he had said 'wa ithnatayn' (and two), then only two would occur? The passage does not fully elaborate, but the key point is the effect of 'bal' in this specific construction.

Key Terms
بَلْ (bal): A particle of conjunction (harf atf) that affirms the second element and turns away from (negates/nullifies) the first.
إِعْرَاض (i'rad): Turning away from or disregarding the first element; the function of bal.
إِبْطَال (ibtal): Nullification; the first element is rendered void by bal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Three divorces
D) No divorce because the statement is contradictory

Key Takeaway
When 'bal' is used in a conditional divorce and nullification of the first divorce is impossible, both divorces take effect, treating the second as a separate conditional statement.

Conditions for 'Laken' in Istidrak after Negation
Explains two conditions for 'laken' as corrective conjunction after negation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions for 'laken' to function as a conjunction after negation and apply them to legal scenarios to determine the validity of the conjunction.

Core Idea
'Laken' after negation only corrects if the subjects differ — you cannot negate and affirm the same thing.

In Hanafi usul, the particle 'laken' (but) is used for istidrak, a corrective conjunction after a negation. However, not every 'laken' after negation is a valid conjunction. The author explains two strict conditions that must be satisfied for the conjunction to hold. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correctly analyzing legal statements, especially in cases of acknowledgment, marriage, and other contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the use of 'laken'
Locate a statement where 'laken' appears after a negation. Note the preceding clause and the clause that follows.
2
Check continuity (ittisal)
Ensure that the clause after 'laken' is directly linked to the preceding negated clause. If there is a break or the statement becomes independent, the first condition fails.
Continuity means the second part is grammatically and semantically attached.
3
Check different subjects (ikhtilaf al-mahall)
Verify that the subject of the negation and the subject of the affirmation are different. If both refer to the same thing, the second condition fails.
Distinguish between the core subject and subsidiary details (e.g., dower).
4
Determine function
If both conditions are met, 'laken' functions as a conjunction (عطف). If not, it is an independent statement (مستأنف).
5
Derive legal consequence
Assess the legal effect: a conjunction integrates the second part into the first, while an independent statement requires separate evaluation.
Example: In the slave case, conjunction leads to ownership by the third party.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ہوا ہو (۲) نفی اور اثبات دونوں کا محل الگ الگ ہو، یعنی بعینہ ایک ہی چیز کی نفی اور اثبات نہ ہورہا ہے، تا کہ دونوں جمع ہوسکیں۔ جیسے کسی کے پاس غلام ہے اور یہ اقرار کرتا ہے کہ یہ غلام زید کا ہے، تو زید مقرلہ کہتا ہے ما كان لي قط لكن لفلان آخر کہ یہ غلام میرا نہیں ہے، لیکن وہ فلاں کا ہے، تو یہ غلام فلاں کا ہوگا، نہ کہ مقولہ کا، کیونکہ یہاں دونوں شرطیں موجود ہیں، کہ لکن نفی کے بعد ہے، اور لکن کا ما یعنی مقرلہ۔ اور شرط مفقود ہونے کی مثال مصنف اللہ نے بیان کی کہ اگر فضولی نے کسی عورت کا نکاح سو درھم میں کر دیا عورت کو جب خبر پہنچی تو اس نے کہا ”لا اجیزہ“ میں اس نکاح کو جائز نہیں کرتی ولكن اجيزه بمائة وخمسين “ لیکن ڈیڑھ سو درھم میں جائز کرتی ہوں تو عورت کے اس قول سے عقدِ نکاح فسخ ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ عورت نے جس فعل کی نفی کی ہے اس فعل کا اثبات کیا ہے، یعنی نکاح کی نفی کی ہے اور نکاح ہی کا اثبات کیا ہے، تو دوسری شرط نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے کلام مستأنف اور مستقل ہوگا، اور جب مستقل کلام ہوا تو یہ عورت کی طرف سے ایجاب ہوگا ، اور ایجاب بغیر قبول کے معتبر نہیں ہے، لہذا نکاح منعقد نہ ہوگا، اور فضولی کا کیا ہوا نکاح لا اجیزہ سے نسخ ہو گیا۔ طالب علمانہ سوال: ہوتا ہے کہ عورت کے کلام میں نفی اور اثبات ایک ہی سے متعلق نہیں ہے بلکہ نفی سو درہم کے ساتھ مقید ہے اور اثبات ڈیڑھ سو درھم کے ساتھ مقید ہے، تو میں مہر کا ذکر نہ ہو، یا اس کی نفی ہو تو بھی نکاح ہو جاتا ہے، لہذا عورت کے کلام میں نکاح ہی کی نفی اور اثبات ہے ،تو اتساق کی شرط مفقود ہے، لہذا عطف درست نہ ہوگا۔۔ ہاں اگر عورت اس طرح کہے "لا اجيزه بمائة ولكن اجيزه بمائة وخمسين " تو استدراک اصل نکاح میں نہ ہوگا بلکہ مقدار مہر میں ہوگا یعنی نفی کا تعلق مائة سے ہوگا اور اثبات کا تعلق مائة و خمسین سے ہو گا تو اتساق پا یا گیا، لہذا لکن عطف کے لئے ہوگا۔
Then the author said: 'But as for conjunction by it: in the case of conjunction by 'laken' for istidrak after negation, there are two conditions: (1) the speech in which 'laken' occurs must be connected, i.e., what comes after 'laken' must be linked to what comes before it; (2) the subjects of negation and affirmation must be separate, i.e., the negation and affirmation are not about exactly the same thing, so that both can be combined. For example, someone has a slave and he acknowledges that this slave belongs to Zaid; then Zaid, the one about whom the acknowledgment is made, says: 'He never belonged to me, but to someone else' – so this slave belongs to that other person, not to Zaid, because both conditions are present: 'laken' comes after negation, what comes after 'laken' is linked to what came before, and the subjects of negation and affirmation are separate – negation refers to the speaker, affirmation refers to another person, so the conjunction is valid; therefore the slave belongs to that other person, not to the speaker (the one about whom the acknowledgment is made). And an example of the condition being absent: the author stated that if a fuduli (unauthorized agent) marries a woman for one hundred dirhams, when the woman receives the news she says: 'I do not accept it' – I do not accept this marriage, 'but I accept it for one hundred and fifty dirhams' – then by this statement the marriage contract is dissolved, because the woman negated the very act she affirmed – she negated the marriage and affirmed the same marriage; due to the absence of the second condition, the speech becomes independent and separate; and when it becomes independent speech, it constitutes an offer (ijab) from the woman, and an offer without acceptance is not valid, so the marriage is not contracted, and the marriage performed by the fuduli is annulled by her saying 'I do not accept it'. An intelligent student's question: In the woman's statement, the negation and affirmation are not related to the same thing; rather, the negation is qualified by one hundred dirhams, and the affirmation by one hundred and fifty dirhams, so their subjects are different, hence coherence (ittisaq) is present, and conjunction should be valid. The answer: One hundred and one hundred fifty are the dower (mahr), and the dower is subsidiary in marriage, it is not considered; therefore even if the dower is not mentioned or is negated, the marriage still takes place; thus in the woman's statement, the negation and affirmation are both about the marriage itself, so the condition of coherence is absent. Yes, if the woman says: 'I do not accept it for one hundred, but I accept it for one hundred and fifty', then the istidrak would not be about the original marriage but about the amount of the dower – thus the negation relates to one hundred and the affirmation to one hundred and fifty, so coherence is present, and 'laken' is for conjunction.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the Arabic particle 'laken' (but) as used in the construction of istidrak (corrective exception) after negation. The author, in his commentary on Al-Husami, explains that for 'laken' to function as a true conjunction (عطف) after a negated statement, two conditions must be satisfied. First, the speech must be continuous (متصل), meaning the part after 'laken' must be directly linked to what precedes it, not a new independent sentence. Second, the subject of the negation and the subject of the affirmation must be different; you cannot negate and affirm the same thing in one connected sentence. If the two conditions are met, the conjunction is valid and the second part corrects the first. If the second condition is not met (i.e., the same subject is both negated and affirmed), then 'laken' is not a conjunction but rather a separate independent statement (مستأنف). The author provides a clear legal example: a slave ownership case where someone acknowledges a slave belongs to Zaid, but Zaid denies it saying 'He never belonged to me, but to someone else'. The ruling is that the slave belongs to the other person because the conditions are satisfied. Conversely, the marriage case of a fuduli shows a problematic use: the woman says 'I do not accept it (the marriage) but I accept it for one hundred and fifty'. Since the same marriage is both negated and affirmed, 'laken' cannot function as a conjunction; instead her statement is an independent offer (ijab) that requires acceptance, so the original marriage is dissolved and no new marriage is formed. The author then addresses a potential objection: the negation and affirmation seem to be about different amounts of dower, so why are they considered the same subject? The reason is that the dower is subsidiary; the core subject is the marriage itself. Therefore the condition fails. However, if the woman specifies the dower in both clauses, the negation and affirmation are about different dower amounts, not the marriage, so 'laken' then functions as a correct conjunction. This careful linguistic analysis is typical of Hanafi usul, where precise understanding of particles has direct legal consequences.

Key Terms
استدراك (istidrak): A linguistic device where a subsequent clause corrects or removes an impression created by a preceding negated clause.
عطف (atf): Grammatical conjunction linking two elements with a particle, where the second is directly connected to the first.
نفی (nafi): Negation; the act of denying something.
اثبات (ithbat): Affirmation; establishing the existence of something.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two conditions for 'laken' to function as a correct conjunction (عطف) after negation?
A) The speech must be continuous and the subjects of negation and affirmation must be the same.
B) The speech must be disconnected and the subjects must differ.
C) The speech must be continuous and the subjects of negation and affirmation must differ.
D) The speech must be disconnected and the subjects must be the same.

Key Takeaway
'Laken' after negation only functions as a valid conjunction when the speech is continuous and the subjects of negation and affirmation are different; otherwise it is an independent statement.

The Particle 'Aw' in Hanafi Usul: Its Functions in Khabar, Insha, Umum, and Hatta
Explains the functions of 'aw' in news, commencement, generalization, and as meaning 'until'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the function of the particle 'aw' in different speech contexts (khabar, insha, negation, permission, oaths) and apply its meaning to derive legal rulings.

Core Idea
The particle 'aw' has four distinct legal-linguistic functions: doubt, choice, generality, or 'until'—context determines the ruling.

The Arabic particle 'aw' (or) is a seemingly simple word, but in Islamic law, its meaning shifts dramatically based on the type of speech it appears in. This lesson unpacks the four primary functions of 'aw' as explained in the Hanafi usul tradition: causing doubt in statements, granting choice in performatives, imposing individual or collective generality in oaths, and even acting as a substitute for 'until'. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correctly interpreting legal utterances and fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Classify the speech type
Determine whether the utterance is khabar (informative) or insha (performative/construction). In khabar, 'aw' indicates doubt; in insha, it indicates choice.
If the utterance is ambiguous, Hanafi principles give priority to the intended legal effect.
2
Check for negation or permission
If the sentence is negative (e.g., 'I will not do X or Y'), 'aw' imposes generality of individuals (umum al-afrad): each alternative is individually negated. If it is permissive (e.g., 'except X or Y'), it imposes generality of collective (umum al-ijtima): all alternatives are jointly permitted.
This distinction is crucial for oaths and exceptions.
3
Oaths with contradictory clauses
When an oath begins with a negation followed by an affirmation connected by 'aw', the particle may be interpreted as 'hatta' (until). This creates a limit such that entering the second situation fulfills the oath even before the first.
This applies only when the two clauses differ in negation and affirmation.
4
Apply the ruling
Based on the identified function, determine the legal consequence: validity of the utterance, breaking of an oath, or scope of permission.
Always refer to the specific examples in the passage for guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا أَوْ فَتَدْخُلُ بَيْنَ اِسْمَيْنِ أَوْ فِعْلَيْنِ فَيَتَنَاوَلُ اَحَدَ الْمَذْكُورَيْنِ فَإِنْ دَخَلَتْ فِي الْخَبَرِ أَفْضَتْ إِلَى الشَّكَ وَإِنْ دَخَلَتْ فِي الْاِبْتِدَاءِ وَالْأَنْشَاءِ أَوْجَبَتِ التَّخْبِيْرَ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا فِيْمَنْ قَالَ هَذَا حَرِّ أَوْ هَذَا أَنَّهُ لَمَا كَانَ إِنْشَاءُ يَحْتَمِلُ الْخَبَرَ أَوْجَبَ التَّخْيِيرَ عَلَى احْتِمَالٍ أَنَّهُ بَيَانْ حَتَّى جُعِلَ الْبَيَانُ إِنْشَاءُ مِنْ وَجْهِ إِظْهَارًا مِنْ وَجْهِ وَقَدْ تُسْتَعَارُ هَذِهِ الْكَلِمَةُ لِلْعُمُوم فَتُوجِبْ عُمُومَ الْإِفْرَادِ فِي مَوْضِعَ النَّفِئ وَعُمُومَ الْإِجْتِمَاعِ فِي مَوْضِعِ الْإِبَاحَةِ وَلِهَذَا لَوْحَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمَ فَلَانًا أَوْفُلَانًا يَحْنَثُ إِذَا كَلَّمَ أَحَدَهُمَا وَلَوْ قَالَ لَا يُكَلَّمَ أَحَدًا إلا فلانا أوْ فَلَانًا كَانَ لَهُ أَنْ يُكَلِّمَهُمَا جَمِيْعًا وَقَدْ تُجْعَلُ بِمَعْنَى حَتَّى فِى نَحْوَقَوْلِهِ وَالله لَا اَدْخُلُ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ اَوْ اَدْخُلَ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ حَتَّى لَوْدَخَلَ الْآخِيْرَةَ قَبْلَ الْأوْلى إِنْتَهَتِ الْيَمِيْنُ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَذَّرَ لِأَنَّهُ الْعَطْفُ لِاخْتِلَافِ الْكَلَامَيْنِ مِنْ نَفْي وَاثْبَاتِ وَالْغَايَةُ صَالِحَةٌ لِاَنَّ اَوَلَ الْكَلَامِ حَظُرُ وَ تَحْرِيمْ وَلِذَلِكَ وَجَبَ الْعَمَلُ بِمَجَازَه
As for 'aw', it enters between two nouns or two verbs and includes one of the two mentioned. If it enters into a statement (khabar), it leads to doubt; if it enters into commencement (ibtida) and construction (insha), it necessitates choice (takhyir). Therefore we said about someone who said 'This is free or this' that since it is construction (insha) that may also carry the sense of a statement, it obligates choice with the possibility that it is a clarification (bayan), such that the clarification is considered from one aspect as construction and from another aspect as declaration. Sometimes this word is borrowed for generality (umum). It necessitates generality of individual in the context of negation and generality of collective in the context of permission. For this reason, if someone swears 'I will not speak to so-and-so or so-and-so', he breaks his oath if he speaks to either of them. And if he says 'I will not speak to anyone except so-and-so or so-and-so', he is allowed to speak to both of them. Sometimes it is used in the sense of 'hatta' (until), as in the saying of one who says 'By Allah, I will not enter this house or I enter that house' – such that if he enters the second before the first, the oath is fulfilled, because conjunction is impossible due to the two statements differing in negation and affirmation, and [the particle] is suitable for purpose [ghayat], because the beginning of the speech is prohibition and interdiction; therefore one must act upon its metaphorical meaning.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the Arabic particle 'aw' (or) and its various legal-linguistic functions. The author explains that 'aw' typically connects two nouns or two verbs and indicates one of them. Its effect depends on the type of speech it enters: in a khabar (informative statement), 'aw' creates doubt (شک) about which alternative is true; in insha' (performative/construction) or requests, it creates a choice (تخییر) between options. The example given is the phrase 'this is free or this' in the context of manumission – since it is an insha' (declaration of freeing) but can also be interpreted as a khabar (informing), it is interpreted as giving the owner a choice. Further, 'aw' can be borrowed (مستعار) to express generality (عموم): in the context of negation, it requires the negation to apply to each individual separately (عموم الافراد), meaning the oath is broken by doing any one of the prohibited acts; in the context of permission, it allows the collective doing of all options (عموم الاجتماع), meaning if someone swears he will not speak to anyone except X or Y, he is allowed to speak to both. Finally, 'aw' sometimes carries the meaning of 'hatta' (until) in oaths where the second clause is an affirmation contradicting the first negation; in such cases, the oath is considered to have a limit, and entering the second house first terminates the oath because the original prohibition is fulfilled. This analysis is critical for understanding the implications of utterances in legal contexts, especially in oaths and contracts. The Hanafi approach carefully distinguishes the semantic effect of particles to determine legal consequences.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle meaning 'or' that can indicate doubt in statements, choice in constructions, generality in negation/permission, or sometimes 'until' in oaths.
تخيير (takhyir): Giving a choice between alternatives, typically in performative speech like freeing a slave.
عموم الافراد (umum al-afrad): Generality of individuals: the ruling applies to each individual separately.
عموم الاجتماع (umum al-ijtima'): Generality of collective: the ruling applies to the group collectively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone swears 'I will not speak to Zaid or Amr', and he speaks to Zaid only, what is the ruling?
A) He does not break his oath until he speaks to both.
B) He breaks his oath because 'aw' in negation gives generality of individuals.
C) He breaks his oath only if he speaks to both together.
D) The oath is invalid because 'aw' creates doubt.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'aw' has four distinct functions in Hanafi usul—doubt, choice, individual/collective generality, and 'until'—and its interpretation depends entirely on the type of speech and context.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Particle 'أو' in Hanafi Usul: From Doubt to Generality
Explains the different uses of the particle 'أو' in legal language.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four functions of the particle 'أو' (aw) in Arabic legal texts (doubt in khabar, choice in insha, generality in negation/permission, and 'until' in oaths) and apply the Hanafi usul principles to derive rulings from texts containing 'أو'.

Core Idea
أو is not just 'or'; its meaning shifts with context: khabar (doubt), insha (choice), metaphorically generality, and as 'hatta'.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the particle 'أو' (aw) is a chameleon — its legal meaning depends entirely on whether it appears in a declarative sentence (khabar) or a constructive sentence (insha), and even then it can take on metaphorical roles like generality or 'until'. This lesson walks through the classical analysis from Al-Husami commentary, showing how these distinctions produce concrete rulings in oaths, emancipations, and Qur'anic interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish khabar from insha
Identify whether the sentence where 'أو' appears is a report (khabar, which can be true/false) or a construction (insha, which creates a legal effect like a command or declaration).
This is the foundational classification; all subsequent analysis depends on it.
2
Analyze 'أو' in khabar
In khabar, 'أو' creates doubt (shakk) about which of the two mentioned items is true. Example: 'Jaa'ani Zaidun aw 'Amrun' (Zaid came or 'Amr). The speaker is uncertain.
The doubt arises from the nature of khabar, not from 'أو' itself.
3
Analyze 'أو' in insha
In insha, 'أو' indicates choice (takhyir) for the speaker, not doubt. Example: 'Hadha hurrun aw hadha' (This is free or this). The master has the right to choose which slave he meant to free.
Because insha creates a new reality, the particle cannot introduce genuine doubt.
4
Identify metaphorical uses
Recognize when 'أو' is used for generality (umum) — in negation it requires each individual separately; in permission it allows both together. Also note when it means 'until' (hatta) in oaths where two statements conflict (negation then affirmation).
These uses are established by context and are not the literal meaning of disjunction.

قَبْلَ الْأوْلى إِنْتَهَتِ الْيَمِيْنُ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَذَّرَ لِأَنَّهُ الْعَطْفُ لِاخْتِلَافِ الْكَلَامَيْنِ مِنْ نَفْي وَاثْبَاتِ وَالْغَايَةُ صَالِحَةٌ لِاَنَّ اَوَلَ الْكَلَامِ حَظُرُ وَ تَحْرِيمْ وَلِذَلِكَ وَجَبَ الْعَمَلُ بِمَجَازَه - ترجمہ: اور بہر حال او تو وہ دو اسموں یا دو فعلوں کے درمیان داخل ہوتا ہے، پس مذکورین میں سے ایک کو شامل ہوگا، پس اگر وہ خبر پر داخل ہو تو مفضی الی الشک ہوگا، اور اگر ابتداء اور انشاء میں داخل ہو تو تخییر کو واجب کرے گا، اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا اس شخص کے بارے میں جس نے کہا " هذا حر او هذا " کہ یہ قول انشاء ہے، جو خبر کا احتمال رکھتا ہے، تو اوتخییر کو واجب کرے گا اس احتمال کے ساتھ کہ یہ قول بیان ہے، حتی کہ بیان کو من وجہ انشاء اور من وجہ اظہار قرار دیا جائے گا، اور بھی کلمہ او عموم کے لئے مستعار لیا جاتا ہے، تو یہ موضع نفی میں عموم افراد کو اور موضع اباحت میں عموم اجتماع کو واجب کرے گا، اسی وجہ سے اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ فلاں سے بات نہیں کرے گا یا فلاں سے تو جب ان دونوں میں سے ایک سے کلام کرے گا تو حانث ہو جائے گا، اور اگر کہا کہ وہ کسی سے کلام نہیں کرے گا مگر فلاں یا فلاں سے تو اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ وہ دونوں سے کلام کرے، اور کبھی کلمہ اوحتی کے معنی کے لئے قرار دیا جاتا ہے، جیسے قائل کے قول میں "وا الله لا ادخل هذه الدار او ادخل هذه الدار یہاں تک کہ اگر وہ دوسرے گھر میں پہلے گھر سے پہلے داخل ہو گیا، تو یمین پوری ہو جائے گی، اس لئے کہ عطف متعذ رہے، دو کلاموں کے اثبات و نفی میں مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے ، اور غایت کی صلاحیت ہے، اس لئے کہ اول کلام ممانعت اور تحریم ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے اس کے مجازی معنی پر عمل کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ تشریح:- حروف عطف میں سے چھٹا حرف او ہے، جو د وفعلوں یا دواسموں کے درمیان داخل ہوتا ہے، اور دونوں میں سے ایک کو شامل ہوتا ہے، اگر کلمہ اوخبر میں داخل ہو تو شک کو پیدا کرتا ہے، مگر یہ شک او سے نہیں بلکہ محل کلام سے پیدا ہوتا ہے، کیونکہ اوشک کے لئے وضع نہیں کیا گیا ہے، جیسے " جاء نی زید او عمر "، متکلم کا مقصد دونوں میں سے بغیر تعیین کے کسی ایک کے آنے کی خبر دینا ہے۔ اور اگر ابتدا میں داخل ہو ، یعنی ایسے کلام میں داخل ہو جو خبر نہ ہو، بلکہ اس میں حکم ابتداء ثابت کرنا مقصود ہو جیسے اضرب هذا او هذا ، يا انشاء میں داخل ہو جیسے "هذا حر او هذا " تو ان دونوں میں اؤ شک کے لئے نہ ہوگا ، بلکہ تخییر کے لیے ہو گا، بہر حال اور دو چیزوں میں سے ایک غیر متعین کے لیے آتا ہے، اور اس میں شک اور تخییر دونوں محل کلام سے پیدا ہوتے ہیں، اس لئے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اگر آقا نے کہا "هذا حر او هذا ، تو يه كلام شرعاً انشاء ہوگا، کیونکہ یہ کلام ایجاد حریت کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہے لیکن چونکہ لغہ یہ کلام خبر کے لئے موضوع ہے، اس لئے خبر کا بھی احتمال ہوگا، الغرض انشاء اور خبر دونوں پہلو جمع ہو گئے ، تو انشاء ہونے کی وجہ سے تو تخییر ثابت ہوگی یعنی مولی کو دونوں میں سے جس کو چاہے آزادی میں متعین کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا ۔ لیکن اس کلام کے خبر ہونے کے پہلو سے یہ احتمال بھی رہے گا کہ مولی پہلے غلام آزاد کر چکا ہے ، اور اس کلام کے ذریعہ اس پہلے والی حریت کی خبر دے رہا ہے اسی لئے اس کے قول کو من وجہ انشاء اور من وجہ اخیار قرار دیا جائے گا، یعنی جس طرح مبین یعنی "هذا حرا و هذا " میں انشاء اور خبر دونوں احتمال ہیں، اسی طرح بیان یعنی مولی کا یہ کہنا کہ میری مراد یہ غلام تھا انشاء اور خبر دونوں احتمال رکھے گا، پس انشاء ہونے کے اعتبار سے دفع تہمت کے لئے محل کا صالح ہونا ضروری ہے، چنانچہ اگر تعین سے پہلے ایک غلام مر گیا اور مولی نے کہا کہ میری مراد یہی غلام تھا، تو مولی کا قول قبول نہ ہوگا، اس لئے کہ اس میں تہمت ہے، مولی کا فائدہ ہے، اور خبر کے احتمال کی وجہ سے مولی کا قول سابق کا بیان ہوگا ، حتی کہ مولی کو قاضی کی جانب سے ایک غلام متعین کرنے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ وقد تستعار هذه الكلمة - مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ کبھی مجاز او عموم کے لئے بھی آتا ہے، تو اس وقت واؤ کے معنی میں ہوگا یعنی او بھی واؤ کی طرح معطوف علیہ اور معطوف کے لئے منفی حکم کو ثابت کرنے پر دلالت کرے گا لیکن دونوں میں یہ فرق رہے گا کہ واؤ اجتماع اور شمول پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور اؤ معطوف اور معطوف علیہ دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے دوسرے سے الگ ہونے پر دلالت کرے گا جیسے اللہ کا ارشاد "لا تطع منهم آثما او كفورا"
And as for 'aw', it enters between two nouns or two verbs, so it covers one of the two mentioned. If it enters into a report (khabar), it leads to doubt; if it enters into a beginning (ibtida) or construction (insha), it necessitates choice (takhyir). For this reason we said concerning one who said 'This is free or this' that since it is a construction that can bear the meaning of a report, it necessitates choice on the probability that it is a clarification, such that the clarification is considered a construction in one way and an expression in another. And sometimes this word is borrowed for generality, so it necessitates generality of individuals in the context of negation and generality of combination in the context of permission. For this reason, if one swears 'I will not speak to so-and-so or so-and-so', he breaks his oath when he speaks to one of them. And if he says 'I will not speak to anyone except so-and-so or so-and-so', he is allowed to speak to both of them. And sometimes it is given the meaning of 'until' in expressions like his saying 'By Allah, I will not enter this house or enter this house' such that if he enters the latter before the former, the oath is fulfilled because the conjunction is impossible due to the two statements being different in negation and affirmation, and the limit (ghaya) is suitable because the beginning of the statement is prohibition and prohibition, and therefore it is necessary to act upon its metaphorical meaning.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the particle 'أو' (aw) in Arabic, specifically within the field of usul al-fiqh. The author first states that 'أو' operates between two nouns or two verbs, and it refers to one of the two (disjunction). If it appears in a declarative sentence (khabar), it creates doubt (shakk) as to which one is meant. For example, 'Zaid came or Umar' leaves doubt. However, if it appears in non-declarative contexts (ibtida or insha), such as commands or declarations of emancipation, 'أو' indicates choice (takhyir), not doubt. For instance, if a master says 'This slave is free or this one,' the statement is considered an insha (creative speech) that grants the master the choice to decide which slave he intended. But because the wording also bears the possibility of being a report (if he had already freed one), the master's later clarification is accepted but under conditions: if one slave dies before the master clarifies, the master's claim that he meant that one is rejected due to suspicion. The passage then explains that 'أو' can be used metaphorically for generality (umum): in negative contexts it requires each individual separately (e.g., an oath not to speak to X or Y means both are included in the prohibition); in permissive contexts it allows both together. The example of an oath shows that if one swears 'I will not speak to X or Y,' he is guilty if he speaks to either one. But if he says 'I will not speak to anyone except X or Y,' he may speak to both. Additionally, 'أو' can mean 'until' (hatta) in certain constructions, like an oath to not enter a house until entering another, where if he enters the second first, the oath is considered broken because the limit was set. The commentary emphasizes that the particle's function depends on the context and the type of speech.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle of disjunction that operates between two nouns or two verbs, indicating one of them. Its meaning varies based on context: doubt (shakk) in khabar, choice (takhyir) in insha, generality (umum) metaphorically, or as a limit (hatta).
الخبر (al-khabar): A declarative sentence that can be true or false. When 'أو' enters it, it creates doubt about which of the two possibilities is true.
الإنشاء (al-insha): A constructive sentence that brings about a legal effect, like a declaration of emancipation or a command. When 'أو' enters it, it gives the speaker choice (takhyir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says to his two slaves, 'هذا حر أو هذا' (This one is free or this one), and one slave dies before the master specifies which one he meant, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The master's claim that he meant the deceased slave is accepted.
B) The master's claim is rejected due to suspicion, and he must specify a slave or be compelled by the judge.
C) Both slaves become free.
D) Neither slave is free until the master specifies.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'أو' is context-dependent: it indicates doubt in reports, choice in constructions, generality in negation/permission, and 'until' in sequential oaths.
